[USER]
Read the following journal entry for my D&D character, Cara. Create a list of important items, locations, names, objectives and events. Each list should be a separate category. Include a summary of the of the journal entry:   32nd of Melimbrim, 2324 IC. Saernhall

Wake and it’s strange to wake to an empty bed. For a moment, I expect to see him and hear him breathing. I pray and then dress in something easy to put on before walking out into the courtyard to commune with Mother. My day guards are here and walk with me. I pad silently out in bare feet. A clear sky shows the sun rising over the edge, a strip of liquid gold and the courtyard is half bathed in soft light. I walk to a place that feels right. I stop, take a deep breath and reach for Mother. She’s easy to find. I stand there with Her, feeling Her breathe. I do that until I am done, and I find an immense sense of calm and purpose. 
I turn around and walk back inside. Warros stays very close to me. I go in search of food, walking through the house to the dining hall. Drinks are laid out at the head of the table and when I walk in, Ohna-yen salutes and disappears into the kitchen. I feel a tiny bit silly being just me in the dining hall, but I sit down. Ohna-yin sets down a feast in front of me. I pick a little bit of this and that to eat knowing I won’t go hungry. It is quite but not uncomfortable. 
Do you wish to hear, Kierna, of what is happening in Ilyrian. I have had word from Lenestra. Olvar
Yes, please, Olvar.
What we had considered a possibility is apparently a truth. The dark fey and a wave of undead struck Ilyrian’s northern edge just before dusk. Among them was a creature that Lenestra described as the largest behemoth anyone had ever seen. A creature made of blood and bone. A creature as tall as a grandfather oak (60 feet tall). It is believed that they gained access to the wood through the feywild. How they went from the Deepening to Ilyrian is as of yet, unknown. Along with this great creature were waves of undead and dark fey, nightmare creatures. The wave was fought. Lenestra did not give a great deal of detail, only to say the fighting was through the night and into the early morning hours and that there was a lull. She said the battles were costly but did not say further. She was very weary, and time was short. 
We don’t know if the undead came from beneath our ruins, do we?
It is believed they did not. Why, I cannot say. Lenestra merely said they are not ‘of here’ and she said there was blood magic. I am sure she would have said more but she was called away. 
Thank you, Olvar. 
I am afraid she said nothing more. 
I nod and finish eating. I go in search of Ethnall who knows the plans of what is supposed to happen today. Mother said my path was elsewhere, not Ilyrian. It does me no good to worry about Ilyrian so I may as well do something. Ethnalla has a proposal for today sent by the Elders of the Saer.
Speaker Calmadon has asked me to join him this morning so that he may tour me through the city. The Mor’bahl (Mother’s son) would like me to join him for a walk (the Arch Druid Orhahnthun), after my meeting with Calmadon. A messenger came yesterday with an unaddressed invitation, brought by a boy from the market. The message is believed to be for me: do not forget to visit my friend as we discussed (the Maker on the edge of the city). I ask Ethnalla to extend an invitation to the Mor’Saer and the Mors for tea in the later part of the evening. I would like to attend the commune this evening. Tomorrow, the Keepers ask that I make no plans as the Ma’ja’deen summons me that day. Ethnalla sends runners to send the messages.
I walk back to my room and pick a dress to wear that is appropriate for a meeting with Keeper Calmondon. Olvar fixes my hair in Saer fashion. I switch jewelry and walk out with slippers in my hand. I walk into one of the libraries where I left my book and wait for Keeper Calmadon. There are highly detailed accounts including the emotions that played on my face. I read for about 25 minutes before a hear the front bell ring. I set the book down and go to answer the door. 
Keeper Calmadon is with a woman I have not yet met. 
Good morning Keeper Calmadon.
Good morning, Mor’dahn. I hope you had a restful night.
A dream, but a restful night despite it. Thank you.
Dreams are the mind and spirit collaborating on the past and the future. Occasionally we get glimpses into their work. May I introduce Jahn’i. 
Good morning Jahn’i. I am happy to meet you.
Good morning, Mor’dahn. I am happy to meet you as well. Welcome to the land of the Saer. I hope you have been content and pleased in your journey and what you have found in our people. 
I have been quite content and please in my journey and I have enjoyed what I have found in my people.
She tilts her head slightly. Jahn’I is one of his daughters. Keeper Calmadon says we will speak as old friends. I agree if they do. 
I step out after Weros goes first and confirms that we will not leave the city. Weros, Reimarn, Arthen, and Quern are awake today. Weros, not liking that we will be among the crowd. I pull my slippers on and we walk out together. Keeper Calmadon takes us to a small cottage and unlock the door. He steps inside and does something that causes the whole central floor to unlock and then swing up. 
Come, let me show you the warren.
I smile and follow him and his daughter, Jahn’i. Quern is not in armor and asks me to stay close to him. We step into an underground room and into a passage way that forces us to walk single file. There are glyphs around the entrance – Ethragen glyphs. 
Each entrance into the Warren is guarded by Mother’s essence. Woe be those who would attempt to come through this portal, not of Her blood and bone. Keeper Calmadon
The stone in the Warren is very similar to the stone in the House of Tranquil Waters but lighter, more like Beruth. There is a bit of the dark slate of the Spine. Crystal globes or crystal diamonds at the ceiling light the tunnels which descend down in spirals. There are 6 branches that come off the main. Some of the branching tunnels dead end into stone, others into empty rooms. The main tunnel twists and turns, deliberately going up and down to confuse any who might invade. We step out into an illuminated chamber which leads into a massive cavern. 
It reminds me of Underhome but alive. The similarity is striking. I keep that thought to myself.
The chambers are lit by two colors of light: a blue from the crystals in the city which mimic blue sunlight and a bright cheery orange firelight. It reminds me of my own aura. 
Welcome to the Square of Thought Given Wind. Keeper Calmadon
The Warren beneath Saerenhall could hold all the Saer. And there are multiple warrens beneath the Saervaghn lands, but they are not all connected. The House of Eastern Wisdoms connects to the House of Tranquil Waters. The Tower of Whispered Truths is where great wisdoms from far aways places were shared. I could live here. It would be more comfortable. 
Coming down the road is a small little man, a Jhobrani. They live in the valley before the Castle of 9 Tears in the feywild.  He’s not native but he does have an aura, it’s chaotic, a riot of colors and his skin is the color of the darker stone from the Spine. His hair is purple, a brilliant violet. He has gem colored light amethyst eyes. He’s about 2 ½ feet tall. There are 112 or so that live some distance away but come for market. 
We tour the inside of the House of Eastern Wisdoms so the Kiern’s Guard can check it out. We walk up the steps. The front door is round, splits in half and disappears into the wall. Just inside are two black headed men, Saer wardens. 
Jahn’i’s mate died to a Sorrowfiend, a nightmare fey. They feed on sorrow and misery, and are drawn to it. Jahn’I works for the Ma’ja’deen as a NaeSayer. There are also Truthfinders or Truthsayer. A NaeSayer listens to what she says and looks for flaws in her thinking. The House of the Wild Rose is where the Ma’ja’deen lives. Eventually the Kiern’s Guard come back and we go in. The first room in small but shaped almost like a plus-sign with rounded corners. This is the Hall of Honored Guests (and entry and reception hall). The ceiling is high overhead and there are places to sit. The acoustics here are fabulous. The center of this room is the domain of the host or hostess. Tables and seating could be brought in for dinners and celebrations. There is a device that gets the guests attention and it’s odd. It makes a noise when struck and hums. 
Jahn’I apologizes for her sharp tone. I think her tone is very mild. In Khovar, there are 9 rings of speaking. The 1st tier of speaking is the voice reserved for Mother and the one within yourself. The 2nd ring is for mothers or mates where fears and doubts and weakness can be shown as well as tenderness. The 3rd ring is for kin, brothers and sisters, mothers and fathers and only in the privacy of one’s shared home. The 4th ring is with kin but in another’s home where one is a guest even though kin. 
Beyond is a tunnel-like hallway and it is masterfully sculpted but empty of carvings or anything on the walls and floors. It is a purposely transitional space to prepare you for the next room. There is an echo, so if you didn’t hear someone before, you definitely hear them in the hall. Room of Worship is the right and behind a stone door. The Room of Worship is a round room and dimly lit. It steps down twice and in the center is a pool of water. On the far side of the room are two statues facing inward toward each other and the pool in the center: Weal and Woe. Weal is in white basalt and Woe is in onyx. I step down and turn to face Weal, then turn to face Woe, then kneel down and commune with Mother at the pool. I feel Her. As I open my eyes, I see the blue glow fade from the pool. 
We go next to the Hall of Forefathers. It is a long hall with large, round tasseled and multi-colored thick pillows for sitting or laying on. On the walls on either side are paintings and between the paintings are pillars with lights. There 6 paintings on each side, 12 Varkier. The first is Thurgen (not in his headdress, sitting on the Dragon throne. His crown is on a table next to him and there are shadows of people in the throne room. Beside him I see at least two of his Kiern’s Guard, one is in Gorhund armor. Thurgen has one hand on his chin starting at whoever stands in front of him while his right hand is on the armrest and one claw is out. The painting is highly detailed. It doesn’t look like the same room as in Kiern’Kirak. There is a stone wall but there are windows. He won’t tell me who painted it but it was painted 83 or 84 years ago and the detail is incredible. 
The second is Demanius Varkier, Thurgen’s father. He is large and heavy-boned. The headdress is carried in his right hand. His build is powerful and muscular and his arms are huge. In his left hand he carries a very strange, ornate axe (silvery-grey). It is bearded on one side with a long blade and small axe blades line the shaft except for one space where his hand rests. He’s half turned looking back at me. His faces has a question. There is sweat and grime and he has heavily curly black hair and sharply trimmed beard which squares off. I can see the marks of the headdress around his forehead. Behind him to one side are the trees and to the other, the grasslands. He has a broad, wide nose and he looks very feline. I walk up close and he feels huge. In life he was 8 knot, a little over 6 feet tall. In nature’s form, he is 14 knots, about 9 or 10 feet. Demanius was blessed with a titan form and they were giant cats with protruding bone spikes. It is rare among the Hularens, even the Varkier. But it is similar to what our Grandfather Bogrim did. Bogrim’s form is unknown to them. Demanius was painted last year.
3rd is Kelgarn Varkier. He is tawny blonde, and he sits on a rock. Behind him is a drop and in the distance, a cliff mountain. On the rocks around him are other bare chested me wearing paint. He’s grinning and staring ahead, he looks amused. He is powerfully built too and around Bronnen’s size. He’s built for speed. Kelgarn and Demanius were cousins. His skin also glistens. He doesn’t look like Demanius or Thurgen. His hair is slightly curly and does almost look like a mane. His arm is wrapped around one knee. He wears bone jewellry in his ears, nose, lip, eyebrows. Most of the men do and I can see the Toltemic-like symbols in the bone. Kelgarn was painted 700 years ago. The location may no longer exists, the stone is greyer than the Spine. 
I look more like Thurgen and Demanius. 
Reimarn stares at a different painting. I walk over and look. A tall, powerfully built blonde man in armor, covered in blood and bits. He holds a dark-skinned man with a forked beard and red eyes off the ground. He is angry. He has the man by the esophagus, not the throat, holding him in the air. His armor is gorgeous, a shiny silver in places and blue enamel in others and built to expand. In the edge of the painting, I see the tip of a long staff and heavily carved. Fierghon Varkier. He’s huge. The man’s feet dangle 2 feet off the ground. In his least form, he stood near 9 knots, almost 7 feet. He has blonde hair with beads woven on the side, and huge mane of a tail beaded all down the back. His hair is whipping around. The innovar is painted innovar, dark-skinned but washed out with grey and slightly blurry. Fierghon stands on a ledge and behind him, a war rages. This is the war with the Jhadahni invaders, fire demons and men from another plain. 
Another painting is a woman. Ohrain Varkier. She is pointing and in mid-conversation. She is looking up because she is small. There is a stone throne behind me. She has auburn hair. She is married to a Varmarkuhn. She is wearing bones. She was fierce and cunning. She faced trials because the Varkier that came before her were great men and warriors of immense size whereas she was known for her speed and accuracy in battle. She led our people when we first defeated the Sumar. This painting was carried from the old lands when the Saer left their hiding spot to come here to Woodhome. (Quote on the 21st of Melimbrim)
All the paintings seem to be talking to the viewer. One is of a very old man. Still powerfully built, wearing fur pants and bare chested. He has a long curled beard. His hair is swept back and tied with a leather thong. His hair is white and grey. Rhul Varkier, the 3rd son of Var (3 sons away from Var, his great grandson. Nothing is known of him except his lineage and that he was Varkier. He sits in a chair made of wood and skulls: innovar, troll, ogre. Furs lay over the lashed sticks of the chair. It is night. To his right is a large standing stone and nearby is a large fire casting a glow on him, the stone and the night. He stares at me like I am a mystery to him or there’s a question in his mind. 
Each painting captures a moment in motion. This is an old style, like the one I saw in Lanneroc. The artform, I was told, was lost. All who stand in front of the paintings feel like the Varkier are looking and speaking to them. I could sketch Var (30s, hairy, squatted down in front of a fire, carving a piece of wood, heavy brow, powerfully built). I wonder if I sketched Var, if they would look like kin. 
We continue on with the tour. The Chamber of the Blazing Sun is next. We pass rooms on the way, several lush sittings rooms with sunken floors and furs, rooms filled with books, and more. We go up a level. The Chamber of the Blazing Sun blazes with a yellow-orange light. It’s fairly small and shaped like a tulip bulb with seating on both sides for 4 people. In the middle hangs a globe containing fire and the lenses are crystal. I can feel the heat radiating from it and it’s warm in here. The seats are cushioned and warm. This room is used to relax, de-stress, and be reminded of the warmth of summer during winter. If you could melt into a pillow, this would be the place to do it. It feels like sitting under a warm summer sun. 
Calmadahn shows me a library that is 3 stories tall. It is a cylinder room with a domed roof. We go up another level to the bed chamber. The room is large but there are no corners anywhere. There is a bed, dressing table, and wardrobes. The room is almost shaped like an acorn and covered in ornate drawings and paintings. The sitting area is very comfortable. The windows are clear glass. A glass alcove holds a glass door and leads out to a small balcony, 3 or 4 stories up. I can see far out into the Underwarren. There are chairs and a small table out here and the light of the crystals shines down on me. For people of shadow and mist, there is a great deal of light. 
He also shows me the Tower of Whispered Truths. There is Hularen writing along the tunnel that leads to the tower. It is a quote and I can read it. It talks about the importance and understanding that some truths should never gain voice, some truths should be shouted across the hills, some truths should be taught, and others only whispered. The most dangerous truth is one that is whispered. It is an excerpt from the Annals of Truths in the Khovar.  A stone bench rings the room. There are alcoves at intervals for study. In the center is a rhodahn made of ornate glyphs, very complex and huge, made in blue stone, not gemstone, with a mix of blue and black stone – not the magic eating stone. 
The alcoves remind me of the ruin in the North where the Kothians were trying to dig up the shard of the Mother and also in the East where the shard fell out of it’s box. This is a much larger version but very familiar. The door in the East rolled out of the way. In the center of the Rhodahn is a single pillar. The room is an old design. This room has power, what is spoken here is not heard. Mother’s essence drawn to this room cannot be felt. It is more than a testament to the old world but of the old world. There are 3 places in the Saer lands where you can speak and not be overheard. The Ma’ja’deen wanted me to have this place though others did not. 
The Tower of Whispered Truths is where one can whisper truths that must not be heard. I will hear whispered truths in this room tomorrow. The glyph on the floor is very complex but not like the one Renna and I made. It was made long before. I walk over to an alcove and slip in to sit down. It’s carved like the others were, in Ancient Hularen. I describe both of those ruins to Keeper Calmidahn. 
Room of the Sung Note, crafting rooms, kitchens, and so on. An armory and a great meeting hall, dining hall, studies. He warns me there are some things that may react to my touch – so I won’t touch, especially artifacts. 
We leave the underwarren and walk back to the House of Tranquil Waters. Keeper Kalmidahn and his daughter Jahn’I return to the House of Bonding Voices. I am supposed to walk with Arch Druid Orhahnthun next. Then a walk to the Durhon Maker at the edge of the village. In the late afternoon / early evening, a possible tea with the Mors. A light mist hangs in the air. I go inside and wait for the Arch Druid to arrive. I go back into the library I last saw Bronnen in as it has the letters I wrote to Faynor and the book of me. I read another few minutes in the book of me. I make a list of odd symbol notations to ask what they are. The front bell rings and Quern goes to answer it. I mark my place in the book of me. 
Quern comes back with Arch Druid Orhahnthun. We greet each other and give one another Mother’s blessing. We leave the House of Tranquil Waters to walk around the city. We will travel to the Trumpeted Vale where we might see some Kopalath, fey folk of flower and grass. Twilloth may also be there. Joath, Purejhanni and other fey live within the lands of the Saer. The Joath & Purejhanni require much diplomacy. There are also satyr and woodwomen, dryads. Occasionally lesche and sometimes at night in the fall, a twajhan (the twinkling twilight folk which appear as dancing lights. 
Originally, there was a small Baern settlement to the West of here. It was already abandoned by the time the Saer arrived. The Baeorn had all migrated into the lands where they are now. The Baeorn see themselves ‘completely not separate’ from the trees, fey, water, wind, stone. Many of the clans holds an unthinking thought that while they are part of Mother, they are somehow distanced from the stone, the wood, the water; from Mother’s flesh but in their making, different. The Baeorn hold no such thought. The Saer way of thinking is far more complex: of the earth and part of the earth but not wholly the earth as the spirit is crafted by each individual. 
The Otarn are not bound to the otter but to the Ohmahlia family: small, fast, furred creatures; ferret, weasel, beaver, mink. Where a few Otarn go, all go. It is believed the Khanyen and the Otarn were close kin. The Volkarn are children of Yhadahn, the Great Elk. They were once tied to the land like the Baeorn. When the innovar slaughtered them, it changed them and rage seeped into their bones. 
We walk along a trail. We look down on a valley filled with tall-peaked houses and a rhodahn is in the center. The style of the buildings are specific to a Saer bloodline and it is called the Circle of Word and Song. The spire architecture pays respect to the nature of Mother. This is the closest communal if I want to join one in the evening. The great building to the left is the House of Captured Thought. The building to the right is the Hall of Singing Voice. There is only one room in the House of Singing Voice and a whisper spoken in the center can be heard across the room, it is a place for song and music. The Song of Saer is sung in the spring. He could tell me which Saer bloodline but thinks it better I learn for myself. 
We travel across the ridge line. I see nemoi floating in the wind. They have blue and green nemoi that are wild and live in the tree canopy. A hawk herds them, no… a tiny fey rides the hawk and that is herding the nemoi. The tiny fey is very spikey and she has brilliant blue eyes. She is one of the Twilloth, a Shamyahni (caretaker, guardian). The Nemoi have predators and the Shamyahni drive them back into the trees if there are predators around. The Twilloth have lived in the woods since the Glimmering. The next place we come to is along a river. A huge hill frames the backdrop of an immense house. A bridge spans a river nearby, a very tall cliff cascades with waterfalls. This is the Hill of the River House. It is believed to be one of the first building the Saer built. Each generation of Keeper adds to the house. This is where Kalmidahn and his family live (Arthen). The histories of the Saer are sung everyday in this house in the Echoing Hall of the Saer. There is a Hall of Sorrows, a Hall of Victories, a Hall of Hidden Truths, a Hall of Held Debts. Each room has a purpose. Etched on the walls in stone or silver are truths. The Hall of Sorrows hold losses, Victories hold celebrations or victories, Held Debts are where the Saer list what is owed (to Mother, to the People). 
I glance at Arthen and his eyes are slightly narrowed. I know better than to ask more. 
The Hall of Held Debts are the names, the incidents where the Saer will go to claim blood debts when the time comes. The Arch Druid speaks of these things and has invited questions. This is a time of learning. Arthen
Blood debts include the Rustani who employ pirates, the Merchant Lords who sent people into the lands to cause havoc, those in the Empire who lead attacks on the people, the assassins of the Diradel and those who employed them. 
What if those people are dead?
Then the debt is cancelled though sometimes it falls to their progeny. Arch Druid
Like the one Elder Dyurgen calls on Lord Karsk’s son?
Dyurgon nods. 
The Blood debt does not always pass on to progeny unless they continue what started the debt. There is an accord among the clans, that all clans not shed blood of the innovar in the East at this time. The Saer have agreed to this for 3 seasons and the subject will be reevaluated then. 
Keeper Kalmidahn lives here. The house is a representation of the people: their victories and sorrows, those upon which vengeance is called for. It reminds the Keepers it is both a home and a reminder of their duties. 
Elder Jurgen was Keeper before Keeper Kalmidahn, does he live here with his family?
For a very long time he did. He now divides his time between the Hall of the Elders and here. A place just up the valley and where we go next.
How many people could live in this house?
Many thousands. 
The Keepers house is much larger than the palace. We walk down the valley to another where the river grows calm and slows. This is the House of the Elders or the House of Saer Wisdom. 
There are many Unspoken Truths here, Kierna, many. Arthen
I know what he means but I am pretty sure I need my blood awakened for those truths. The truths known here are not captured in the House of Captured Thought. So when the Rustani invaded and burned the old building, some of the truths were lost. King Mowak of the Uhdrain Kingdom in Rustin, his name is on the wall in the Hall of Debts. He and all who shared his blood were slaughtered and the debt was fulfilled. King Mowak’s death led to a civil war and then many more after it. This was very long ago and the Rustani threats lessened when they turned on themselves. This is listed in the Hall of Victories and the Hularens who achieved this are revered. 
Keeper of the Hallow > Keeper of the City > Keeper of the Saer & Arch Druid > Elder & Wisdom. No one sits on a problem for more than 5 days before escalating the problem to someone higher up. 
Arch Druid Orhahnthun shows me where the Saer are bonded to Mother and bonded to one another. Around a hill to a large cave with a rounded entrance. Payo’sahn guards the entrance. 
Greetings on this Whispered Day, may Mother’s eye stay upon you. We wish to journey comfortably to the Valley of 9 Waters. ADO
A girl of 9 or 10 comes out with a tray in her hands.
Greetings Arch Druid Ohrahn.
Mother’s greetings to you Corrilathan.
Would you like some safura. Would you care for, would you like some safura, Arch Druid?
She dips and the tray wobbles.
No, thank you but the Mor’dahn may like some.
Mother’s greetings to you Mor’dahn. Would you like, would you care for some sufura?
Mother’s greetings to you Corrilathan. Yes, I would like some safura. 
I take a glass. She offers a glass to Arthen but he declines. She’s adorable. She quick walks back into the cave and just at the edge of darkness, I see a woman who is watching. I take a sip of the safura which is fermented honey and fruit and spiced. 
Payo’sahn returns with a cart pulled by two small shaggy ponies. They are not as large as a horse, but larger than a typical pony. The horses understand the Saer dialect. Climb into the wagon. The ponies are Vano’to’shay’tegan (old Hularen – High Stepper of the Valley Ridge). Long ago, a Saer elder found a way to awaken the minds of this breed. They are a Saer steed, not ridden by adults, but used to pull carriages. There are maybe 60 in total, and they live about 45 years. They prefer the Saer lands and do not roam outside them. A mated pair were given to the Oren. One tried to return to Saer lands and was killed, the other died not long after (broken heart). 
Child names are chosen after Contemplation with Mother and during the Ritual of Naming with which a druid aids. The seasons and star alignment are also considered. We travel through the cavern complex, up and down winding trails and in the distance, I start to hear running water. A river runs through the cavern and into the Valley of the 9 Waters and considered by many to be the Heart of Saer. It is here that all 9 rivers flow together. It is stunning. There are bridges and houses dotted all over the ledges and outcroppings. Saer live here, too.
I am entranced. 
We step out of the carriage. Many who live here are druid, but not all.
Do you live here?
No. I live in a place called the Valley of Ancient Waters but I am rarely home. People fish these waters. We walk to a Pool of Mother. Water from one of the waterfalls pours directly into the pool. It’s hard to hear in here. A water spirit lives in the water and occasionally the water swirls and then stills but it has been here for as long as the pool has. Either the spirit is ancient or has descendants. The Mah’ja’deen comes here on occasion, and all are welcome to swim in the waters below as long as they do not get too close to the waterfalls. The depth of the Pool of Mother is unknown. The deepest in the swimming portion reaches 240 feet deep. 
I stand there and gawk for several minutes, closing my eyes to let the sound of falling water replace everything, block everything out. It’s loud, but peaceful. I open my eyes and find the Arch Druid studying me. We walk over to the Pool of Mother and pay our respects. He bows his head and communes. I take off my slippers and kneel down and commune with Her. I feel Her presence the minute I kneel. She is quick to respond and aware of my presence. She was waiting for me just like She was in the house. I also catch the strange sense, the strangest feeling that someone is standing on the other side of the water and talking to me, but I can’t hear them. 
When I end my communion with her, I turn and look. Only Arch Driud Ohahnthun is there, watching. I stand up and put my slippers back on. We walk back up the path, back the way we came. 
The Meadows of Golden Fields are to the South and to the West. The Northern Saer lands have high mountain vales and caverns. There is very much to see here. I don’t know what sights are important, but I do know it is important for you to see the Saer lands. Mother sent a fever dream that when the child of the Varkier came, traversing the 5 bloodlines was important. 
5 bloodlines?
5 bloodlines of the Saer. Without more of Mother’s wisdom, we do not know how to translate that request to you. 
There are only 5 bloodlines of the Saer?
Yes, there have only been 5 bloodlines of the Saer since the great war. We do not know how many bloodlines we started with or grew to. It is odd, but we have never found anything that might guide us on it. 
A Saer truth hidden from the Saer?
There are many truths, some remain hidden even from the Saer. The difference is we name those truths when we can and we hunt them. 
We climb back in the cart and the ponies take us back to the entrance. He wants to know why we are trying peace with the innovar. 
Mother has a plan and I am gathering the threads. At the moment, we are trying diplomacy. 
He looks at me quizzically. 
But diplomacy is not Mother’s plan, it is yours, is it not?
Yes, diplomacy is my plan. At the moment, She does not call for war with the Hulean Empire.
There is no Hulean Empire, only innovar.
There is a truth I know but not one that I can voice.
He seems displeased. He wants to know the truth of it, but I cannot speak it. He presses, very politely. 
Even when Bronnen and I were discussing it in the privacy of our room and in the silence of our empty home, Mother was clear that we shouldn’t even discuss it among ourselves. 
It makes me wonder why Mother would keep such a thing secret from Her children and how that ties to keeping the innovar alive and holding the truths of our people. Yet, somehow you believe that to be the case. Arch Druid Orhahnthun
That’s true.
So not only do we not understand, but we also cannot understand. We are not allowed. 
Not yet.
He thinks for a moment.
Never in our history, to our knowledge, has the Mother ever had a plan for innovar other than destroying them but much has changed. I do not believe you offer deceit, Mor’dahn, nor would I even remotely infer that. I believe that you have a deep love for our people. I think you are overjoyed at learning about the culture of our people which makes me proud and happy. I do; however, think you do not understand Mother yet and that is certainly no fault of yours. In fact, how could you possibly. We who have served Her our entire lives have so very much to learn and you have been aware of your bloodline for what, 4 months?
3
Not even a year. Let me offer you a very powerful wisdom, one that is not known broadly, one to keep with you, one that pertains to you: Mother does not plan for innovar or such things. Mother plans the life cycle of living things, the mating cycle of birds, the flow of water. Mother plans Her children but Mother created the Varkier to plan and as unjust as it is, whichever Varkier has their blood awoken, whichever Varkier survives that journey, they are the plan and the planner. It is Mother who gives blessing to it or not. Ever has it been such. All Saer people know this though they don’t realize it. It was the truth that the sons of Gor learned. It is Var and his bloodline who plans and Mother who approves or does not. Our ancient kin lived by who was strongest and smartest. The sons of Gor in their foolishness challenged Var by leaving and proved him to be the strongest and therefor his right to lead. So, if you take the journey to become the Varkier in the eyes of the Saer, the Baeorn, and others, it is your plan, your duty, your calling. It is not Mother’s nature to plan for the innovar. Therefor, if there is a plan, even if you do not intend it, it comes from you for you are the most blessed of Varkier among Her first children and I cannot imagine you would see the innovar who you grew up among as the rest of your people do. Mother needs no words, She can read the truth of you without them. That is what I believe to be true. Your unthinking thoughts, your desires, they become a plan. Mother’s plan is to survive and create. 
Thank you for that wisdom, Arch Druid.
It would be foolish of me not to speak it. You must, I beg of you, keep in mind, I want what is best for you and our people but I fear that those who have already anointed you as Kierna, even if they know this truth, will not speak it for fear of your… distaste of it. 
Thank you for voicing your thoughts into the air, Arch Druid. Not all truths are palatable nor do they go down easy.
What I have spoken is neither good nor bad, just heavy with responsibility. We are taught something else, the wise of Saer, the Mother has slept for a long time, only a part of Her has been awake. How this is and why this is we don’t know. Your smile speaks that you might but that She has slept is very well known. That She comes awake now, in part, and that moment between sleep and wakefulness is a dangerous moment. Dangerous to all of us as we saw not long ago. 
That is not a truth I can voice into the air here. (I am not going to tell him that I will need to awaken her another 3 times)
He nods slowly.
Our next stop will be a significant moment for you and our last stop this day before I return you home. 
May I ask you something Arch Druid? I had the strangest feeling that someone across the water was trying to speak with me but I couldn’t hear them. Did you have that?
Yes, and not just me, and not just today. There is a truth, Mor’dahn, that cannot be spoken or not yet or at least that we, in our mortal forms cannot yet hear. But with it comes great foreboding and great significance. 
Does it always happen there?
For myself and others, it happens at every Pool.
It did not happen at the Pool in the portion of my home in the Underwarren.
You will need to discern if there is a truth she is trying to tell us, or warn us, or one we cannot see but is right here. We are Saer, we have twisted and turned it in every direction. The truth is we have come to one fact, a word we rarely use, there is a puzzle piece missing. Mother wants us to know there is something we need to hear. She expresses it when we commune with Her, tells us to seek it and not allow it to be held from us. If She did not wish us to know it, why would we have this feeling? We show our faith to Her and we feel Her presence, we feel Her love, but we also feel this sense of a truth we cannot hear, cannot understand. Why would She do this other than to cause us to seek it? Mother is nature, Cara, She does not speak directly. The storm teaches us to find shelter, cold to find fire, threat to fight, in this way Mother communicates with us and with all living things. Mother teaches the vole to fear the owl through death. This feeling exists, She teaches us to seek. She is telling us to seek. It is why this desire of yours to leave the innovar alive, to leave our wisdoms in their hands so vexing. It is Mother who tells us to seek and you who tells us to stop. It is very hard to reconcile these things. Can you see the truth in that. 
Yes, Arch Druid, I can see the truth in that.
But you believe they are separate, perhaps, or in this moment you would change your mind, for it is Mother’s will?
I smile.
Arch Druid, none were with me in the Hall of Kings on the 27th of Melimbrim. There is a puzzle piece missing, several. Mother knows the plan. She poured out my thoughts, my memories all that I remember and all that I had forgotten and all that I did not remember I had forgotten that day. She knows all. We did not speak of the plan, then, She said we would speak later. She told me to ‘prepare Her children, they were confused.’ I cannot give you the pieces of the puzzle I am missing. I cannot give you the pieces I have which cannot yet be revealed. Everything must happen in the right order and in the right time and some truths must remain hidden until the time is right. Mother was clear, some truths must remain hidden. We don’t like it, Bronnen and I, but they are necessary to keep Her children safe and to keep Her safe. 
All truths are hidden from those who do not know them. But Mor’dahn, if Mother has combed through your thoughts, as you say, She has drawn truths from your experiences. From your knowledge and wants, from your experiences. If there is a plan and if She sees you as the Varkier to attempt surviving the Awakening, then it is from your mind the plan has come, from your experiences. You must contemplate what experiences have led your life that She might see a plan in. I accept and support that there are unspoken truths that you must hold. It is vexing as it would be were it reversed. There are truths I set here, that it would vex you not to know but I cannot release them. There is an order in which things must occur. We have trusted to the order of things for a very long time though I can say it does rub on occasion. There is more than one purpose to your coming here, in fact, there are many. Some, we are still discovering so I will support, as will the Elders of the Saer, your journey but we fear for you. None living have taken the journey to Awaken their blood. I have expressed the truths that I know and that I can and with them comes risk. To be Varkier is to serve Mother and Mother alone. You are far from prepared for becoming the Varkier. That is not a judgement, you have failed at nothing. It is history that fails us. The Varkier have lost themselves and there are none who yet hold the wisdom of how to teach a Varkier to become the Kiern. There are no Kiern to teach a Varkier to be the Voice of Mother. The gap between what we knew and what we are is vast. For all your accomplishments as brilliant as they have been for they far exceed your years, you are yet, to my old eyes, a child. Not only because of your years but because none can describe the path that you must take to go from where you are to where you must be. Mother is capable of great love but also great brutality. She expects Her children to adapt and to succeed, to survive. We Saer leaders do not know how to help you do that and if any have told you they do, they are being foolish. We have a slender piece of hope, one we are cautious to even call hope: a great name of our people beyond all reason yet survives. He alone could be the answer to your path and if our hopes and request to Mother bear fruit, he will soon be returned here. He alone can give living voice to your journey for he witnessed it himself. Do you know of whom I speak?
Orlim the Watcher. ‘He is the last to know, Cara, and he cannot be the last. Find him.’
Mothers words to you?
Yes.
Let us hope they return for in Orlim is the wisdom how to be the Varkier. Let us hope he has not lost this knowledge and is willing to share it. There must be a reason that he yet survives.
More than one.
As in all things. Perhaps we will know more before the end of the day.
I ask him to deliver my letters to the House of Singing Souls for Faynor. He will. We ride near the edge of the city. People have disappeared, so have houses. 
When did you become Arch Druid, how old were you?
I earned the title of Arch Druid in my 44th year. That was some time ago. 
And you would have studied under a druid?
I did indeed, a number of them over many years.
And that is what I have lost.
Yes. 
Arch Druid Ohahnthun is a son of the Tai’ghan. 
The Saer are considering traveling to Vara’han the city of Varkier, Kiern’Varn, and the city of Gor’jhn because these places are where the Varkier were, their centers of power and places of birth, their training. Somewhere out there it is possible the silver tomes of the Varkier exist. Those tomes are also needed to teach me the rituals of being a Varkier. Vara’han is at the edge of Gorhund lands, in the East. The city was destroyed. It included rituals like calling Mother’s Titan to War, the Oath of Mother, Calling Mother’s Rage.

Read the following journal entry for my D&D character, Cara. Create a list of important items, locations, names, objectives and events. Each list should be a separate category. Include a summary of the of the journal entry:    6th of Quern, 2324 IC. Ilyrian 

Wake, pray, dress, and eat. Ohjan asks to speak with me in his study. He tells me he has been speaking with the Elders, Arch Druid Emric, and Mor’Renna. She salled a meeting of sorts about the Ascension. At Thurgen’s Ascension, 102 bulls were slaughtered and he meditated for 3 days at the base of the Mother tree, after, he was given his armor and scepter. She told the Elders that they were “making it up,” their plans for my Ascension and did not approve. So, 6 days ago, she called together the Elders of all the major clans, all but the Thierkiernon, and most of the Elders came. Mor’Renna told them all how the Ascension should proceed and she explained the rituals that the druids should perform. Specifically, the druids of the Gorhund, Varmarkuhn, Uhlarn, Weivarn, Raelos and a couple others. She said she would teach them the rituals but only to those Arch Druids who would follow the Varkier kiera – me.
“The Elders and druids agreed that the path she offered was the path forward. Emric and Gulrian are speaking with the other Arch Druids to bring them around. Mor’Renna gave me something to hold for you: the Hularen crown of the Kiera.” Ohjan
He opens a wooden box and shows me a crown. It looks like delicately woven slender wooden branches of silver. The crown is not silver fashioned to look like wood, but the actual silvery wood of the Mother Tree from Homewood.
“It can only be worn by a female descendant or relative of the anointed kiera,” Ohjan explains. “That is what Mor’Renna told me. Also, it can only be held by a Varkier.”
I reach for the crown and pick it up expecting it to be heavy, but it is light. There is a blue gem in the front, nestled in the branches. The gem is shiny like a piece of polished hematite but it is a deep blue. 
“The gem is an Askerene – they are the anointed Eyes of the Mother and is referred to as the ‘Eye of the Mother Tree’.” Ohjan
The silvery branches of the crown have the texture of wood but the branches are not supple, they are hard and rigid like silver.
“Does it fit?”
I place the Hularen Crown of the Kiera carefully on my head and it shapes itself, resizing to fit while the thorns of the branches weave into my hair securing it in place. I feel a thrum of power and I am aware of a number of things: 1. Ohjan is Gorhund, not just because of his family name but because of his bloodline. 2. As long as the crown is worn, I have advantage on all rolls against Asha’kari magic. When saving throws are not allowed, I receive one. Where damage is halved, I take none. 3. Those who attempt to read my mind are actually attempting to read Mother’s mind. 
There is more but it is not revealing them yet.
“Mor’Renna said that if you accept her advice and guidance, and grow into the Kiera you can be, she will deliver Thurgen’s crown to the People as well, to be worn by your children as they must also be of Varkier blood to wear Thurgen’s crown. Mor’Renna will take part in your Ascension and crown you just as Thurgen’s father crowned him.” Ohjan
I wonder how Demanius could have crowned Thurgen when he was killed by a dragon when Thurgen was only 16 but I say nothing. I am to meet with Mor’Renna at the Pool of the Mother tomorrow morning. At dinner that night, Ohjan explains that Mama & Papa will be “gifted” a home. They will use it for the Mating (Wedding) rituals but it is their home whether they choose to live in Ilyrian or not.

Wake, pray, dress, and eat. Mama & Papa return. I am in the living room laying out different components for dyes. Khendia and another woman work with me, explaining the different colors and when they are used as well as what they symbolize. I hear Mama’s voice, she is talking to Mor’Sovra in the kitchen. I go and say hello to Mama, happy she has returned. I go and find Papa next. He is outside talking to Bronnen. Papa is wearing a silver and cobalt ring on his right hand, that’s new. Read the following journal entry for my D&D character, Cara. Create a list of important items, locations, names, objectives and events. Each list should be a separate category. Include a summary of the of the journal entry: 39th of Solik, 2324 IC    Wake, pray, and eat. I write my dream into my dream journal and send a copy to Father Sandlin. After breakfast, Ohjan suggests I speak with the Elders outside but first, I help clean up after breakfast. 
After, Bronnen helps me read the speeches of Thurgen Varkier. The accounts are 2nd and 3rd hand and there aren’t many.  Thurgen is very confident and his speeches sound fierce: this is the way it will be and this is why, this is where we must be as a people and how we are going to get there, how we will face this threat or that threat. His speeches set a path the people are expected to follow. He does talk about the terrible gift of responsibility of the people, that the people are responsible for who they are and who they will be: “We are not Sumarac, or Sindi, or Eladri… we are Hularen.”
Later that afternoon, I speak to the Elders. There are 8 Elders in attendance and 16 guards. Elder Ohjan and Dyurnok Voren join me along with Tythis and a number of Gorhund off to the side. Some of the Elders are from smaller clans close to Ilyrian and within a day or tw0-day journey. All are in their 50’s or 60’s. Voren welcomes them all to Ilyrian and offers them a seat. Once seated, Mor’Sovra and her daughters come out with long mugs filled with drink. Another daughter brings salt, bread, meat, and cheese. Ohjan breaks the bread, salts it, then eats a small piece and welcomes the Elders to his home (Sovra’s home). The Elders repeat the gestures, some a little slower than others: a quiet show of resistance, hesitation, and doubt. Ohjan stresses to all present that this is not a moot.
“Thank you, Elders, for making the journey to Ilyrian and for coming to speak with me. I hold your positions as Elders in high regard. I will need you in the days to come. If you have questions, I will entertain them now and I appreciate your eagerness to understand. This is not a moot which will be held in the days following the Ascension.”
I wait for an Elder to speak and answer their questions. They ask about being born in the North and how that has affected me. They ask about bringing the innovar here; they mean the keys. They ask about me speaking to the Hulean Empire and how I was able to get Hularen relics returned to us in exchange for seemingly nothing. They ask if I am an agent of the Hulean Empire, a spy. They ask if I plan to bring more innovar into Thornwall or whether I will push them out of Woodhome. Ohjan and Voren answer questions, too. The Elders ask what I will do with Jurva Thierkiernon, whether I will denounce her and her innovar ways poisoning our people. They ask if I will remove her as an Elder and have her family deal with her.
As I answer their questions, some of them nod while others do not move a muscle. Some show signs of relief but others maintain their rigid stance of mistrust. Some are reassured but others are not. Ohjan and Voren speak to those who remain unhappy after I answer all their questions. When the men leave, Ohjan and Voren speak to me. They both say it went well. Of those who came to ask questions, 3 fully support me, 3 support me but remain worried, and 2 oppose me becoming Kiera. Ohjan reiterates that I did well.
I continue to study more of Thurgen’s speeches to prepare for the speech I will give after my Ascension. Bronnen helps me. As we work, Mor’Sovra comes in to speak with us. She tells us the Ascension will be on the 10th of Quern and the Mating Ceremony will be on the 12th. I am told that Mor’Renna has a heavy voice on the Ascension and both Ohjan and Emric agree she should be listed to, having been Ascended to Kiera once herself. Sovra does not seem upset by this. She tells me about the robes and dresses I will wear for the Mating Ceremony and all that is involved in the rituals, all the steps and all that is expected of Bronnen and me. 
We have to prepare the robes, not make them, but gather everything needed for them: paint, specific oils, fetishes, etc. Sovra talks about shoes we need to wear – fawn skin shoes made from a single piece of fawn skin. She talks about our tone of voice and how we walk procession style, gliding. Bronnen and I are both stunned and shocked by the amount of work and detail that goes into a Hularen wedding: meditations, what to meditate on, ritualists words, and so on. Sovra answers all our questions and after she leaves, Bronnen and I walk for a bit afterwards. Bronnen has attended Hularen weddings but did not know all that went into preparing for them. I have attended innovar weddings and I don’t think any are as detailed and involved as a Hularen wedding.
That afternoon, Bronnen and I head out of Ilyrian with our weapons. We go out into the wilder forest that surrounds Ilyrian and walk for almost an hour. Bronnen finally stops and speaks to a fey in the trees. I hear a female voice respond. I understand nothing that is said as I do not speak Sylvan. From a bag, Bronnen pulls out twisted sprigs of thyme and sage and lays them at the base of the tree. He bows and walks by to a small brook where he lays out a lunch and pulls out a skin of wine. As we eat, invisible water sprites jump out of the water. Near a large rock, near a fern is a large bullfrog with a brown spot on its back. I look closer and see that the brown spot is a tiny saddle.
“Belliobanship live here,” Bronnen explains, “they are a family of fairies, a large family. I found this place as a boy. The eldest son of the head of the family is Agmaramiellas Icathacuskialbontiam Belliobanship. The oak tree is Kodemathenagog. Kodemathenagog sleeps most of the time and dreams. He remembers the Great War. Shialla of Kodemathenagog is his wood-wife.”
A female voice above our heads speaks, “We do not know this one. Why do you bring a stranger?” Shialla of Kodemathenagog.
“Shialla of Kodemathenagog, this is Carathul Yornlin of the Varkier line. We are bonded and soon to be mated,” Bronnen says as he introduces us to one another.
Shialla is beautiful, like a yellow flowering bush and very tall, standing about 6’6”. Shialla is a Dryad like the one I saw on the Dragon’s Foot near Kiern’Kirak.
“We know Thurgen; knew him” she says.
“Cara is Thurgen’s descendant,” Bronnen explains.
A different voice, “Is it true?”
“I won’t wake Kodemathenagog for a mortal, he’s been asleep for a long time. He is peaceful.” Shialla of Kodemathenagog
Bronnen and I both nod before Bronnen turns to the fairies behind us and tells them how he and I met. The tiny fairies are interested in his quest to Travaghn and all the times he defended me. He tells them about some of my adventures before we met, including the Dryad I met near Kiern’Kirak.
“Shenthunka, perhaps,” Shialla muses. 
A fox mount appears with a tiny rider who welcomes Bronnen. Bronnen introduces me to Belliobanship.
“Cara of the wild lands is different. The aura of her being shines with a different light,” Belliobanship.
I look around and see fairies ringing us in the tall grass.
“We have another guest today,” Belliobanship says.
I look around and see another fairy. She is blue with purple braided hair, 6 translucent wings and wears a gossamer silk tunic and short skirt. Her toes and fingers are very long and she’s very slender. She is crouched on a branch.
“I am Pikilitharnilia,” she says, “I am from the North and came with news of the dark things. The druids of the North are angry and hurt, separated from the Mother. Some seek the fey for help but the blood of Thurgen has judged them. Queen Yaullatheratizia, the Queen of Thurapix, sent fey out to learn the truth. Destiny brought us together on the same day.”
Bronnen translates her words for me. He speaks to all the fairies gathered around us in Sylvan and tells them about me.
“It is true, the kin of Thurgen Varkier judged the druids unworthy of the Mother’s touch,” Bronnen answers.
“Queen Yaullatheratizia would have the druids restored,” Pikilitharnilia says.
“We’ll listen and give it thought but this act, while harsh, will prevent great bloodshed. There is a darkness beyond the wood and Cara wants to make sure our people do not become prey to a predator – one of the great Boggerwahl trapped in the Homewood – and the enchantments on his prison are fading.” Bronnen
An older barefoot tiny fairy steps out. He has a long beard with silent bells woven in, paws for feet and grey hair with blue and brown streaks. He holds a long pipe between his sharp teeth and wears a red and green floppy hat. He is Belliobanship’s father and Elder of the tribe. An old woman creeps out behind him and peaks around him to see. She has grey hair covered by a green and orange handkerchief. There are silent silver bells woven in her hair. She is Belliobanship’s mother.
Bronnen tells me that Shialla and Koda were from the Homewood and left long ago. The tiny fairies run out to share our food. We enjoy our lunch with the Belliobanship family of fairies. About mid-way through our lunch, we hear a crunch in the grass. All the fairies scatter and Tythis comes into view. He wants to know what we are doing and why we are out here. Bronnen tells him we were having a quiet lunch and that we will be back in an hour or two. Volik nods but advises Bronnen to stay closer to the house next time, he knows how dangerous the woods can be. Volik backs off some distance so we can eat in peace. We finish our lunch and pack up. Bronnen bids the fairy folk farewell before we leave and we walk back home. 
In the market square, we see so many new faces. People are coming from near and far to see the Varkier descendant and to see my Ascension.
That night when we sleep, I do not dream.

**Summary of the Journal Entry:**
Cara spends the day preparing for her Ascension by studying Thurgen Varkier’s speeches and meeting with the Elders to answer their questions about her background and intentions. Although some Elders remain skeptical, Cara gains their respect through her responses. In the afternoon, she and Bronnen visit a sacred area in the forest, where they encounter fey creatures and share stories with the fairy family of Belliobanship. They also meet Pikilitharnilia, a fairy with news from the North regarding troubled druids, and learn of a looming threat: the release of a dangerous creature, the Boggerwahl. After a peaceful lunch with the fey, Cara returns home, contemplating the mix of support and uncertainty surrounding her Ascension.

---

**Key Items:**
- **Dream Journal**: Where Cara records her dreams and sends copies to Father Sandlin.
- **Speeches of Thurgen Varkier**: Historical records that Cara studies to prepare for her own leadership speech.
- **Fawn Skin Shoes**: Special shoes needed for the Ascension and Mating Ceremonies, made from a single piece of fawn skin.
- **Twisted Sprigs of Thyme and Sage**: Offerings placed at the base of a tree by Bronnen as part of their communion with the fey.
- **Silent Silver Bells**: Worn by the fairy family, symbolizing their connection to magic and tradition.

---

**Important Locations:**
- **Ilyrian**: The main setting, where Cara prepares for her Ascension and addresses the Elders.
- **Elders' Gathering Site**: Where Cara meets the Elders to answer their questions and concerns.
- **Kodemathenagog’s Grove**: A secluded forest area where Bronnen and Cara meet the fairies and commune with the fey.
- **The Market Square**: Filled with visitors and onlookers arriving to witness Cara’s Ascension.

- **Cara (Mor’dahn)**: The protagonist, preparing to step into her role as Kiera.

- **Bronnen**: Cara’s bonded partner, who introduces her to the forest fairies and supports her preparation for the ceremonies.
- **Mor’Sovra**: Host of the Elders’ gathering and helps Cara with ceremonial details.
- **Pikilitharnilia**: A fairy from the North with news about druids troubled by separation from Mother.

- **Tythis**: A cautious figure who checks in on Cara and Bronnen during their forest lunch.
- **Kodemathenagog**: An ancient, sleeping oak tree in the grove, with a connection to Hularen history.
- **Shialla**: Kodemathenagog’s wood-wife, a tall Dryad familiar with Cara’s ancestors.

- **Gain Support from the Elders**: Cara answers questions to reassure the Elders of her intentions.
- **Study Thurgen’s Speeches**: Cara reads these to understand the leadership style expected of her.
- **Prepare for Ascension and Mating Ceremonies**: Gathering ceremonial items, understanding ritual steps, and practicing procession.
- **Communion with the Fey**: Connect with Bronnen’s fairy allies, learning about their customs and discussing the challenges facing their lands.
- **Address the Northern Threat**: Understand the possible resurgence of the Boggerwahl, a deadly creature whose prison enchantments are fading.

- **Meeting with the Elders**: Cara faces questions regarding her loyalties and background, securing partial support for her role as Kiera.
- **Learning about Thurgen’s Leadership**: Cara studies Thurgen’s speeches, shaping her understanding of her responsibilities.
- **Forest Gathering with the Belliobanship**: Cara meets a family of fairies and receives insights into fey life and history.
- **News of the Druids’ Troubles**: Pikilitharnilia shares information on the separation of Northern druids from Mother, hinting at turmoil and the need for intervention.
- **Discussion of the Boggerwahl Threat**: Cara and Bronnen consider the fading protections over a monstrous creature, foreshadowing a potential crisis.

These lists capture the political, ceremonial, and mystical elements surrounding Cara’s journey, her interactions with the fey, and the looming challenges as she prepares for her Ascension.

Read the following dream as recorded by my fictional D&D character, Cara. Summarize the dream and include important facts and instructions. Give a title to the dream:  Dream 88: 
It’s cold and the wind is blowing. I open my eyes. I am propped against a tree way up in the mountains. It is daytime and I am wearing my traveling gear. I cannot tell which mountains I am in. The Waif sits on a boulder nearby, His knees tucked to His chest. He’s staring out over the distant plains at trees. I stand up and walk over to Him and wrap my cloak around Him. He smiles at me. I look where He’s looking and see column after column of men, hundreds of thousands of Hulean Imperial Soldiers. Blue pinions dot the land, and I know these are the troops that returned from Arboria. These are the troops Lieutenant Major Commander Everass said were on our Northern border, waiting for his order to attack and raze our home to the ground for any presumed provocation. 
We are in the Spine facing West, North of Woodhome and South of the Diradel lands. The Waif grabs my cloak, stands up, and walks toward a mountain pass through a few trees and into a crevice into the mountain which goes down at an incline, deeper into the Spine. As we descend, it gets dark. We walk until the crevice opens into a huge cavern filled everywhere with lit flickering candles. He walks around a pool of water to a set of stalagmites that almost look like a chair or a throne. He hops up and props Himself up on them. He swings His legs watching me as I stand opposite him on the other side of the pool of water.
“Are you happy, Cara?”
“Yes, I am happy.”
“You don’t seem happy, Cara. You complain a lot more than you used to.”
“I do? About what?”
“Too much to do, too many places to go, you don’t know how to do this or that, too many people to talk to. You seem like you worry about a lot of things. That’s why I ask if you are happy.”
“Did you know how to be king?”
He shrugs, “I just did stuff and people followed but you know the stories. We made mistakes, and sometimes terrible things happened, but we still did it. You’re gonna do what you need to do.”
I hear a beast slamming at a cage somewhere in the darkness behind Him. I look down at my waist and on my belt hangs a key ring with 7 keys (the 7: Sarana, Malin, Reynar, Roland, Silas, Venrik, and Hardin), plus one black iron key and one blood red metal key (Father Timmeran & Fire Mountain Girl). 
“You got stuff to do, Cara, but are you happy?”
I tilt my head trying to remember. Something about this place tugs at my memory but I cannot remember, and it bothers me.
“You want to remember, don’t you? You want to remember why you’re here.”
He looks down at the pool of water, which is still and dark, the surface glassy. I step forward and stare into the water. In its reflection, I see myself standing in a different cavern, in a homespun dress that hangs to my knees. I am standing in the water up to my mid-calf and the water glows blue. Nearby is a tower of stone ringed with mist and blue-white lightning. Near me stands a woman and I recognize Mor’Renna. We are deep within her cave. 
The water clears and now I am way above in the sky looking at an enormous wood cut through by a river: Woodhome. As I watch, the river turns from blue to grey to black and the green trees wither and blacken. At the same time, millions of people begin screaming, choaking, and crying out as the entire wood turns black from corruption.
I see children screaming in terror, clawing at their throats as the air they struggle to breath burns their throats and lungs. They die by the thousands clinging to their mothers or each other. I see mothers trying to protect and shield their children, embracing them, holding them close. The terror of their children reflected and multiplied in their eyes as they, too, die. I watch fathers and warriors clawing at their skin and the air, unable to fight the corruption invading their homes and killing their families, their weapons useless, as they die where they stand.
“This is what happens,” Mawdra’s voice comes through the pool.
I watch in horror as the woods of Woodhome fall eerily silent and still. Fewer than a dozen heartbeats pass before I see the corpses of millions of Hularens begin to twist, twitch, and jerk until they once again stand in the places they fell. Their skin is grey, their eyes empty of all but death, their hands clawed, their teeth fanged: gross mutations. They are still the Mother’s children, but the dark, corrupted children of a dark, corrupted Mother. As one, they turn to face the North and surge through the woods in the millions, bent on destruction and death and the singular purpose of destroying all of Mother’s enemies.
“Either you unleash our people or the Mother will and this is what will become of us. So, you see, child, there is no other path,” Mor’Renna explains.
The image fades away. I look up from the pool of water to the Waif who sits silently watching me. I hold back tears. He tilts His head.
“You still like my dog, though?”
I laugh at the unexpected question and change in direction, “I love your hound.”
“I thought when I showed you this, you would remember, but somehow you forgot.”
“I don’t remember this, I don’t remember You showing me this.”
“Well, now I’ve reminded you. Now you remember?”
I nod my head, “I have a memory of a memory.”
“Well, it was a long time ago. Be your own person, Cara. Do as I ask, uncage the beast. Wood, earth, and water will lead you to fire. Do not tarry, travel beyond, use the key, then fast away.”
The Waif slides off the stalagmite chair and stands up. My vision blurs and He’s gone. I turn around to leave the cavern and the Waif’s face is in front of mine. He’s floating in mid-air, lightning flashing in His eyes. Thunder crashes in the cavern and echoes, almost blowing the cavern apart around us. 
Porthios speaks, “Travel to the place that was, gather what is required. Harken to Me, child: travel forth when the great bird calls. The last of the set is close at hand, but so too, is the enemy. All things in order, child, all seasons in their right time.”
Thunder explodes flinging me backward in slow motion into the pool of water. 
“Do not be Sinas,” the Waif whispers.
I hit the water in the pool, and it steals my breath away.

**Title**: *Dream 88: The Path of Fire and the Unleashing of Mother’s Children*

**Summary of the Dream:**
In this intense and prophetic dream, Cara finds herself high in the mountains, looking out over the vast Hulean Imperial forces with the mysterious figure known as the Waif. Together, they descend into a cavern, where Cara glimpses visions of potential devastation. She sees the horrific consequences of inaction: a corrupted Mother, her children turned into deathless, monstrous beings, wreaking havoc on the world. Mor’Renna warns that Cara’s decision to unleash their people or face a dark transformation is the only way forward. The Waif encourages Cara to be her own person, guiding her with cryptic instructions to unlock the beast, align the elements, and heed a coming call.

---

**Important Facts:**
- **Hulean Imperial Soldiers’ Presence**: The Northern border of Cara’s homeland is lined with hundreds of thousands of Hulean soldiers, prepared to destroy her people if provoked.
- **The Keys on Cara’s Belt**: Cara possesses seven keys tied to significant figures (Sarana, Malin, Reynar, Roland, Silas, Venrik, Hardin), along with two unique keys—a black iron key and a blood-red metal key.
- **Visions of Woodhome’s Corruption**: Cara sees a twisted vision of Woodhome, overtaken by dark forces that mutate the Hularens into a monstrous army, turning them against their enemies in the North.
- **The Beast Unleashing**: Mor’Renna’s message is clear: Cara must unleash their people to prevent the darker fate.
- **Four Elements for the Path**: The Waif instructs Cara to follow the elements—wood, earth, water, leading to fire—as steps to fulfill her role.

---

**Instructions from the Waif and Porthios:**
1. **Unlock the Beast**: Cara must release the dormant power within her people to prevent their transformation into corrupted beings.
2. **Travel the Elements**: Begin with wood, earth, and water, ultimately leading to fire. These elements will guide her in unlocking the necessary power.
3. **Respond to the Great Bird’s Call**: This mysterious “call” signals the timing for Cara’s journey to the past location to gather essential items.
4. **Do Not Be Sinas**: Avoid the fate or choices of Sinas, a figure likely associated with failure, hesitation, or defeat.

---

**Key Insights:**
- Cara’s inaction has catastrophic potential, risking the transformation of her people into a force of deathless monsters, corrupted by Mother’s rage.
- The Waif and Porthios, both cryptic and powerful, suggest that Cara’s path is one of personal choice, responsibility, and awareness of time’s order.
- The elemental journey through wood, earth, and water to reach fire hints at a spiritual or physical transformation critical to her role.

This dream warns Cara of the weight of her decisions and the inevitable reckoning that lies ahead. It urges her to follow specific elements, heed symbolic calls, and uphold her purpose to prevent the loss of her people’s soul and connection to Mother.
