Read the following journal entry for my D&D character, Cara. Create a list of important items, locations, names, objectives and events. Each list should be a separate category. Include a summary of the of the journal entry: 37th of Solik, 2324 IC    37th of Solik, 2324 IC. Ilyrian; Dream 88: 

Wake, pray, and eat. Bronnen wakes me up early so we can see Mama and Papa off, they are leaving for Travaghn today. Papa is dressed in full uniform. He and Mama are ready to leave. Ohjan and Mor’Sovra are here, too. Emric arrives and opens a tree portal for Mama and Papa to travel through to Travaghn. Emric tells them he will wait for 2 days and then 2 more for their return. We say our brief goodbyes and I watch Mama & Papa walk through before returning to the house.
Emric returns in an hour for me and we walk back to his hut. While he sets everything up for my tattoos, I tell him of Lysara’s memory of Kiern’Varn. He gives me blue selkie poison which makes everything tingle before going numb. It has a slight paralytic effect; he can’t have me moving around as the runes must be perfect. He works quickly and deftly. It hurts but not nearly as much as if I were not paralyzed and numb. 
“You have come a long way, and I would not have picked you for who you were. Maybe the Storm God brought you here, maybe,” Emric says quietly.
He continues to work and talks while I listen. He talks about my little move in Laneroc with the Varmarkuhn and what I did to the Arch Druids.
“Now,” Emric advises, “you need to speak with the people of Ilyrian. They think you allow innovar to come and go as they please, that our home is not worth defending. Give them a good reason why you let Lieutenant Major Commander Everass leave – some kind of strategy whether real or not, but something.”
Emric spends 2 ½ hours just on the tattoos on my face. As he works, Johlon Wiervarn appears.
“You have her under a knife, that’s what I want,” he growls.
Emric just grunts in response and continues to work.
“Say whatever it is you want to say to me,” Emric replies peacefully.
“I want her, pieces of her. I promised I would bury her in the soil she defiled,” Johlon seethes.
I cannot move my head, but I can see him. 
Emric scoffs and continues to work, “You wouldn’t hurt a girl as I give her the marks of her family. The young druidess is not invited.”
“She’s Mawdra’s pawn,” Johlon’s rage boils in his words.
“She summoned the glyph. She wore the amulet. She is Varkier and we are hers. I don’t agree with what she did, but she has the right to do it. You will come to your senses,” Emric says, his voice calm and even.
Emric sets his tools aside, reaches down and opens my shirt, exposing my heart. He looks from me to Johlon, “There. Do it. Spill Varkier blood. Spill Hularen blood.”
I stare up at Johlon Wiervarn as he walks over to me. He looks terrible: gaunt and hollowed out. I am unable to move as he wraps his fist around a knife. I read pain, anguish, and rage in his face. I meet his eyes, and I do not look away.
“Johlon has led the Wiervarn for 97 years. Cara has Varkier blood. You can kill her and give the people back to Jurva but you don’t want that. Cara’s 20. There’s much she doesn’t know but you can help guide her. She was taught by Mawdra, do you wish to teach her?” Emric goes back to work starting on the left side of my chest while Johlon continues to debate killing me.
Emric lists all of Johlon’s good qualities.
“I know Cara’s mind. She is not mad at you for wanting to kill her. She hopes you are here for the people, and she is scared shitless of all the decisions she must make. She hates what she did, and it tears at her,” Emric says, glancing briefly into my eyes.
A single tear slides from the corner of my eye as I watch Johlon who finally releases the knife and sits down on a stump.
Emric continues to talk, “She thinks the druids are hiding the people from the Asha’kari because that’s what the druids have allowed everyone to believe. A little honesty and truth would go a long way. Cara has been places she shouldn’t be able to go. I think Renna brought her into a Pool of the Mother, that she saw an active Eye of the Mother, and even a live Font Tower. She has found other things.”
Emric rolls me over and begins working on my back. Johlon Wiervarn begrudgingly agrees with Emric. I will restore his connection to the Mother. When Emric is done with my tattoos, I dress and go find Mor’Renna. She says that I can restore his connection on my own, she taught me how. I return to Arch Druid Johlon and reconnect his connection to the Mother before returning to the Gorhund home. There are 40 men in the back garden. I do not recognize all of their family tattoos. There are 4 Gorhund and one of them is Tythis. Another is Keldoss, one of Voren’s sons. 
As I walk into the back garden, one of the unfamiliar men spots me, gives a signal whistle, and the men stand. Tythis walks over me and the Gorhund surround me which I find odd.
“These men are from the Raelos family. Elder Grakis Raelos is inside speaking with Ohjan. They want to hear the truth of Jurva Thierkiernon.”
Tythis introduces me to the men of the Raelos family. One of the men, the one who whistled approaches, staying an arm’s length back when the Gorhund stomp a warning.
“The Gorhund were not the only ones who defended the Varkier. I am Faeron Raelos, Warleader of the Raelos. You are small for a Varkier,” Faeron says.
Faeron and I look one another up and down. 
“Raelos are ravens. Can you fly?” 
Faeron’s eyes go wide, and his face turns red. Everyone goes very still and I don’t understand that what I have said is considered by Hularen culture inappropriate and rude. But Tythis breaks the tension by laughing and clapping his hand on my shoulder.
“Go inside little cub,” Tythis says. 
He stays outside with the Raelos while I walk inside, into the kitchen, and begin prepping vegetables for dinner. Moments later, Tythis comes in and laughs at me, telling me that what I asked was considered rude but I certainly make things interesting. Ohjan walks into the kitchen and finds us there. He says Grakis Raelos wants to speak with me. Ohjan says he told him my truth, my journey here, and why the innovar (keys) are hidden here in Ilyrian.
I walk into the living room to meet Elder Grakis Raelos. He is in his 50’s and has lots of facial tattoos and very bird-like features. He wears a feathered cloak of black raven feathers. His chest is covered in tattoos. Ohjan introduces us to one another. We all sit and Elder Gradkis speaks.
“The Gorhunds told me your story. I am from the West in the Old Wood.”
We talk at length about many things, and he asks a number of clarifying questions which I answer. Ohjan, Grakis and I talk about the Tahlrin (Council of Elders) which meets every 6 weeks. They suggest the Tahlrin bring a list of topics and suggestions to me after their meetings. After Grakis leaves, I tell Ohjan that Tythis thinks I should kill an orc before I send men to kill them. Ohjan is surprised and agrees I should join in the fight with the orc. 
“Can you fight as a Hularen?”
“I can but I have worn armor since I was 14,” I reply.
“We can find you something to wear.”
Ohjan opens a hidden door, and we walk into the armory together. In the armory there are 80 suits of armor. Some are leather, others are metal, and a few are mithril. Almost all are intricately detailed. There are also close to 100 weapons ranging from daggers to longswords, bows, and other weapons I have never used. Most of the weapons are common metals but a few are made of blue metal (Ehrduhn). There is also a silver band that creates a magical armor shield “suit.” 
In Ohjan’s study are books written in Hularen. One of the books contains speeches made by Thurgen Varkier, his father Demanius Varkier, and his grandfather (X) Varkier.
“You may read them or, rather, have Bronnen read them to you,” Ohjan offers.
Ohjan leaves to attend other business while I go to eat a late dinner. The rest of the family has already eaten. I speak with Mor’Sovra, Eladia, and Bronnen about various topics and ask Sovra’s permission to speak with the Elders here in her home tomorrow. She consents.
“Tythis, please tell the Elders who are waiting to speak to me that they can come all together tomorrow and bring two warriors each.”
I eat dinner and clean up after myself before going upstairs to check the scroll cases Arch Bishop Sandlin and Father Bodin gave to me. There is a message from Arch Bishop Sandlin informing me the matter with Commander Everass has been resolved and he’ll let Papa explain further. I reply to the Arch Bishop’s message with Father Bodin’s message to me in case Bodin was unable to send us both the same message.
I wash and go to bed. 

Dream 88: Are You Happy – Do Not Be Sinas
It’s cold and the wind is blowing. I open my eyes. I am propped against a tree way up in the mountains. It is daytime and I am wearing my traveling gear. I cannot tell which mountains I am in. The Waif sits on a boulder nearby, His knees tucked to His chest. He’s staring out over the distant plains at trees. I stand up and walk over to Him and wrap my cloak around Him. He smiles at me. I look where He’s looking and see column after column of men, hundreds of thousands of Hulean Imperial Soldiers. Blue pinions dot the land, and I know these are the troops that returned from Arboria. These are the troops Lieutenant Major Commander Everass said were on our Northern border, waiting for his order to attack and raze our home to the ground for any presumed provocation. 
We are in the Spine facing West, North of Woodhome and South of the Diradel lands. The Waif grabs my cloak, stands up, and walks toward a mountain pass through a few trees and into a crevice into the mountain which goes down at an incline, deeper into the Spine. As we descend, it gets dark. We walk until the crevice opens into a huge cavern filled everywhere with lit flickering candles. He walks around a pool of water to a set of stalagmites that almost look like a chair or a throne. He hops up and props Himself up on them. He swings His legs watching me as I stand opposite him on the other side of the pool of water.
“Are you happy, Cara?”
“Yes, I am happy.”
“You don’t seem happy, Cara. You complain a lot more than you used to.”
“I do? About what?”
“Too much to do, too many places to go, you don’t know how to do this or that, too many people to talk to. You seem like you worry about a lot of things. That’s why I ask if you are happy.”
“Did you know how to be king?”
He shrugs, “I just did stuff and people followed but you know the stories. We made mistakes, and sometimes terrible things happened, but we still did it. You’re gonna do what you need to do.”
I hear a beast slamming at a cage somewhere in the darkness behind Him. I look down at my waist and on my belt hangs a key ring with 7 keys (the 7: Sarana, Malin, Reynar, Roland, Silas, Venrik, and Hardin), plus one black iron key and one blood red metal key (Father Timmeran & Fire Mountain Girl). 
“You got stuff to do, Cara, but are you happy?”
I tilt my head trying to remember. Something about this place tugs at my memory but I cannot remember, and it bothers me.
“You want to remember, don’t you? You want to remember why you’re here.”
He looks down at the pool of water, which is still and dark, the surface glassy. I step forward and stare into the water. In its reflection, I see myself standing in a different cavern, in a homespun dress that hangs to my knees. I am standing in the water up to my mid-calf and the water glows blue. Nearby is a tower of stone ringed with mist and blue-white lightning. Near me stands a woman and I recognize Mor’Renna. We are deep within her cave. 
The water clears and now I am way above in the sky looking at an enormous wood cut through by a river: Woodhome. As I watch, the river turns from blue to grey to black and the green trees wither and blacken. At the same time, millions of people begin screaming, choaking, and crying out as the entire wood turns black from corruption.
I see children screaming in terror, clawing at their throats as the air they struggle to breath burns their throats and lungs. The corruption causes their flesh to bubble and boil, blacken and rot. They die by the thousands clinging to their mothers or each other. I see mothers trying to protect and shield their children, embracing them, holding them close. The terror of their children reflected and multiplied in their eyes as they, too, die. I watch fathers and warriors clawing at their skin and the air, unable to fight the corruption invading their homes and killing their families, their weapons useless, as they die where they stand.
“This is what happens,” Mawdra’s voice comes through the pool.
I watch in horror as the woods of Woodhome fall eerily silent and still. Fewer than a dozen heartbeats pass before I see the corpses of millions of Hularens begin to twist, twitch, and jerk until they once again stand in the places they fell. Their skin is grey, their eyes empty of all but death, their hands clawed, their teeth fanged: gross mutations, monsters of corruption. They are still the Mother’s children, but the dark, corrupted children of a dark, corrupted Mother. As one, they turn to face the North and surge through the woods in the millions, bent on destruction and death and the singular purpose of destroying all of Mother’s enemies.
“Either you unleash our people or the Mother will and this is what will become of us. So, you see, child, there is no other path,” Mor’Renna explains.
The image fades away. I look up from the pool of water to the Waif who sits silently watching me. I hold back tears. He tilts His head.
“You still like my dog, though?”
“I love your hound,” I whisper as the tears fall down my cheeks.
“I thought when I showed you this, you would remember, but somehow you forgot.”
“I don’t remember this, I don’t remember You showing me this.”
“Well, now I’ve reminded you. Now you remember?”
I nod my head, “I have a memory of a memory.”
“Well, it was a long time ago. Be your own person, Cara. Do as I ask, uncage the beast. Wood, earth, and water will lead you to fire. Do not tarry, travel beyond, use the key, then fast away.”
The Waif slides off the stalagmite chair and stands up. My vision blurs and He’s gone. I turn around to leave the cavern and the Waif’s face is in front of mine. He’s floating in mid-air, lightning flashing in His eyes. Thunder crashes in the cavern and echoes, almost blowing the cavern apart around us. 
Porthios speaks, “Travel to the place that was, gather what is required. Harken to Me, child: travel forth when the great bird calls. The last of the set is close at hand, but so too, is the enemy. All things in order, child, all seasons in their right time.”
Thunder explodes flinging me backward in slow motion into the pool of water. 
“Do not be Sinas,” the Waif whispers.
I hit the icy water in the pool, and it steals my breath away as I plummet below the surface.

I sit bolt upright in bed, sopping wet and terrifyingly cold. I shiver uncontrollably, my teeth chattering, and my breath frosting in the air. Bronnen jumps out of bed. A heartbeat later, his hands are on either side of my face. I don’t know how many times he says my name before I hear him, thunder still ringing in my ears.
“Cold,” I manage to stutter. 
Bronnen picks me up and then wraps me in robes and a fur. He’s wet, too, and the bed is soaked. I cannot stop shivering from the cold and my jaw is starting to ache from my chattering teeth. Water drips from my hair and eyelashes. Bronnen scoops me up, carries me downstairs into the living room and kicks up the coals. He wraps the fur tighter around me and sits behind me, holding me close until the shivering stops. As we sit in the firelight, warming up by the fire, I tell him of the dream.
I do not know if the Great Bird is Father Bodin or the Lord Emperor or something else. When we are both warm and dry, we return to the bedroom, strip the sheets and blankets from the bed and hang them to dry. We pull the mattress off so it, too, can dry and replace it with a mattress that is not currently in use. Then we put clean, dry sheets and blankets on the bed and go back to sleep.

Awakening from the dream physically cold and drenched, Cara shares the vision with Bronnen, deepening her resolve to confront her destiny.

Read the following journal entry for my D&D character, Cara. Create a list of important items, locations, names, objectives and events. Each list should be a separate category. Include a summary of the of the journal entry: 36th of Solik, 2324 IC   36th of Solik, 2324 IC.

Wake, pray, and eat a quick breakfast. I put on my Porthion armour. Bronnen is in his leathers. Ohjan is in a blue tunic with black breeches and boots and a sword. 25 men and women wait to escort us. There is an older man among them carrying only a moon sickle. His name is Weyron and he is a Shepherd Druid. Ohjan tells him and the other druids to stay back a mile. Weyron picks up a leather wrapped bundle. Inside is a gold short-staff capped by an orb and carved with runes. Most of the men and women are in their 30’s and 40’s.
Weyron walks to a tree and opens a portal for us to walk through. Weyron is one of the most powerful Shepherd Druids in Woodhome. The man next to him is Tasaar from Laneroc and taught most of the Moon Druids like Eladia. A second portal is opened. 5 druids turn into seagulls and fly through the portal as Uhlarn druids join us. 
I step through the portal behind Ohjan. When we step through, it’s chilly and I breathe in the ocean. We are an hour early and outside the cabin. When all are through the portals, Ohjan gives directions to move, and we start walking toward the buried trench where Jeggred and I found the dark shard. I am surrounded by warriors, and everyone is on guard.
Close to noon, a very wide dimensional door opens. 12 griffons and riders fly over the area. On the beach, multiple portals open and Dragon Guard walk through. There are 4 units and each unit consists of 4 Dragon Guard in armor and 1 Dragon Guard Mage. 20-30 magical eyes fly in all directions scanning the immediate area and beyond. Next to walk through one of the portals is High Prince Shirock Leighon. Behind him, Vamathagarius swoops through. He is 187-feet long with a head large enough to bite a ship in half and talons the length of a 12-foot pike. When he lands, the ground shakes and the Lord Emperor looks tiny perched on him. Vamathagarius is an elder dragon. The Lord Emperor, in full armor, slides off Death Strike’s back.
I give the Lord Emperor a soldier’s salute and bow. The Lord Emperor and High Prince advance and I hold my bow. Vamathagarius says something in Draconic and seconds later, meteors fall from the heavens about 400 yards up the beach. The Lord Emperor walks straight up to us.
“Rise,” he tells me.
He wants to speak to me alone, so we walk off some distance together and talk.  We walk to where Jeggred wielded Lygoth and closed the ground over the ruin. Lord Emperor Greyhawk pulls Lygoth and blasts open the door Jeggred and I had previously sealed. I feel the corruption pour out in waves. The Dragon Guard create a Sphere of Force around the box holding the dark shard which partially mutes the corruption I feel. Vamathagarius picks up the sphere of force enclosing the box holding the dark shard.
“Take it to the oubliette,” the Lord Emperor instructs.
A Pelorian priest opens a gate to another plane. Vamathagarius sets everything down inside the planar gate.
“There are 6 more like it there,” the Lord Emperor says.
The Lord Emperor reaches out, touches my armour, and we are suddenly elsewhere. We appear in a giant square stone room. There is a Porthion priest I do not know in here. He opens a gate, and we walk through into a strange place with a reddish-pink sky and oddly coloured trees. Here, a Mishakelian priest opens another gateway, and we walk through into a wooden room. This room is very plain. There is a table ringed with 10 chairs and 4 more positioned in front of a fireplace. The Lord Emperor uses magic to light the fire. There is a window, and when I walk over to look out, I see stars that I do not recognize. A huge chunk of wall floats by in the distance. Half a city floats by upside down.
The Lord Emperor pours me a glass of wine before pouring himself a glass. He watches me for a moment before sitting down in one of the chairs at the table. He says he wants detailed answers from me.
“Porthios has meddled in many things he should not have and kept too many secrets,” Lord Emperor Greyhawk says, his voice soft and low.
“There are truths I cannot speak, Lord Emperor. Hunger knows and hears and sees what you know, hear, and see – or he can. There are some things he cannot know. Some things that the other Asha’kari cannot know. I don’t know if Hunger and the others have contact or not or send messages using minions or not. Porthios is clear, some things must remain secret from everyone, even you, Lord Emperor.” 
 He acknowledges that Morvic may have connections outside of Travaghn. He pulls a scroll over in front of him and reads a bunch of notes he wrote about me. I find this odd but say nothing.
“You have 6 months to bring Woodhome to heel and who legitimate progress or I will remove the threat,” Lord Emperor Greyhawk warns. 
He asks many questions, and I answer as many as I am comfortable with but when the Lord Emperor begins prodding for answers I refuse to give, a shadow of a man filled with lightning appears in the room with us. Lord Emperor Greyhawk is not surprised, he was deliberately asking questions he knew I would not answer, waiting for Porthios to make an appearance. 
“The Watcher is her task, leave her to it,” Porthios says.
Lord Emperor Greyhawk pushes his chair back, stands, and walks around the table right up to Pulo, challenging him, emperor to God. Porthios says nothing and after a moment of prolonged silence, He disappears.
Lord Emperor Greyhawk and I continue our discussion, and the Lord Emperor is very candid when he speaks. He tells me to reach out to Arch Bishop Sandlin who will arrange access to the shards the empire has retrieved. He also tells me to send Arch Bishop Sandlin a list of the Asha’kari names that I know. He writes notes as we talk.
I watch as the Lord Emperor pulls a small vial from a concealed pocket and drinks the contents of a potion to forget everything we talked about in this room, only the notes remain and those stay here in this room. The Lord Emperor opens a portal, and we walk back onto the beach. There is a forest dragon (Lenorn) in the Duskwood. The Hularens are angry at my disappearance but say nothing. Bronnen’s eyes are filled with anger.
Lord Emperor Greyhawk flies off on Vamarthagarius while the High Prince and the Dragon Guard leave the way they came, through portals. I walk back into the woods with Ohjan and the rest of our wardens and warriors. I look in the direction of the forest dragon and Druid Weyron says its name is Veranthagus. The druids open tree portals, and we walk through back into Ilyrian.
Ohjan dismisses the Wardens and we walk over to Mama, Papa, and Mor’Sovra. I tell them what happened on the coast with the Lord Emperor and our chat after. Papa is concerned.
“The Lord Emperor expects you to align the people as one unified force and get rid of dissidents. I think he didn’t tell you what to do because he doesn’t think you can and he already has a plan in motion to deal with Woodhome and its inhabitants. Either he believes you are a distraction, Cara, or he’s giving you room to see if you are trustworthy. Regardless, he already has a plan for either outcome. You need to unify the people quickly.”
Bronnen speaks up, “We are going to take the Dragon’s Foot. Cara has decreed it.”
We both know I haven’t.
“We need it,” he continues, “Cara doesn’t need to convince anyone why, not a Kiera.”
“It’s a large ask,” Ohjan says and he’s right.
Mama, Eladia, her sisters, and I all help Mor’Sovra prepare dinner. After we eat and clean up, I sketch Lysara’s room in Kiern’Varn and give them to Ohjan to put in Thurgen’s book of speeches. Bronnen and I talk quietly outside. He worries about assassins. I tell him of the Waif’s warning and as if on queue, Dragon Guard magi appear outside Sovra’s house.
“I am Lord Militant Commander Everass of the Hulean Imperial Army, recently returned from Arboria with 22 brigades (5000 men per brigade) stationed in the plains North of Woodhome. I am here to speak with Bron Yornlin.”
I turn and quickly walk into the house to get Papa and Ohjan. This could turn sour very quickly. Either the Lord Emperor is testing us just after our talk or this man is acting on old orders. Either way, we need to resolve this as quickly and peacefully as possible before war erupts here and now between Woodhome and the Empire.
Papa addresses the man first, “Kaidran.”
“Bron.”
They exchange pleasantries before Lord Militant Commander Kaidran Everass informs all listening why he is here in Ilyrian.
“The Emperor has given me the rights to take military control over Woodhome, whatever the cost, if I see fit but not for 6 months. I have remit to burn the whole forest to the ground if necessary, and that is what I will do to avoid a prolonged war on our border.”
He and Papa have a good long talk soldier to soldier, quietly, but the Gorhund have excellent hearing and I know they can hear every word said between the two. Papa finally gets Kaidran to agree to leave and just as he and his men try to leave via magic, Emeric shows up and nullifies their spell.
In perfect Imperial common, Emric says, “It is easier to get here than leave.” Emric makes a small hand gesture and shows the Imperial Dragon Guard all the many sets of eyes surrounding them, watching and ready to spring into action. Ohjan reminds Everass of the agreements in the treaty between Woodhome and the Hulean Empire.
“You have breeched the Lord Emperor’s own contract and made him a liar,” Ohjan growls softly.
I quote Hulean Imperial Law to Lord Militant Commander Kaidran Everass as pertains to the illegal breech per our treaty. He gives me a small smile.
“You are also in breech of the treaty. Preventing the Army of the Hulean Imperial Empire to leave is a call for war.” He all but sneers at me and I realize he is just looking for any excuse. 
“There would be no need to prevent the Hulean Imperial Army from leaving these lands if they had been invited in. They were not. The Hulean Imperial Army and the Dragon Guard are in breech of the alliance between Woodhome and the Hulean Empire, having come into these woods uninvited and unprovoked and threatening war. You want this,” I say.
Everass’s eyes glint. He thinks I am a silly child.
“Your men can disarm, stay the night, and return with my father in the morning when he goes to speak with the Lord Emperor. You can explain to the Lord Emperor then your actions and the breech of our alliance.”
I watch as Everass calmly dismisses the Dragon Guard with him.
“You have made it clear that you are not allies with the Empire.”
I look at Papa and whisper, “He wants to be captured. I don’t understand this tactic. He deliberately breeched the alliance and came without provocation. He wants war.”
Papa doesn’t understand either. He and Everass speak quietly for another 5 minutes after which, Papa walks back to me and leans in close.
“Let him go, Cara. There will be bloodshed tomorrow if you don’t.”
Papa doesn’t look at me but turns back around to face Everass. I don’t like it. I don’t like it at all.
“Leave, Lord Militant Commander Everass. Take all the men you brought into Woodhome with you and leave. Do not come back, do not breech the alliance again. Whatever your orders, they are old and I will not be goaded into war with the empire simply because you want more bloodshed.”
After they leave, we all go inside to discuss what just happened. Emric says that the druids allowed the Dragon Guard to breech the woods and enter Ilyrian. Papa explains that Everass fought in Arboria for the last 7 years and he along with his men are highly capable soldiers. Sovra says I should have killed them all. Ohjan says Everass has made the internal struggle among Hularens worse and this incident will quickly spread across Woodhome with many calling for war with the empire. 
They switch topics to potential enemies closer to home. Papa agrees with Ohjan, Sovra, and Bronnen that killing Jurva won’t stop her siblings from trying to kill me and she has 5 brothers and 4 sisters living. The Thierkiernon line is 40-thousand strong.
“You need to know how far to prune the tree, Cara,” Ohjan says.
He explains that an execution would create a Blood Debt but if Jurva dies in a challenge, she loses her power, her control, and there is no blood debt to claim. Although, the rules are slightly different for the Varkier.
I help prepare dinner and we eat together. After I help clean up, I write a letter of the day’s report to Arch Bishop Sandlin to share with the Lord Emperor. His reply is almost immediate. He is quick to remind me that detaining or imprisoning a Hulean Imperial soldier is against Hulean Imperial law and punishable by death. He is relieved I released Everass. I do not wish to argue with the Arch Bishop. I do not need to remind anyone that Everass broke the terms of the alliance between Woodhome and the Empire. Instead, I do as I always do with the letters he sends, I do as he instructed me to do: I burn the letter.
 I check the second scroll and find a message from Father Bodin, too, short and brief but I am happy to hear from him. When I am done, I burn Father Bodin’s letter, too. Bronnen says he has something he wants to show me. I pull on my cloak and grab my boots so we can travel to the Southern Fields where people from Lanneroc have come and set up camp. I do not yet have my family tattoos, so Bronnen applies them with makeup. A man named Tythis walks up as Bronnen works. Tythis is huge, has brown hair, and three long scars across his face. He has family tattoos of Gorhund and Vartress (a Wiervern family). Tythis is a Gorhund War Chief and Bronnen’s uncle, Ohjan and Voren’s younger brother. 
He laughs at the job Bronnen is doing and takes over. He runs the War Hounds in the West at Werfol. While Tythis works, skillfully creating my family tattoos, Bronnen tells me the words he thinks I should say.
“Bra’gen werethun Varkier. It means, ‘come again, Varkier.’ You should scream it out at the top of your lungs when we reach the Laneroc camp just South of Ilyrian. The Varmarkuhn and the Vratheen are old clans, Cara, and they have made the journey from Laneroc to see you, to hear you. You should announce yourself as Carathul Varkier, a daughter of Thurgen Varkier, and bond-mate to Bronnen Gorhund. Then scream, ‘Bra’gen werethun, Varkier!’ When they stop chanting and cheering, you should thank them for showing their loyalty and then make the sign for ‘I see you.’ Do it several times to encompass them all and so that all gathered may see.”
I don’t quite understand the importance of this moment, but I know they have been waiting for the return of the Varkier line for a very long time. Bronnen and Tythis walk with me and Borvahn joins us. The hounds surround us and suddenly, I have a large escort. We get beyond the trees to where there was a field. The open space is now covered with tents and campfires. We are on a rise looking down over the field.
Bronnen whistles and signals to get their attention and I watch as people from Laneroc pour through the trees. At least 400 people come out of tents. The people of Laneroc are even more heavily tattooed and pierced than the people of Ilyrian and it is quite a sight.
I do as Bronnen suggested, waiting for everyone to gather and quiet. 
“I am Carathul Varkier, a daughter of Thurgen Varkier, and bond-mate to Bronnen Gorhund. ‘Bra’gen werethun, Varkier!’”
The people of Laneroc roar back and those who can take war form. The crowd is dotted with cats and the trees nearby come alive. 80-foot tall trees add their roars to the din and I cannot help but smile. When the roaring stops, they cheer and when the cheering ceases, I continue. 
“I thank you for your loyalty.”
They roar and cheer again when I make the sign for “I see you,” several times. The people go wild stamping their feet and beating their fists on their chests. I raise my sword into the air and as I bring it down, two ghostly shapes flank me. They are the size of horses, and they have giant fangs and claws. The ethereal cats roar and the people roar back chanting Varkier. As we walk away, I hear them chanting the war chant and the trees keep the beat. Their chant rings across Ilyrian.
“That was just one warband from Laneroc,” Bronnen explains. “They can field just under 1000 warbands, close to half what the Gorhund can field.”
We walk back to the house. Sovra and Ohjan are standing on the front porch waiting and listening. I cannot quite tell what Mor’Sovra’s look says and Ohjan is as unreadable to me as ever. I tell them about the two cats that appeared beside me.
“Var’thagen,” Sovra says in way of explanation. “They are the cats of the Varkier.”
We listen to the war band from Laneroc chanting and we are not alone, most of Ilyrian has stepped out of their homes and onto their porches to listen. I step up next to Mor’Sovra and lean into her. She wraps an arm around me. She’s proud, fiercely proud as the people chant for over an hour. Ohjan steps in front of me and cups my face in his hands.
“It is amazing what a little hope can achieve. Words are the most powerful of magic.” He, too, is proud.
As he walks back into the house, he tells Sovra that I need to be marked tomorrow. She nods but we stay as we are, her arm wrapped around me, listening to the people of Lanneroc chant. Receiving my tattoos will take most of the day. When quiet descends over Ilyrian once more, I go find my parents. They are out back and they, too, were listening to the people chanting. 
I tell Mama goodnight, but Papa wants to speak to me first before I go to sleep. He has suggestions and plans. Even when he is at rest, Papa is always strategizing.
•	Settle the Dragon’s Foot and protect the South of Hule.
•	Open trade with Blackwall and protect the channel. 
•	Do not profit from the empire’s shipping trade by taxing those who pass through the channel.
•	Ask for 30-50 expert magi to be stationed at Seastone, all unmarried, to help defend the South-western border of Hule.
•	Crush the lotus trade coming out of Thornwall.
•	Woodhome has wikkin – Soldier’s Paste – and an herb that grows only here which the empire uses to make healing potions. Keep the trade for both open and keep the price fair.
•	Ask for 2 or 3 ships to help patrol and protect the Southern borders.
•	Offer to become the Western defense of Hule, watching everything from Farwood and South to Seastone, from Wouthern Woodhome East to the tip of the Foot. 
•	Wait 5 years before allowing anyone to settle outside Woodhome in the West, North of our borders.
•	Spend the next 10 years settling the Dragon’s Foot, opening trade with Iron Hill and Treetop.
When I go to sleep, I do not dream.

Read the following journal entry for my D&D character, Cara. Create a list of important items, locations, names, objectives and events. Each list should be a separate category. Include a summary of the of the journal entry: 35th of Solik, 2324 IC   35th of Solik, 2324 IC. Ilyrian

Wake, pray, and study my bible. Bronnen is writing a list.
•	Collect the shard & store it in the Deepen Well on Kiern’Kirak.
•	Collect the Key & bring to Ilyrian with the others.
•	Complete the Mating (marriage) Ceremony.
•	Complete Pilgrimage to Raven’s Point Lake – take Thurgen’s Var’fascar and Sarana’s blood with us, we’ll need both somehow.
•	Find and help the Watcher (Orlim) & return to Ilyrian.
•	Deal with Jurva Thierkiernon and the orc.
Bronnen and I walk outside together to greet the Mother before I go bathe. Like Sovra, while I am here in Ilyrian, a lovely warm bath is part of my morning ritual. When I connect with Her, I feel Her and Her heartbeat, Her breathing. I feel the sun on my skin and hear everything around me begin to wake. When I open my eyes, I see someone in the shadow of the trees but I cannot tell who. When I ask Bronnen, he smiles and assures me it is only the Wardens who ring our home.
“Why do they watch us?”
His eyes widen slightly as he looks around. He takes my hand and we walk toward the trees. A large man steps out. He reminds me of Quarn, the Knight of Porthios, but he has Gorhund tattoos and 2 heavy serrated bladed axes on his back. He is Barath Gorhund. 
“Why are you here, Barath,” Bronnen asks but just as quickly answers his own question. “Ohjan called you here.”
Barath says nothing, just stares.
“How many are here,” Bronnen quizzes.
“50-some-odd from our house. I was in the North yesterday. I’ll be here as long as needed. There are Uhlarn Wardens and Druids here, too. Fissok is here,” Barath says.
Bronnen’s eyes widen but he doesn’t explain his surprise to me. Instead, he says, “Barath is a pack leader and very skilled.”
Barath speaks again, “Morvahn Uhlarn speaks as leader at Wardenhall. Cordin is also there, another cousin. Peran is in the West – trouble with Rustani. He took 3 packs West 2 months ago blood-hunting up and down the coast. What is going on, Bronnen. I understand defending a Varkier but there’s more.”
I tell Barath why they are here, what I did to the Arch Druids, and I explain my plan to raise an army for the orc. Barath likes what I say.
“It shows strength and power,” he says as he salutes me. “We’ll be ready, Carathul Varkier.”
I watch as he silently melts back into the woods before I walk to the bathhouse to bathe. When I return to the house, I help make breakfast. Eladia is still quiet.
She growls low and accuses, “You kept a secret and ambushed them all.”
Not for the first time do I wonder if it was my suggestion, if severing the Arch Druids from the Mother was part of my plan. It seems cruel and suddenly, I remember a conversation with Mor’Renna.
“I remember,” I say, slowly and quietly, “I remember arguing with Mor’Renna that I couldn’t keep such a secret for so long from so many people. I argued that I couldn’t do something so cruel. We argued back and forth until finally she said, “Fine,” and walked away.”
I look up at Eladia who is watching me, her eyes full of anger and hurt. 
“She wiped my memory because I was afraid I couldn’t keep this plan a secret from Bronnen. I didn’t want to keep secrets from him or Emric, Ohjan, Sovra, or anyone else. I didn’t remember because I couldn’t remember and I couldn’t remember because she made it so.”
Some of the heat leaves Eladia’s eyes and we finish making breakfast. We bring breakfast out to the family and we all eat together. The talk is kept light. Ohjan asks to speak with Bronnen when he is done and when all are finished eating, I help clean up. Papa wants to speak to me when I finish and walks out back to smoke his pipe while he waits. While we continue to clean the dishes with Sovra, Bronnen comes by with his full kit, sword, and bow.
He looks at us, “I’ll be back.”
Mor’Sovra sees and she also has a look. She nods her head at me indicating I should go and find out what he is up to.
“There are scouts along the Northern border,” he says but offers no further explanation.
As we pass through the trees, we come to a camp. I count 24 campfires with 4 to 5 men at each fire. Eladia and Jehan are also here along with many of the Gorhund Wardens from Ilyrian. There are many others I do not know.
“Ohjan is concerned the scouts are not tracking Spriggen,” Bronnen says. 
There are 135 Wardens and 20 Druid here. While Bronnen checks on the status of things to learn what information he can, I speak with Eladia. She has some hard things to say. She does not like what I did or how I did it and she expects me to fix it. I listen to her and say nothing, offering no apology or excuse.
Papa comes over and talks about me as a little girl. Papa and Eladia both advise through different ways to show mercy and restore or kill the severed druids.
“Talgrin Meryl was a horse thief, do you remember, Cara? He killed men and stole their horses. He was the first person I ever executed in front of you. Life isn’t always about forgiveness. You have power and a responsibility, a duty to use that power to make the world better,” Papa instructs.
After talking with both, I go find Mama and talk to her. As we talk, I hear whistles of alarm. A hawk swoops down, lands near us, and becomes a person. Ohjan walks past us and to the druid.
“Druid Sircon?”
“It’s not scouts trailing Spriggen, Elder, but 2 Thierkiernon war bands. Arvahan Thierkiernon leads them. He says that you, Carathul, and her parents are to be brought to Thornwall.”
“No,” Bronnen responds. “Thierkiernon have no right to demand Varkier do anything and these are Gorhund lands. We welcome brothers in peace but we will bury enemies.”
“They have backed away from Ilyrian and say they will give us a day to change our answer. They are camped 2 days North,” Druid Sircon tells Ohjan.
“Take 2 more war bands,” Ohjan says calmly. He gives Druid Sircon a message penned on paper. “Give this to Arvahan to give to Jurva. It’s an invitation.”
Ohjan looks at Bronnen before he continues, “4 to 2 or 5 to 2 against. Arvahan will not want conflict unless Jurva has ordered him to shed blood.”
“That would simply things if she struck first,” Ohjan says. “% feral war bands are on their way from Laneroc.”
I remind both Ohjan and Bronnen of the timeline. I must be in Raven’s Point in 21 days and we cannot afford a delay because of infighting. They aren’t happy about it but agree. Mor’Sovra takes charge then, leading me away to take my measurements so that I can be fitted for an Ascension Ceremonial dress and a Mating Ceremonial dress. Mama and Mor’Sovra argue over design, cut, color, style, fit, embellishments, and so on. 
By late afternoon, we go into the town square where they continue to argue over jewelry. Mor’Sovra insists on silver, Mama wants gems and finally they compromise on silver inlaid with gems. I let them decide whatever they want. I am Mama’s only surviving child and compared to her wedding, both to Sargeant Major Papa and to my birth father, this wedding will be extravagant. 
While we are out, I tell Mama and Sovra that I dream-walked again and need to speak with Emric. They allow me to go for an hour to speak with him and I dash off. At his hut, I explain what happened in detail. He says I am not really dream-walking but that Porthios is enabling this.
I walk back to the house and help with dinner. Bronnen comes back and tells us the Thierkiernon war bands retreated, returning to Thornwall. We catch one another up on what happened during the day. 
“Arvahan Thierkiernon was only here because Jurva sent him to bring you to Thornwall. He said he didn’t come to shed blood.”
Bronnen says we need to come up with a plan for Jurva, she’s causing no end of trouble, but I cannot help wondering if it is all a misunderstanding. We eat dinner together and I help clean up after. Then, we all gather outside to talk and relax around the fire while the children play and for the first time, I hear Eladia sing in a perfectly beautiful voice. It is mesmerizing and when I look over at Sovra, she is watching her eldest daughter intently, unshed tears glistening in her eyes. Eladia hasn’t sung since her mate died over a year ago.
Papa says the Lord Emperor is already in the East and will have a war battalion with him of 100 men, 25 priests, and 25 Dragon Guard magi. Ohjan says we will leave at dawn to meet the Lord Emperor and his host.
When Bronnen and I retire to his bedroom, I check the scrolls and find a brief message from Arch Bishop Sandlin reminding me of my loyalties and duties.
We sleep and I do not dream.
