Read the following journal entry for my D&D character, Cara. Create a list of important items, locations, names, objectives and events. Each list should be a separate category. Include a summary of the of the journal entry:   33rd of Solik, 2324 IC. Ilyrian

Wake early. The robe is still damp. I write the dream down in my dream journal. Bronnen also had a dream. His dream was a warning and he tells me that if we get separated, I must kill anyone who isn’t blood, who isn’t family – trust no one and allow no one near you.
Dress, pray, pack our gear, and kit our armor. We go downstairs. Mor’Sovra is dressed in fancy Gorhund regalia. She disapproves of what we are wearing and tells us we must change into something more appropriate. She tells Bronnen exactly what to wear before taking me to her room. She hands me a blue over-robe to wear. I put it on and she tells me to be calm, respectful, and strong and to speak with confidence.
“As an Uhlarn, you are Speaker of the Trees and Caretaker of the Mother. As a Varkier, you are first among Her children: Her rage when needed and Her wisdom when it is not.”
She talks a great deal about duty versus choice. As she talks, the uses traditionally prepared paints to mark my face “Varkier” on one cheek while Eladia marks me “Uhlarn” on the other cheek. When they finish, we go eat breakfast and make our final preparations. Bronnen, Eladia, Mor’Sovra and I walk to the traveling tree where 40 people are already assembled and waiting for us along with Ohjan, Mama & Papa. The Gorhund Wardens are all armed.
“We agreed to 6 Wardens, not 40.”
Ohjan and Bronnen look at me but say nothing about the increased number of Wardens accompanying us. 
“Jorrel will meet us. He has returned to Oakdelve to retrieve more people,” Ohjan says.
Mama’s face is painted with the Uhlarn symbol on one cheek (birth family) and a Kingfisher (3rd Brigade & Papa, her mate) on the other. Papa’s face is also marked with the Kingfisher on one cheek (birth family) and the Uhlarn on the other (mate), opposite sides of Mama’s. I turn to Eladia and ask her, “Do you remember the time I described the 9 Chairs and said I needed to speak to the Trees?” 
We both smile. The Wardens to not recognize the Varkier marking. Arch Druid Emric arrives, dressed and painted, wearing a fur stole and bones. He has his staff with him. He speaks briefly to Bronnen and me and in so many words tells us not to pick a fight with the Arch Druids and answer their questions – that’s it.
The 40 Gorhund Wardens form up around us as Emric opens a tree portal and steps through first. Half of the Gorhund Wardens follow Emric before we walk through followed by the rest of the Gorhund Wardens. The trees are massive. I see oak trees as big around as a house and multiple Grandfather oaks with black and silver bark. There is a moss-covered cartouche. This place reminds me of the Homewood but without corruption. 
Ohjan calls for Jorel who steps forward with 40 Uhlarn warriors, 25 of which are large Shield Wardens and the rest are druids in green robes. A man that looks almost identical to Jorel steps forward wearing a necklace of wooden leaves with silver veins. Ohjan wears a necklace of large fangs. Jorel’s twin brother Ederas Uhlarn, greets Ohjan and they appear to be friends. Ohjan introduces Bronnen and me to Ederas Uhlarn. He greets Mama and Papa as well. Ederas walks up to Mama and hugs her, welcoming her to the Uhlarn family. He speaks to Papa with respect and welcomes him as family. It is a genuine and heartfelt welcome. Then, Ederas welcomes me.
“Wherever you go, Carathul, you will not walk alone ever again unless you choose to do so,” Ederas says to me.
Bronnen, Arch Druid Emric, and I walk on through the barrier and as we near the cartouche, I start to feel Mother’s presence. It is in the air and my vision becomes even clearer. The deeper we walk, the stronger the feeling grows. We pass broken ruins, pieces of a wall, and bits of statuary. We are in one of the old places.
I feel flashes of emotion: anger, fear, longing, remorse, perseverance, confusion, and more. It is Lysara. The feeling becomes stronger and I realize I am not just feeling Lysara but other spirits here.
“Emric,” Bronnen whispers.
“Keep moving, the feeling will pass,” Emric says quietly.
He keeps us moving at a steady pace and whispers th entire time. I feel sadness and grief. I sense the spirits trapped here and it feels very wrong for them to be trapped here in this place. We pass through another barrier and back into the forest and the feelings fade. Waiting for us near the cartouche are the Arch Druids: Gulrian Uhlarn of the Heartwood, Garratos Jakarn of the Western Ridge, Alveron Thierkiernon, Johlon Wiervarn of the North-west, Alveron Gathier of the North-east, Yannik Raelos of the Southern Reach, Torvel Gallerohn of the Eastern Reach, Eldain Baeorn of the North. Emric Thulmaroon of the South joins them.
The Arch Druids are standing within the stone circle. Emric has prepared us for this. We know he will walk up the steps and then we will be invited to approach. Emric will take his place within the circle with the other Arch Druids and then, Alveron will invite us into the circle. The Mor’Fang are carved with their points straight up and while there are 12 cartouches, the is called the Circle of Nine. Emric walks to the top of the stairs and speaks in ancient Hularen before inviting us up to the stone circle. Emric takes his place, standing in front of one of the pillars as Bronnen and I walk up the steps together and stop at the top, careful not to cross the cartouche. We wait for several heartbeats before Alveron calls us forward by name.
Bronnen and I walk forward. In the center of the Circle of 9, surrounded by the Mor’Fang is a well and we feel the presence of the Mother. I feel something at the center of my chest thud, right where Mowdra’s amulet was and disappeared. I smile and look at each of the Arch Druids in turn, happy to be here. 
“Welcome Carathul and Bronnen…” Arch Druid Alveron Thierkiernon begins.
Everything goes in slow motion and something inside my head feels broken, almost panicked, as words pour into my mind. My first thought is that Lysara is chanting, and I am saying the words of that chant out loud but that’s not correct. The voice in my head is my own. I know these words. I have a memory of this. I have practiced the words, repeating them over and over until they are familiar. My hands are moving, drawing a glyph. This, too, I have practiced over and over until I can form the glyph and say the words comfortably and with ease.
The Arch Druids go from looking confused to horrified. Even though everything around me has slowed, I am quick and speak the words comfortably, my movements and gestures are fluid. The stone circle around the well shines and runes glow as energy pours out into the Circle of Nine. I finish the chant and clap my hands together. I am immediately weary but deeply satisfied. From all the Arch Druids, lines of energy pull from them into the circle and they collapse where they stand.
I hear a voice outside the Circle of Nine say something. I don’t understand the words, but I know I need to repeat them, it’s important that I finish. The air around us pops and Mawdra walks out of the woods. Bronnen stares at me wide-eyed. 
Arch Druid Alveron looks up at me and asks, “What have you done to us?”
Mawdra answers, “Done to you? What has she done to you? What have you done, you foolish, foolish men? How long have you  and the line before you piddled about these woods speaking fear? You, who defanged and declawed us, making us deer and cattle. I have waited thousands of years for this moment. I have endured generations of your predecessors. Weak-willed rabbits satisfied to teach our people softness, to hide. For thousands of years I have listened to the echoes of my husband’s rage, his grief, his disappointment. I have toiled in silence waiting for one of our bloodline, one of our lost children to return. 
“You lay crumbled by the bloodline of Varkier. You who would say you hold power here, know this: the spirit of the greatest Kier of our people has looked on in disgust. You think the druids led our people to safety. What does a gentle druid of Naemora know about leading people? But fear not, our line has returned. The burden of leadership is no longer yours and the only payment for your crime of peace, of platitudes, of placidness is your connection to Naemora, Herself. You will spin no more spells. You will no longer feel Her touch. My child will lead you and should those of you who see the error of your ways and come to support the re-awakening of our people, in time you may re-earn the Mother’s touch. For those who resist, you may walk this earth as an innovar. Such is my will, not Mawdra, not some twist of my name: Mor’Renna.”
“You’ll destroy us,” Arch Druid Emric says.
“You will, certainly. Our people matter, but you, Emric and you, Gulrian, have a choice: serve the Varkier in power or remain as you are. Your actions have been to restore us. For that, you may swear fealty now and return as some aid to the rule of Varkier.”
The dreams of Mawdra’s cave were not dreams but memories. The glyph was powered by the Mother – this is what Mother wanted. I know this is right, this was something I agreed to – I know I must happen for us to face the darkness to come. I remember, after touching the skull, Mor’Renna would take me to a place to feel Thurgen’s panicked rage of what the druids were doing to the Hularen people and being furious at his own impotence to do anything about it. Thurgen believed the Hularen druids must be conquered. I remember.
“Emric, Gulrian, I will have your answers now,” Mor’Renna demands. 
“I will not serve you, woman. You are a remnant of a Kiera long gone but I will serve the Varkier and I will aid Cara in any way I can,” Emric responds.
“Spoken like a true Hularen. Cara, return him to our bosom, he will serve us well,” Mor’Renna instructs.
I know exactly how to do this and as I say the words, the Mother allows Emric to be reconnected to Her. Emric gasps and stands. He doesn’t look at me but instead turns to face Mor’Renna.
“The glyph Cara created here will remain for 200 years and at any moment your link with the Mother can be severed. Your fire will serve you well. Serve our queen and your king, if she chooses to mate him,” Mor’Renna says to Emric.
I remember another memory. I remember asking Mor’Renna why she didn’t find the Varkier line. She told me she failed to find the Varkier line because the Mother was not strong enough. Mor’Renna said she was a link for the Mother and she had to stay near the Mother to keep hopping bodies until the Mother was strong enough for her to leave. I remember her telling me that I am part of Porthios’s peace offering. Porthios needed Mor’Renna’s forgiveness, no one else, because she was a link to the Mother.
“Gulrian, what do you choose,” Mor’Renna asks.
“I hold no respect in deceit,” Gulrian replies.
“Deceit is a weapon, and all weapons will come to bear in the fight to come. There is no honor where survival is at stake but know the deception of the druids is spread through all Hularens today. So, complete your lie, you believe it yourself as truth. Even now, you keep people from Kiern’Kirak. The druids were not leaders of the people but of our faith in the Mother: caretakers, advisors, not leaders. Do you wish that role again, Gulrian, or will you stay among the innovar?” Mor’Renna asks.
“Like Emric, I will not serve you, but I will serve Cara if she takes the role of Kiera. I will serve our people,” Gulrian responds. 
“Serving our people is the point, Gulrian, not neutering them. Cara,” Mor’Renna nods at me.
I say the words a second time to reconnect Gulrian to the Mother. There is a pause before the Mother accepts his reconnection to Her.
“You, Alveron, no words will ever bring you to peace with me. You who supported the perversion of our people and allowed the Thierkiernon to pervert our ways. You who would have us scheme, connive, and betray like the innovar. Never in this life or any of the following you might survive to live them will you ever be returned to the Mother. If you utter one word, I will kill you and cast your spirit into the abyss myself” Mor’Renna threatens.
Alveron says nothing. Gulrian stands.
“My descendant carries the Varkier blood and the Uhlarn. Where do you think she gets it from?”
Mor’Renna shifts into the Uhlarn war form of a tree wife before she slowly shifts back to her own form.
“You do not hold power here anymore. The rest of you will consider these words: you may feel hate if you wish but what you should feel is shame. You have only to look there at the Mother to know it is She who powers your shackles. So weak is our connection to Her that you cannot hear Her and Her chosen sat quietly in the wood all this time. Naemora is the nature of this land; spouting the Mother does not get involved – lies. You who allowed Her wounds to persist and called it the remnant of Her. The rest of you sondiers this and when you have decided, you may approach your new Kiera and beseech her to speak on your behalf to the Mother. Perhaps She will restore you, perhaps not, but I will think of you not at all,” Mor’Renna says emphatically.
She turns to me, her eyes flashing, “The next step, Cara. Gulrian should take us.”
I know in my bones the next step is to go to “Nuan’legot.” She doesn’t need to tell me, I remember. 
I turn to Gulrian and tell him, “We must travel to Nuah’legot.”
Nuah’legot means Valley of Trees and is in the (Spine of the World) mountains that cradle the West side of the Vale. Gulrian looks between us: Emric, Mor’Renna, and myself. Emric nods and I follow them down the steps and out of the Circle of Nine. I know, I remember, that Nuan’legot is not in Woodhome. I know, I remember that the Mother demands our presence there. We walk to a tree and Gulrian opens a tree portal which leads to El’Lendrun and from there, we’ll go to Nuan’legot. Mor’Renna steps through first and we follow her into an old place, the ruin of El’Lendrun. Gulrian opens a second portal door in what was a wooden wall. There are torches lit here and inside the ruin of El’Lendrun is a single, large, block of stone.
“Place your hands on the stone and I will take us to Nuan’legot,” Gulrian instructs.
I know, I remember that Mor’Renna cannot leave Woodhome and so cannot travel with us. I look at her and she gives a small nod.
“You know what must be done,” she says softly. “Return to the Circle of Nine when you are done. Be safe. Be careful. Remember, he has slept for a very long time.”
Something soft moves behind Mor’Renna’s eyes. I feel her own longing and love, her own grief and remorse. I place my hands on the stone. I know what to do next. A moment later we appear somewhere else. I see another large stone block with symbols etched into the stone. I also see part of a circle and the remains of 10 stone cartouche. This Mor’Fang is no longer complete. I know, I remember that I need to enact a set of keywords in the stones to show me a passage to my destination. I enact the runes and chant the words Mor’Renna taught me.
Bronnen is silent, purposely so. I feel his anger and confusion. I touch the stone and hear a crack as the large stone block slides sideways revealing stairs that lead down. As I descend the stairs, stones begin to glow and light the path. I walk through a broken gate. This place is old. More stones light up with a pale blue-white light. When we reach the bottom of the steps, a path leads up to a central section which can be reached by a few steps up onto a platform. All the lights in this room flare to life. This place feels familiar. I walk toward the water. I feel a presence and something inside me stirs. Lysara stirs, eager to move forward with urgency. The blue glow becomes stronger and across the water, I see on the central stone platform a large, shiny box. I know, I remember, we need whatever is inside.
“I need a way across,” I say. My voice infused with Lysara’s need and urgency. 
Emric creates a way for us to cross the water. On the central platform is a statue of a giant cat – my cat – a lion. I walk over to the solid silver box which stands 4-feet tall and 4.5-feet wide. It is covered in Toltemic runes. I know, I remember, I need to touch the silver box. No one else must touch it, no one else is Varkier. I reach out my hand and place it on the silver box and hear a hidden lock click open. I slide the lid off and look inside. Inside the silver box is a layer of rotten velvet. A mere touch causes the ancient material to crumble, revealing bones. In the air around us, I hear a moaning growl and then a voice speaks in ancient Hularen. We turn toward the voice and see an ancient spirit. Thurgen looks at me and I watch as his eyes shift from familiarity to confusion. He was expecting Lysara, not me. I do not understand his words but Emric and Gulrian do. 
Gulrian translates the ancient Hularen into current Hularen, “I am Thurgen Varkier, your Kier.”
We all bow. After three heartbeats, I straighten but Emric, Gulrian, and Bronnen remain bowed. I have freed the spirit of my many times great-grandfather. As I watch, Thurgen shifts into his war form of a lion, then back again.
Thurgen speaks again in ancient Hularen and Emric answers his questions in ancient Hularen while Gulrian quietly translates their conversation so I understand what is being said. Emric tells Thurgen what they know as to what happened. He tells Thurgen of the flight of the people to Woodhome and their struggles after. He then explains why the Varkier no longer rule because the line of Varkier was lost for generations until recently.
“Awaken our people, Carathul,” Thurgen instructs, his eyes fierce.
“You have weapons that can kill Asha’kari. I need to understand them,” I say. 
“I only have wisdom. In life, there were two: the Thumb-Fang of Goraxsos and the Mask of the One. These two the Asha’kari feared. If the Ethragen remain, the more there are to give power to the Mask of the One, the more power you wield. The claw of an ancient red dragon, Veraxamathius, is imbued with its spirit and it knows no fear of Asha’kari magics. Both were in Kiern’Kirak when I died. The claw is long, the length of a walking stick. These the Asha’kari feared. Thuin Dutharn (Sanctuary) has a headdress like mine – it is important. ”
Jeggred has the Thumb-Fang (Claw) of Goraxsos. He hid it away in the cave in the Wild Wood. 
“The evil spell remains unfinished by those who ambushed Hunger.”
Thurgen seems to jump topics a bit.
“The Ethragen channel their magic to the mask and the wearer may use it to destroy. Once the mask is powered, it will tie you to the war city of Ortheal and the war city of Senaroc. It will drive great beams of energy, powerful enough to destroy and Asha’kari – they (the beams) are Mother’s power. The Ethragen are mine (possessive tone, not that he was Ethragen but that they were loyal to him), the fascar was created for me and the fang is impervious to Asha’kari magic. 
“Renna’s form is Uhlarn. Mine is the lion. Only a child of Varkier blood can carry both their parent’s war forms.
“Destroy the spell, find the mask, gather the Ethragen. Rule our people with wisdom, strength, patience, and love. Balance these against the Asha’kari. Beware of cunning and deceit. Their greatest weakness is each other. Return our people to glory. Be the leader our people need. Rule well.”
Thurgen fades away, his spirit free of this place.
Inside the silver box holding Thurgen’s bones I also find the remains of his feathered headdress. All the feathers are gone having decayed long ago but the silver band is untarnished. I also find a man’s torc – his mating torc. It is braided silver and inscribed with runes. I pick up both items knowing his spirit is at rest. I carefully pull out all of Thurgen’s bones and place them gently in a sack. We will take his bones into the woods and place them in a tree. I close up the large, silver box which is now empty. We walk up and back out. I reseal the tomb, placing my hand once on the stone until it moves back in place, hiding the stairs that lead down. Then, I chant the words Mor’Renna taught me to silence the runes on the cartouche and circle before walking out of Nuan’legot. Gulrion closes the portal through the wooden wall behind us and we return to the Circle of Nine.
The moment we walk through back, Bronnen stops and refuses to take another step.
“We need to talk,” his anger leeches into his words. 
He watches me closely. I hand Mor’Renna the torc, Thurgen’s torc and watch as she removes the one, he gave her, putting his on. She hands me her torc and walks away. I walk back over and stand next to Bronnen.
“Tell me what you did,” he demands. His body is rigid next to mine, “We agreed we did not want to rule. We agreed, Cara. We made plans together. Explain this to me. Did you lie?”
“No, Bronnen. I don’t want to rule as Kiera. Me, now, here. I don’t want to rule. I want to adventure with you. I want to do all the things we planned together. I want that. I didn’t know, I don’t remember that when I was brought to Mor’Renna’s cave, I made a different choice. That was two years ago. All this time we talked and made plans; I don’t remember that I had already made a different choice. She convinced me this was the path, and the only path forward to heal the Mother, to strengthen Her children, and to defeat Her enemies was to become the Kiera. I didn’t remember until the moment I did. I feel like I don’t know my own mind. It is confusing and I don’t know how to sort through it.”
He looks hurt and it tears at me.
I do my best to explain. I have never been to the Circle of Nine before, but I knew it instantly in the moment when time slowed down. I do not know the words I spoke in ancient Hularen, or didn’t, but in the moment I began speaking them, I knew them and what they would do. I did not know about the glyphs I was drawing in the air, or I didn’t before I started drawing them, but the moment I began, I knew them and what they would do. I knew because I remembered. I knew what I did would sever the Arch Druids from the Mother, I knew that should be their punishment for how they have failed Mother and Her children. In that moment, I remembered why I was doing what I was doing and that this was the only way – cruel and decisive and final and necessary. 
I try to explain to Bronnen that these memories, I didn’t have them, I didn’t remember them until the moment I stepped past the boundary of the Mor’Fang and into the Circle of Nine. It was like something unlocked within me and suddenly, all the time I spent practicing the words and inflections and cadence and rhythm and hand gestures in Mor’Renna’s cave came flooding back. I knew, I remembered, this was the right path, the right thing to do because the other path would lead us to ruin and destruction and corruption and darkness.
I explain to Bronnen that even as I was doing it, knowing what I was doing, I couldn’t stop myself. Even though part of me despised what I was doing, I couldn’t stop because stopping meant failing Mother and Her children. This path was the only path, the only choice to make, the least terrible of all the terrible choices presented to me. What I have done repulses me but part of me knows it was right, it is right, and at the same time, I hate it.
He stares at me in silence and minutes pass before he speaks. His voice is soft, but I hear anguish and revulsion. 
“I am afraid you have started a war. You didn’t give the people or the druids a choice. We need to find a way to undo this, to wrestle control from Mor’Renna.”
“Maybe I reconnect the Arch Druids to the Mother and give them the choice,” I offer.
“No, that won’t work. We could bring the heads of the families together and explain how the people should be – convince them. Then you could return the connection to the Mother to those druids that will work with us.”
He says ‘we’ and ‘us’ and I feel relief flooding through me. We did not agree to this but he’s not walking away. Bronnen and I discuss a number of topics including the orc coming out of the mountains on our Northern border, reclaiming the Dragon’s Foot, the Sumarac, and Thornwall. We move to the topic of Hunger and the Sleeper (Greed).
“I think they are underestimating Hunger’s essence. I think they (the Empire) are trying to chain the ocean.” 
As soon as I say that I feel pressure in my feet and then, everything goes black. I haven’t fallen unconscious, I realize I am in a pitch black room. Something or someone grabs my wrist. I am without mass, traveling through darkness like the shadowed Dragon Guard. I stop again in another pitch black room and a voice speaks in the darkness.
“There is a chair behind you, Carathul Yornlin of the Varkier line.”
I do not recognize the voice, and I do not move. Someone, perhaps the owner of the voice, takes my hand and guides me to the chair. I sit in the chair, still unable to see. I hear someone walk a few paces away. Boots echo in the dark room, marking the footstep. I also hear the distinctive sound of Dragon Guard armor as someone sits in another chair near me. The steps are sure and confident so whoever this is either knows the room and its contents well or can see in the total darkness. 
“Do not speak about Morvic,” he says.
The voice is quiet, calm, and refined. I say nothing, not knowing who I am with and aware that Bronnen will be livid at my disappearance.
“I was instructed to listen for certain words from you,” the voice explains. 
I remain silent. The person speaking pulls out a small object enchanted with a Continual Light spell. Sitting across from is a half-grey elf with blue eyes dressed in the armor of a Dragon Guard Weapon’s Master but the gemstone that is a normal part of the Dragon Guard’s armor is missing. Now I know who sits across from me: Darhawk Leighon, only son of High Prince Shirok Leighon, and grandson of Lord Emperor Greyhawk. I look around the room and discover we are in the Black Basalt room, the one Father Bodin took me to and told me that if things went bad in Travaghn, this was a safe place. No one could find me here or overhear our conversations here.
“Aladin told me to keep an eye on you and he told me to tell you some truths. The remnant of Morvic became “unruly” some years ago, the first time in many years, and the emperor’s connection to Morvic alerted him. The emperor secreted messages to a few trusted people through him (Darhawk) which Morvic could not intercept,” Darhawk explains.
He noticed that my gaze noted where the Dragon Guard gemstone should be.
“6 years ago, the gemstone of the Dragon Guard was removed so I could act independently and so my thoughts could not be overheard. This allowed me to pass messages to those working on a way to destroy Morvic if the need arose,” Darhak continues. 
“When did Hunger struggle for control,” I ask.
“5 years ago. Not long after, a man working on this problem was attacked in his home, kidnapped and tortured to learn what he knew. The kidnappers were desperate to understand Hularen magic. Osric (Tarn) was recovered. A maid who was training as an arcanist (Devlin) was affected by Osric’s spells and linked to him. She helped find him. Shortly after, you arrive to train at the Porthion Temple. Dark things watched you which should not have been possible. You know things you shouldn’t, terribly dangerous things.”
“What caused Hunger to become ‘unruly?’
“A small group of people are working to destroy Morvic. The stones (Mor’Fang) below Travaghn are old and Morvic has bashed his spells against them for thousands of years. He weakened them until he broke free, but the wards and chair kept him shackled and weak. Bodin said there would be a time when I would be drawn to you and when that time came, I must take you to this room and convince you to tell me all your secrets and I would tell you ours. Bodin said I was to tell you, ‘It is time to move to the next step of the strategy.”
I am not convinced. I trust Father Bodin but Porthios told me to tell no one what I know except Bronnen. I shake my head. 
“A number of relics have been used on Morvic over the years but not even a sphere of annihilation would harm the essence. His essence is tied to the incomplete dweomer. When the stones cracked, his essence was escaping. Those escaped fragments were destroyed,” Darhawk says.
Another man comes into the room. He’s tattooed on both arms from shoulders to fingertips, in his late 40’s with shoulder-length brown hair, and an accent. Darhawk knows him and introduces us.
“This is one of my traveling companions, Var of the Solarian Circle. He creates magic through his tattoos,” Darhawk volunteers.
“This room always feels like it’s trying to eat me,” Var says. 
Var sounds brusque and irritated, but it could be the effects of this room.
“Var’s specialties include destroying other’s magic. His other specialty is containing (magic).”
Var holds out what looks like a fancy, octagonal scroll case. Darhawk takes it from Var and holds it out to me before continuing.
“Var made this container. Any magic, conduit or otherwise, fed into this tube is contained and protected. The tube feeds off the magic within to fuel its own words. The more powerful the magic, the more powerful the protection. Only Var, you, and I can touch this container. Anyone else will be obliterated. This is the only one of its kind. The empire has 7 dark shards, and the emperor has said they will be given to you when you have a place to safely store them. It won’t last forever, eventually the magic it contains will destroy the container. So, you should not put the shards in the container until you have a place to store the shards. We know the Gith’yanki have two shards and have hidden them in the Abyss,” Darhawk explains.
“The Gith’yanki took the shards – it’s a trap,” I say.
“I think you are doing things out of order,” Darhawk muses. “Gather the shards, give the signal, the prison falls, the enemy is destroyed, and the shards are cleansed. It sounds out of order.”
“The druids do not know how to cleanse the shards. It is foolish and desperate to allow them to try. The Sleeper is once again confined but powerful creatures walk freely. I don’t know who is listening. Porthios was clear in His instructions to me. There are some things, very specific things I cannot talk about to anyone save Bronnen,” I say.
Darhawk hands me the octagonal case that Var made to hold the dark shards.
“Sandlin also wants to speak to you before I take you back,” Darhawk says.
Darhawk stands up, walks over and holds out his hand. I stand up and take his hand. He transports us to Father Sandlin’s office. I am surprised by his appearance; he looks exhausted and haggard. I explain to Arch Bishop Sandlin what has transpired this week. 
Father Sandlin tells me, “If you are with the Lord Emperor and afraid of telling him something because of ears who might be listening, work into your conversation the phrase, ‘the winter lilies are blooming.’ This will let the Lord Emperor know that I know the answer, but someone listens. The phrase changes weekly and this is the phrase for this week. Next week will be, ‘the hedges need trimming.’ I will send you the phrases to use each week they change. 
We discuss the possible order of things that happened 5 years ago trying to discover what may have caused Hunger to ‘become unruly.’ 
5 years ago:
•	Olen Marwood and several other Hularens of the oldest bloodlines came to Travaghn as Knights of Porthios. Perhaps Hunger recognized so many Hularens in one place.
•	Master Osric Tarn used a Pykerian (Hularen) Mirror and transferred magic to a maid who is now Lady Devlin Douth’Rujva.
•	Ordinary citizens of Travaghn were corrupted with ancient magic and became sleeping assassins. The magic was Asha’kari magic.
•	I arrived in Travaghn to begin my trainings as a Porthion priestess.
Which of these caused Hunger to act out or was it a combination or something else we do not know about? Unable to puzzle this out, Father Sandlin has me open a very heavy and heavily warded chest. The chest reforms into a cabinet holding perhaps 1000 scrolls.
“Periwinkle,” Arch Bishop Sandlin says.
Labels appear on all the scrolls. Father Sandlin tells me to look for a scroll labeled: Tarn, Sarl, Mirror. I find the scroll among the many. I pull the scroll out for Father Sandlin.
“Do you have a scroll somewhere with the words I keep hearing Greed say? I have written them down phonetically each time but there is one word whose meaning has changed. More than that, I think the translation has more than one meaning and at least 3, but perhaps even more as I do not understand the nuances of Seulean.”
Op’aran na’theel courum sala. Op’aran na’theel thaluum nissal. 
Father, I (your son) come after / pursue (both) literally and figuratively to end (destroy) all that you are. Father, I (your son) come after / pursue (to) finish / possess what you failed (to possess / accomplish).
Op'aran - Father
Na'theel - I go after, I come after, pursue, or son.
Corrum - to end all that you are, to take away, to take back, destroy.
Sala - is this a bridge word, a possessive which when used with Na'theel means not only those words above but that the son himself is literally and figuratively coming after the father.
"Et'talama" ... which in the dream seemed to be some sort of beckoning, the people were coming to him in sacrifice. so maybe "come to me" or "bring all to me" or "give yourselves to me" or some such. I whispered it first, then the tree said it after all the people placed nooses about their own necks. This was Hunger’s voice.
"Na et'tun urcor vi'al" the voice was clear; the words were clear but trying to capture them based on phonetics and rhythm are tricky. After the sacrifices were made, after most of the wisps of smoke were absorbed by the Heart Tree / Mother Tree (but a few were not), the tree had a powerful voice, not the same voice I heard earlier. This was not spoken by Greed.
Arch Bishop says that there is a theory that Lady Devlin Douth’Rujva might be or was a vessel for Greed. She, along with her husband, and their adventure party went into the Homewood and made it back out again. She says they say the Sleeper while they were in the Great Wood. Not only did they see him, but he appeared in some sort of physical form and spoke to them. He said they / she has something he wanted and now the empire wonders if he used her as a means to leave the wood, at least, a small piece of him. Or perhaps he found a way to hear what she heard and see what she saw. They are not certain this is the case. 
Arch Bishop Sandlin also speaks of Chosen Colin.
“Colin’s messages from Porthios are scattered and vague like yours. He is hunting a key now. Without any training, Colin started healing people at the age of 11. The people of Widebend did not know if it was a miracle or if he was a demon. His mother kept him locked in a room for months on end for his safety. His brother released him after listening to Colin’s pleas, that he was late, and people were dying because he was not where he should be. Colin’s last message was that he feared he would fail, and the key would be killed by agents of Greed,” Father Sandlin relays.
“5 Chosen remain, Cara. There were 11, not including the girl Jeggred found before you (though her status as Chosen was unconfirmed by the church). 6 have died to undead or corrupted beasts or nightmares given form. The most recent Chosen died last night, a girl of 19. You were in class together. Like you, she was to tell no one, but her identity was her downfall. They cannot resurrect her – there is no body.”
Now I understand why Father Sandlin looks so tired and sad, he’s silently grieving. In all the centuries since Porthios ascended, there’s only ever been one Chosen at a time during times of great trouble. Now, there are, were 11 of us – all children. Arch Bishop Sandlin has tried to watch over us all but 6 have died. We are hunted and he is haunted. 
Father Sandlin has me get a pouch from his desk. Inside the pouch is another smaller pouch which he gives to me. Father Sandlin pours a number of vampire fangs into the palm of his hand from the first pouch. They are grey and very old from old, powerful vampires. 
“These were delivered by a vampire to the Douth’Ruja estate. The vampire is said to have black hair and a strange accent and despite the wards, he walked through the bars of the Douth’Rujva Keep. About a week and a half ago, a young man from a farm in the Vale walked into the church here. He prayed, then asked to deliver a package to me to give to one of the Chosen who was in another place. When the boy was questioned, he could not remember who gave him the teeth or the brooch, worth 5000 gold, after. What is in the smaller pouch is meant for you.”
I open the smaller pouch and pour out more vampire teeth. The teeth are inscribed with tiny words: out, danger, quick, time, more, running. I arrange the teeth in my palm until they read: running out of time, move quick, danger.
Father Sandlin says one other interesting statement, “A lich in the Great Eastern offers aid.”
I quote Porthios, “Not all our allies look as we expect.”
“Cara, Jurva Thierkiernon told the empire to ‘remove their agents (you and your father) from Woodhome and all would be forgiven, or they would remove you both at a cost to the empire: doubling taxation on all goods in and out of Woodhome over the next year. An imperial loss of 30 million gold. She also threatened to stop sending white bellacum (used in healing potions) which only grows in Woodhome. The Lord Emperor’s response was very dark, ‘Handle this.’ 
“He has turned his eyes back home and brought back most of the Imperial soldiers fighting in Arboria. He intends to use them if Woodhome tries to fight the empire. The Lord Emperor’s of a mind that if a handful of dissidents cannot be swayed, they must simply be removed.”
“Father, I am not queen of Woodhome yet. I am doing what I can, all I can but I will have more power when I am crowned queen. I am learning as fast as I can but most of them see me a child, an outsider,” I try to explain.
“This is a test of fealty, Cara.”
I cannot explain or argue my way out of this. It is unreasonable to expect me to control an entire people and the Lord Emperor, the High Prince, the Arch Bishop, they all know it. This started long before I was born.
“We need to find Jeggred, Father, he has something I need. We found it in Kiern’Kirak. It looks like a walking stick and I know he took it with him when he returned East. I know he put it with other items and relics, hidden in the cave in the Wild Wood but it’s crucial it be returned to me. I have tried Sendings to him but he doesn’t respond,” I say. “Do you have a way to reach him, to find him, to ask him to return the walking stick?”
“I will attempt to reach out to Jeggred but he went missing after the war with the orc in the North-east. We cannot find him by any means. He may have gone into the Wild Wood back to Father Nero’s hidden cave.”
“Thank you, father.” I do not mention that Jeggred may be using Ethragen magic to hide himself from anyone who is not Hularen or Ethragen.
Darhawk appears to take me back. We quickly arrive back where I was taken from. By the trees, I see Gulrian and Bronnen. I show up alone and walk over to the trees. Gulrian is beyond angry that the empire snatched me away. As soon as he sees me, he awakens the trees here in El’Lendrun then immediately creates a tree-portal back to the Circle of Nine.
We step. I look at the Arch Druids who remain. I don’t know what to say to those who remain. I know what it is not to feel the Mother, or barely feel Her, but they have felt Her most of their lives and now… She is gone from them and they from Her. Only Arch Druid Johlon Wiervarn and Alveron Thierkiernon are here, and they are staring into the swirling blue magic of the Mother contained within the well. They look grey, ashen, and hollow to my eyes. Alveron sees me and just stares. Johlon walks down the steps of the Circle of 9, squats down, and picks up a handful of dirt. He breathes it in deeply before standing and walking over to me, the dirt still in his fist. With his free hand, he takes one of mine and holds it palm up before gently putting the soil in my hand.
“Learn this soil well,” his voice is soft. He turns and as he walks away, he whispers, “this is where I will bury the pieces of you.”
Emric hears him and says quietly, “give him time, he didn’t make the declaration (to kill you) out loud.”
Alveron is angry, repulsed and in shock. He starts to walk into the font of the Mother and I stop him, yelling out no. He turns his gaze back to me before walking silently into the trees.
“I’m sorry,” I whisper, the words catching in my throat as tears threaten.
“Stop apologizing, Cara. Console the druids, they are your people but do not change the punishment. Stick to it. Admist you do not know what you are doing and that Mor’Renna has control. That control belongs to you. Her words have weight and she would be fit to judge the druids but she is no longer Kiera. She has not been the Kiera in a very long time and today, she made you Kiera today,” Emric says.
“We need to tell our families what has happened,” I say, “and discuss Jurva.”
Bronnen nods.
“Jurva is a blackbird squawking and making noise. The empire and the rest of the world will soon realize that is all she is. Cara and I need to talk alone. Cara is safe with me. Keep a hound’s pace away,” Mor’Renna says. “A hound’s pace is 1500 feet, Cara, the Gorhund cannot hear beyond that distance and neither can anyone else.”
I watch as everyone moves some distance away.
“Step 1 is done. I told you this would be difficult. We must hope they (the Arch Druids) grieve and return. Be war those who come too soon and grieve those who do not return – replace them. You must take Thurgen’s fascar to Ravan’ar. You must find Orlim. There was once a great Eirinese tower there called Ravan’ar (Raven). You need to make the pilgrimage to Ravan’ar, anyway.”
I tell her the empire is waiting to give me the shards they have found but I need a place to store them, a safe place.
“Do not bring them here. Take them to the Deepen Well in Kiern’Kirak. Mate Bronnen, then he can go with you. Return to Kiern’Kirak, find the Deepen Well. In the South and East of the palace there is a pile of rubble and there you will find the remains of another Eirenese tower. South of that stone rubble lies the Deepen Well where Asha’kari magics are stored until they are ready to be destroyed. The Bones of Therassius are in the Deepen Well. 
“Through your blood, you are resistant to the corruption in the shards. Retrieve the shards and go directly to the Deepen Well, then go to Ravan’ar. Return with Thurgen’s fascar and assert control over the people. Teach them the war forms. Raise the broods, hoards, and herds. Only a Varkier can channel all of the Ethragen and only a Varkier channeling the Ethragen can harm the Asha’kari from a distance. Do not close the distance with Asha’kari. If they see you, they can kill you with a thought. Kill them before they make their armies. The shards are made to corrupt the innovar. Get the shards from them before they are corrupted,” Mor’Renna advises.
Lysara can feel my doubt and when Mor’Renna finishes speaking, Lysara shows me a memory of the war with the Asha’kari against the Hularens. Lysara’s beloved is there. The war is terrifying and awe-striking and horrifying. What I see, what was, is impressive, breath-stealing, and heart-stopping in its intensity and power. She alleviates my doubts.
“You spent a year with her in her cave. She taught you many things,” Lysara whispers.
I walk back toward Bronnen and Emric as Mor’Renna walks over to the Circle of Nine. She begins chanting and naming each of the stones: Fang, Ordesh, … I remember the names; she taught them to me. I know, I remember, she is closing the font of the Mother to protect it and hide it from the world. 
Bronnen, Emric, Gulrian, and I walk back to where our families wait. 4 hours have passed since we left them. Emric explains what I did with Mor’Renna’s help. Mama is shocked, Eladia is visibly upset and angry, but everyone else absorbs the news and moves ahead.

**Summary of the Journal Entry:**
Cara begins her day preparing for a significant encounter with the Arch Druids at the Circle of Nine. With her memory gradually unlocking, she recalls ancient knowledge and a prior decision to wield the Mother’s power against those who have failed her people. In the Circle, Cara, guided by Mor’Renna, severs the Arch Druids’ connection to the Mother. She reestablishes this bond only with those willing to serve her vision, marking a new path for the Hularen people under her rule as Kiera. Afterward, Cara retrieves ancient Varkier relics from Thurgen’s resting place, gains crucial wisdom from his spirit, and begins to face the consequences of her leadership. She receives additional guidance on securing the corrupted shards and contemplates the gravity of her role.

---

**Key Items:**
- **Blue Over-Robe**: Worn for formal respect, marking Cara’s Varkier heritage.
- **Varkier and Uhlarn Face Marks**: Applied by Mor’Sovra and Eladia as symbols of Cara’s dual lineage.
- **Cartouche Markings and Mor’Fang Stones**: Sacred stones in the Circle of Nine with ritual power.
- **Thurgen’s Silver Box and Relics**: Contains his bones, a headdress, and a torc—all symbolic of his lineage.
- **Var’s Octagonal Case**: A unique container for safely holding dark shards.
- **Vampire Teeth Inscription**: Reads a warning message: “running out of time, move quick, danger.”
- **Torc from Mor’Renna**: A personal relic handed down, symbolizing Cara’s place as the new Kiera.

---

**Important Locations:**
- **Circle of Nine**: An ancient sacred site where Cara confronts the Arch Druids.
- **El’Lendrun**: The ruin through which Cara accesses other sacred places.
- **Nuan’legot**: Known as the “Valley of Trees” and an ancient ritual site where Cara retrieves Varkier relics.
- **Ravan’ar (Raven)**: An Eirinese tower significant to Cara’s future pilgrimage.
- **Deepen Well in Kiern’Kirak**: A secure location to store and eventually cleanse dark shards.
- **Black Basalt Room**: A hidden imperial room where Cara meets Darhawk Leighon and Var for secret discussions.

---

**Key Characters:**
- **Cara (Carathul Varkier)**: Embraces her role as the Kiera, wielding the Mother’s power and enforcing justice on the Arch Druids.
- **Bronnen**: Cara’s bond-mate, questioning her sudden acceptance of leadership but ultimately supporting her.
- **Mor’Renna**: Cara’s mentor and the force guiding her to reclaim the Mother’s power and enforce Hularen strength.
- **Arch Druid Emric**: One of the few druids Cara reconnects to the Mother due to his loyalty.
- **Gulrian**: Another Arch Druid reconnected to the Mother after accepting Cara’s leadership.
- **Thurgen Varkier**: Cara’s ancestor, whose spirit shares critical knowledge of ancient weapons and his legacy.
- **Darhawk Leighon**: A Dragon Guard with secret imperial duties, allied with Father Sandlin to aid Cara.
- **Arch Bishop Sandlin**: Provides Cara with vital information and secure means of communication within the empire.

---

**Objectives and Goals:**
- **Complete the Ascension as Kiera**: A role Cara steps into to fulfill her duty to the Mother and her people.
- **Retrieve and Store Dark Shards**: Cara must gather these dangerous relics, safely storing them in the Deepen Well.
- **Unite and Strengthen the Hularen People**: Cara’s leadership focuses on restoring Hularen power and rallying them for impending conflicts.
- **Make a Pilgrimage to Ravan’ar**: This journey holds further spiritual and tactical significance.
- **Safeguard the People and the Mother**: Cara is tasked with reclaiming ancient power, preventing corruption, and balancing alliances.

---

**Notable Events:**
- **Confrontation at the Circle of Nine**: Cara’s memory returns as she enacts an ancient glyph to sever the Arch Druids from the Mother.
- **Retrieval of Varkier Relics at Nuan’legot**: Cara finds Thurgen’s remains and sacred items, which further solidify her connection to her heritage.
- **Meeting with Darhawk and Var**: She gains insight into imperial strategies against Morvic and receives the unique container for dark shards.
- **Reconnection and Forgiveness of Druids**: Cara offers a path of redemption to certain druids who align with her vision.
- **Counsel with Thurgen’s Spirit**: He reveals crucial information about ancient Hularen weapons and advice for Cara’s leadership.
- **Imperial Warnings and Father Sandlin’s Guidance**: She learns about empire expectations, threats from dissidents, and methods of discreet communication.
- **Debrief with Family**: Cara updates her family on recent events, facing varied reactions as they grapple with her transformative role.

Cara's commitment to the Mother and her people deepens as she wields powers that solidify her role and alliances but risk alienating her allies.

Read the following journal entry for my D&D character, Cara. Create a list of important items, locations, names, objectives and events. Each list should be a separate category. Include a summary of the of the journal entry: 14th of Solik, 2324 IC   14th of Solik, 2324 IC. Ilyrian

Wake and realize I still have the tiny scale in my hand. It is made from the heartwood of a living oak, an Awoken Tree. The wood is reddish-brown with streaks grey. Only the druids hand them out to heroes as the wood is very rare. I show Bronnen the tiny scale and he thinks I should hide it as it came from Porthios and not the Mother. I put is on the shelf with other items I treasure.
Dress, pray, and go downstairs to eat breakfast with Bronnen. Ohjan wishes to speak to him in an hour about me and the Varkier bloodline. Ohjan is with other men who are in his study: Elder Thyurdon Varmarkuhn, and the Dyurnok of Lanneroc (Mor’Sovra’s father), the Elder and the Dyurnok of Seastone, and two others. After breakfast, while Bronnen talks with his father and the other men, I go speak with Roland.
In the house in which Roland is staying and working, all the books, scrolls, papers, and quills have been put away. He is sitting in a chair in the middle of the room staring at nothing. 
Roland tells me, “We already lost the coming war during the Neighbor’s War. The fuel source of the dewormer magic is the darkness – the Dark Mother who grows and feeds on death, to grow the darkness and strengthen the corruption. The more people dies, the more it grows. A fleet of Kothians will soon arrive and begin their slaughter. I think the Asha’kari will use the death to fuel the magic (of the Dark Mother and enable Her) to escape the prison. The dewormer is self-perpetuating and I think the relic you brought back could be used as a lever 0r a handle to a lever, perhaps.”
Roland’s explanation is long and complicated, and I must ask him to repeat things a number of times and simplify other concepts for me. He speaks so quickly, his mind already fixed on distant points, I cannot always keep up or make the leaps he believes should be intuitive.  
“The keys. I need to do some research in Travaghn and then find a far away plane to hide all the keys on,” Roland says as he works through the problem while I sit with him.
“The empire will not allow you into Travaghn, Roland. The empire is just waiting for you to leave these woods, watching for you to leave. They are waiting for the moment you leave the safety of Woodhome to capture you, imprison you, and eventually hold you accountable for what you did in the palace. Several people have warned me of this.”
Roland’s small smile is not quite a sneer, “They can try.”
He gives me a list of books he would like me to request from the empire. I tell him I will make the request, but I cannot promise it will be approved. He may have to find another way to get what he needs. I leave Roland’s and go to speak with Silas and Reynar. I show Reynar a sketch of the skull I saw and touched in Mor’Renna’s (Mawdra’s) cave. The markings on the skull are Toltemic and ancient Hularen. They are similar to Thurgen’s var’fascar. Reynar says the Toltemic are the marks of a powerful Ethragen, or were, as the marks are ancient. The skull is, or was, Thurgen’s.
I return to the Gorhund home where I am called into Ohjan’s study. I see the group of men that Ohjan and Bronnen were speaking with. One of the men stands when I walk in. He has bones in his eyebrows, 2 bone rings in his lips, a shock of braided white hair woven with bones and the tattoos on his face are claws running from his forehead to chin. He also has the Varmarkuhn clan tattoo. He has scarification lines down his arms as well as tattooed symbols. He looks at me up and down, assessing me.
“You I am Delaner of the Varmarkuhn. We are cousins and until your arrival, I was the strongest of the Varkier line, though I have only a thimble-full of blood. You are small, little Varkier.”
The other men in the room stay quiet, watching my reaction. Waiting to see what I will say or do. I remain silent, waiting to hear more.
“I come to bear witness to the awakening of the old kings. I have come to see it with my own eyes. I formally ask to stand before you with open hands, Carathul of the Varkier line.”
He holds out his arms with his hands held face up. On his palms are symbols that look like the glyphs I saw on the Dragon’s Foot. Ohjan tells me that Delaner is a druid and a warrior, and Keeper of the Lost.
Delaner switches to Old Hularen, “I offer you greetings, blood of my blood – if in fact you are.”
Ohjan translates the words for me so I can understand Delaner’s words. As he inspects me, I inspect him. He appears to be in his 40s or 50s and is very well muscled. He looks strong and fierce, tanned and leathered, and smells of the outside. His pupils are not round but neither are they cat-shaped, either.
“She smells of the lost lands,” he declares. “It is disturbing that she smells so strongly of the lost lands, and yes, the Mother is here, too,” Delaner announces to all here.
“Cara has lived in the lost lands for many years,” Bronnen explains.
“If I kill you, girl, and bathe in your blood, I once again will be the strongest Varkier blood among our people. What do you say to that?”
“You will not draw blood in Mor’Sovra’s home,” I say, holding still, sure in my understanding of the consequences of spilling blood in another’s home.
Delaner gives a small chuff of a laugh. He takes one of my hands in his and squeezes hard. His face screws up and his eyes change.
“I can feel the Varkier blood in her. It burns, the blood is strong. I do not feel rage,” Delaner declares to all in Ohjan’s study, scowling at that last revelation.
Delaner lets go of my hand and sits down.
“Thank you, Cara, we still have matters to discuss,” Ohjan tells me, motioning to the door.
I nod at him and leave his study, closing the door behind me. When I walk out into the hall, I find Mor’Sovra waiting, keeping guard. She looks protective and angry, someone threated to spill blood in her home – to spill the blood of a Varkier. 
“Did he harm you?”
“No. It was an empty threat. I am well.”
“Go, eat.”
I walk into the kitchen, put food on a plate, and walk outside to eat. There are 30 men out here standing or sitting around the fire. Jorrel is out here but I do not recognize the others. They all look like warriors or wardens in their 30s. I walk over to the family table and sit down to eat a late lunch. Jorrel sits with me and we talk.
“I can move the Keys to Oakdelve if you are worried about their safety. We can bring some of the Gorhund wardens with us, too, if that is more comfortable for you, Cara,” Jorrel offers. 
“Thank you, Jorrel, but they will be safe here. We will stay here in Ilyrian. I know the people here, I know the Gorhund, and they know me.”
We talk until I finish eating. After, I clean my plate and put everything away, then I go find Mama and Papa. They are eating in the town market square after doing some shopping. We talk together and it’s nice, our conversation is pleasant and light. Mama and Papa are relieved that we are all here. As we sit, a screeching arrow signals from the East. Men start running the direction of the arrow. 3 more screechers come from the East. Papa starts to rise from the table.
“Best we stay out of the way, Papa.”
We watch as wardens and warriors run East and Papa looks ready to fight, every muscle tense and ready to spring. Druids fly overhead. 6 birds land nearby and transform into wolves. Eladia sees us, shifts into her natural form and signals to us to “stay.” I respond using the warden signals Bronnen has been teaching me, “understand.” Mama, Papa, Eladia, and I all wait and watch as minutes pass. A warden comes over and makes lots of gestures to quickly for me to understand. An older warden comes over and leads us South to see whatever caused the alarms.
Jehan joins Eladia and the warden as they escort Mama, Papa, and I. We climb some rocks and squat down among the shrubs and trees, watching the forest for anything that moves. 
“We are watching for something older than the Hularens,” Eladia whispers. “It traveled between the mountains and ocean.”
We wait in silence and watch for something ancient to show itself. Others join us as we watch the forest and wait and many of them are children. They look excited, eagerly waiting to catch a glimpse of something special. We hear something impossibly large moving through the forest. What we see is huge: 15-feet in diameter and so very long. The creature is wingless and seems to be made of trees and vines. It moves like a serpent but not. It’s terribly quiet. It’s 80-yards long and must weigh 30-tons.
“This is a forest wyrm, a Lenorn. It has not been seen in a very long time,” Jehan whispers. 
I can hear the awe in his voice. The forest wyrm stops and we watch as its body delicately curls around itself. It looks around at all the people who have gathered to watch the wonder that is the Lenorn. To my eyes, it looks like a tree with people and children in it – tiny fey creatures. It looks my direction, directly at me, and seems to speak before continuing on its way. As we watch, it takes 10-minutes for all of the forest wyrm to pass through. I can feel the power of this creature and it almost glows with life.
We are all in wonder and awe and once it is gone, we all crawl down to look at the path it took. Children and adults alike search for pieces of the Lenorn. Eladia finds 3 small branches that the Lenorn shed and gives me one.
“The forest wyrm gave a blessing, Cara. It said, ‘mel-gor-norm,’ which means, go in peace. It came down from the Spine of the World and it will go South to the ocean to gorge on sea creatures, then sleep in a nest for 2 or 3 years. Lenorn hate dragons and stories say the Hularens grew them to fight during the war with dragons thousands of years ago,” Eladia says.
We all walk together back to the market. 
“Bronnen will be heart-broken he missed it,” Eladia says.
I hear Mama talking to Papa about becoming a druidess and Papa smiles. The square is filled with people who are excited and drinking, laughing and talking. It turns into a celebration. I introduce Mama & Papa to Andolina & her little boy, Malin, as well as Silas, Reynar, and some of the other people in Ilyrian who I have come to know. 
We are still at the square when dusk falls. Mor’Sovra, Ohjan, and Bronnen come join Mama, Papa, Eladia, Jehan, me and a few others. Ohjan locks eyes with me but says nothing. Some of the Elders and Dyurnoks that he met with earlier today are also here. Bronnen comes to stand next to me and I tell him what we saw. We listen to music and enjoy the fires in the square.
Papa walks over to Bronnen and I and quietly asks, “Why are we being flanked?”
I look around and see 4 Gorhund wardens. One has the Gorhund fang (Gorak Gorhund) which means he is a life-long warden. Another of the wardens wears a bone necklace made of grey fingerbones (orc). 
Bronne explains, “12 men from Thornwall came here 2 hours ago. The Thierkiernon have summoned Cara to Thornwall.”
“Why,” Papa asks.
“They say I broke the treaty by bringing outsiders here, even with the Gorhund’s and Emric’s permission. It is thought they somehow know I am Varkier blood so the Gorhund are ready for a fight. Jurva wants me and the other outsiders in Thornwall.”
Bronnen continues, “Jurva sent her brother, and he made a threat to remove Cara and you, her parents, and the innovar keys. My father said no and turned them out. Now, the Bloodhounds, Captains of the Wardens protect you in case the Thierkiernon return and try to force you to Thornwall.”
Eladia walks over, having overheard the conversation.
“That explains why Gorack, the one with the fangs, is guarding you,” Eladia offers.
We stay in the market square for another hour enjoying the impromptu celebration before walking back to the house through throngs of people. The Bloodhounds shadow us at a distance. When we get to the house, Bronnen signals to the Gloodhounds and they leave to join the Gorhund wardens who are ringing the house. 
Mama & Papa go to bed while Bronnen and I stay up and talk some more. During our discussion, we decide we don’t want to be Kier and Kiera, we don’t want to rule. We discuss all the reasons we don’t want to rule. We are not trained, we are not prepared, we have other duties, we might do more harm than good, we want to travel, we want to see other places… and many other reasons. Before we go to bed, I check the scroll cases first and read the messages. 
Both messages are from Father Sandlin and reads, “Cara, hope all is well. The Lord Emperor wishes an update on your progress. Don’t tarry in responding. Porthios be with you.”
The second reads, “Conflict in East. 11 Imperial Agents died. 34 cultists (Mor’Kar) killed. Leader had a scroll with your name and likeness along with a bag of rubies believed as payment. Be watchful.”
I burn both messages and get ready for bed. I see something tiny move in the rafters overhead. I remember not to look directly up and crawl into bed, trying to see the little fey from the corner of my eye. There are 5 tiny shapes, miniscule blue fairies with white hair, dragonfly wings, and 4 arms. They are armed with bows and arrows and impossibly small scythes.
“Breggis,” Bronnen whispers, “they don’t ever come into houses.”
I slip back out of bed and pad softly across the hall to Eladia’s room to ask her about them. 
“Breggis are drawn to conflict. Their arrows are poisonous, and their scythes create wounds that do not heal. They can cast magics that cause blindness, fear, and illusions. They are dangerous little sprites that live in the deep, old places but they hunt evil fairies,” Eladia explains. 
Shea walks with me back into Bronnen’s room. We both walk slowly, and Eladia speaks softly in Sylvan to them. They answer her but all I understand is “Gorhund.” A heartbeat later, a cloud of black smoke and fire boils up from the floor, reaching a height of 10-feet. Lightning and fire weave through the blackness and out of it steps a creature. The creature is 9-feet tall with blue skin, 2 long horns, and 2 short horns. It has 4 eyes, 2 blue and 2 green, a nose with 4 nostrils, and a mouth full of razor-sharp teeth. It has long fingers and glowing marking on its 4 arms, chest, neck, legs and feet. The markings glow blue, green and red. It wears only a loincloth of purple and has huge wings, one wingtip passes through the wall of the room. Long white hair flows down the creature’s back. It looks like the tiny Breggis but it is also different.
When it speaks to Eladia in Sylvan, its voice is deep. Eladia translates for me.
“They came from the Deepwood. They sensed a calling to be here. They will not say by whom. Only they will be in this place. If they are offered no harm, they will give none but if we offer harm, they will give harm; however, you will not die, for they have come here to make sure you do not die. Such is the pact they made.”
Eladia speaks to the creature again and then translates a second time.
“They do not like that we are not speaking in Sylvan and that I must translate their words to you, Cara.”
I look up and see 16 pairs of blue eyes, 8 tiny warriors staring down. The large creature disappears.
“Who can make a pact with Breggis?” I ask.
“I don’t know, but they are here to keep us alive,” Bronnen says.
“The large creature is a Theormgarr – a god of the fairy Breggis – or rather, an illusion of him,” Eladia offers. 
Eladia goes back to her room and Bronnen and I go to bed. 
“Something big is happening,” I whisper, “something big is coming. The Bloodhounds guard, Mor’Renna is here, a Lenorn passed by this afternoon, now a pack of Breggis tell us they made a pact to keep up alive.”
I fall asleep listening to Bronnen’s heartbeat.

Dream 86: With All Choices Comes a Cost
I wake up to a rainstorm and thunder. I am in the bed I share with Bronnen. It is night. I look around and do not see tiny eyes staring down at me from the rafters. There is no one in the room who shouldn’t be there. Bronnen is still asleep and this is how I know for certain I am dreaming. I get up and walk over to the balcony doors. I open the doors and step out into the pouring rain. Lightning flashes, illuminating the houses and trees in Ilyrian. Huge blue-black clouds filled with lightning blanket the sky blocking out the stars and moons. Lightning fills the sky again and I see the Waif looking up at me.
I walk back into the room, closing the balcony doors behind me, leaving wet footprints in my wake. I go downstairs to Him and back out into the storm. It’s cold and the rain makes it even colder. I can see my breath. I wait for a flash of lightning to see Him again and walk His direction. He’s soaked and the ground is soddened. Lightning strikes and the Warrior has replaced the Waif. He raises his hand, and lightning strikes the wood in the fire bowl. It burns blue and I can see. The Warrior has a gash running from forehead to ear and blood mixes with the rain. He looks fierce.
“Time of change is coming. You will have to choose. Are you ready?” He asks.
“I am ready,” I answer but a howling wind snatches my words away.
I yell above the wind, “I am ready!”
“Do not make us regret Our faith. Here, above all things, beyond all trials, are you now led to power. The choices you have made light the paths open to you. Only one leads to a key and that key to a cage.”
He holds out a bloodied hand. In His palm is a black key and I reach for it.
“With all choices comes a cost,” He warns.
“We need this,” I respond as I take the black key from His hand.
“Lament not your burdens but take refuge in your purpose. Bleed where blood is called for, kill without question when the purpose is true. An army to some is many arms but to the wise, an army is one heart filled with rage, bent on purpose. Craft inside yourself that skill or lend your voice to another who can. Do less than this then all that comes before is naught. Fail your duty to the woe of many. Do you understand your calling? We have chosen you, child: messenger, sword, and light. Both burden and purpose are yours.”
Thunder cracks overhead and lighting flashes across the sky. The Warrior is gone. I turn around and I almost walk into a black-robed figure. I look up at a delicate chin and pursed lips. The Woman looks down at me.  
“You must be what is needed, or you must be what is desired but the choice made demands the choice that is avoided be cast away. Doubt is a smell; it lingers in the eyes; it is a tone in the words spoken. Suffer this to the failure of all. If you stand, child, stand firm and know this: I stand with you.”
Lightning flashes and the Woman is gone. I walk back to the house and into the kitchen trying not to trail water through the house. I see something waiting in the shadows of a corner.
“Betrayal, go armed,” the Waif warns. “Everybody wants to survive, Cara. Everyone will kill to survive. One winter (3-5 years) is not a long time to change the world. Keep walking, I’m not here.”
His voice fades and I walk on through the house to the stairs. I hear a faint whisper follow me up the stairs.
“Not all good are friends and not all evil are enemies.”
I am not sure if the voice belongs to the Waif or someone else as the whisper is so faint. I walk back to Bronnen’s room. Bronnen is up and facing into the room, indicating he is not waiting for me. 
He speaks, “I understand, if it must be.”
He speaks to an empty room or, if someone is there, I cannot see who. I watch as he concludes his conversation and climbs back into bed. He doesn’t seem to see me so he must also be dreaming. I crawl into bed, curl in next to him, and go back to sleep.

**Summary of the Journal Entry:**
Cara spends the day preparing for an increasingly complex future. After discovering a rare item and speaking with allies like Roland and Reynar, Cara learns of ancient threats from the Asha’kari and the nature of the dark forces at play. She witnesses the appearance of a Lenorn (forest wyrm), a powerful sign of nature’s protection, and a group of Breggis sprites, who make a pact to guard her. Despite the emerging symbols of power and protection, Cara faces internal tension regarding her role as Kiera, expressing her reluctance to rule. That night, she dreams of the Waif, the Warrior, and the Woman, receiving a dark warning that change is imminent and that she must make choices aligned with her purpose, prepared to sacrifice or act ruthlessly when necessary.

---

**Key Items:**
- **Heartwood Scale**: A rare scale of heartwood from an Awoken Tree, given only to heroes by druids.
- **Black Key from Dream**: Given by the Warrior in her dream, symbolizing access to hidden power or a “cage.”
- **Thurgen’s Skull Sketch**: Marked with Toltemic and ancient Hularen symbols, related to powerful Ethragen.

---

**Important Locations:**
- **Ohjan’s Study**: Where Cara meets influential Hularen elders, including her cousin Delaner.
- **Forest near Ilyrian**: Where Cara and others witness the passage of the Lenorn, a symbolic creature of nature’s power.
- **Market Square in Ilyrian**: Hosts a celebration sparked by the Lenorn’s appearance, showing unity among the people.
- **Gorhund Home**: A place of relative safety, but now under heavy protection due to threats from Thornwall.
- **Dreamscape**: Cara meets the Waif, the Warrior, and the Woman here, gaining crucial guidance.

---

**Key Characters:**
- **Cara (Carathul Varkier)**: Balances her identity as a leader and warrior with her reluctance to rule.
- **Bronnen**: Cara’s bond-mate, who shares her doubts about ruling and stands by her side.
- **Ohjan**: Cara’s guardian and strategist, preparing her to meet her responsibilities.
- **Delaner of the Varmarkuhn**: Cara’s distant cousin, tests her strength and purity as a Varkier.
- **Roland**: Scholar, advising Cara on the nature of the Dark Mother and the impending war.
- **Eladia**: Helps Cara navigate both familial and mystical responsibilities, translating Breggis’ messages.
- **The Waif, Warrior, and Woman**: Divine figures in Cara’s dream, offering guidance and forewarning her of sacrifices ahead.

---

**Objectives and Goals:**
- **Prepare for Imminent Threats**: Cara learns of the Asha’kari’s dark plan to fuel magic through death, indicating that war is close.
- **Preserve the Integrity of the Varkier Line**: Cara must assert her lineage while navigating Thornwall’s challenges to her authority.
- **Avoid Direct Conflict with the Thierkiernon**: Though summoned to Thornwall, Cara intends to remain in Ilyrian under Gorhund protection.
- **Secure Important Relics and Keys**: Roland and others emphasize the need to safeguard mystical items that may control or contain dark forces.
- **Internal Conflict over Leadership**: Cara and Bronnen affirm they do not want to rule as Kier and Kiera but struggle with their inevitable duty.
- **Fulfill Divine Purpose**: The Warrior and Woman’s guidance reminds Cara to fulfill her calling, despite her personal reluctance.

---

**Notable Events:**
- **Meeting with Delaner**: He challenges Cara’s strength as a Varkier, marking her acceptance by the Varmarkuhn as a leader.
- **Lenorn’s Appearance**: A forest wyrm’s passage signals nature’s blessing and unifies the people in celebration.
- **Summoning from Thornwall**: Jurva’s summons indicates rising political tension; Thornwall wants Cara and her allies under its control.
- **Visit from Breggis Sprites**: Dangerous sprites pledge to protect Cara, revealing the mystical forces aligning to guard her.
- **Message from Arch Bishop Sandlin**: Warns Cara of cultist threats and the empire’s heightened interest in her progress.
- **Dream Encounter**: Cara meets the Waif, Warrior, and Woman, receiving a black key and an ominous warning about the sacrifices her path requires.

Cara continues to walk a path of personal transformation, aware that her choices will have powerful consequences for herself and the Hularen people.

**Summary of the Journal Entry:**
Cara spends the day encountering influential figures, relics, and creatures, all pointing to a looming, large-scale conflict. After discovering a sacred scale and speaking with Roland about ancient threats and strategies, she meets her formidable cousin Delaner, who challenges her Varkier heritage. The appearance of an ancient forest wyrm, the Lenorn, brings a powerful blessing, while Cara’s encounter with Breggis sprites and a vision of the Theormgarr heightens her awareness of impending danger. Her dream offers messages from divine figures, foretelling critical choices and sacrifices. Amid these revelations, Cara faces her role in coming struggles, encouraged by her celestial allies to fulfill her purpose with strength and resolve.
