Read the following journal entry for my D&D character, Cara. Create a list of important items, locations, names, objectives and events. Each list should be a separate category. Include a summary of the of the journal entry: 13th of Solik, 2324 IC   13th of Solik, 2324 IC. Ilyrian

I wake up before sunrise. I feel a strange sense of excitement. I pull on a robe and step out into the balcony. I feel anticipation in the air. We are waiting for something. I see the light of the sun blaze over the trees. This! This is what we were waiting for: the warmth and glow of the sun. I shiver with pleasure. The trees – we were waiting for the sun!
I dress, pray, and walk downstairs. Eladia and Jehan are in the living room with two of their younger brothers and sisters. They are playing a game called bishashash. I watch them play while Eladia braids my hair, and we talk. When she is done with my hair, I practice braiding hers. I tell her something I remember and when I am done braiding her hair, she and I walk quickly to Emric’s so I can tell him of Mawdra and the Mother speaking. 
Eladia says, “It is a very big deal that the Mother spoke even one word to you, Cara.”
Emric’s place feels powerful and steeped in the Mother. Eladia and I stop at the edge, and she calls for Emric. There is no answer. A large raven calls from the trees.
 “Grosarr, we need to speak to Emric, please,” Eladia addresses the raven.
Grosarr the raven groks and flies off to find Emric.
“Tell Emric the Mother spoke. Tell him what you saw and what She said, “embrace both sides of your blood.”
When Emric arrives, he tells us, “Thurgen Varkier gave up 2 of his progenies to defeat Hunger. This is a truth that cannot be told.”
Eladia disagrees citing that I am Varkier and as Varkier, such a truth is mine to decide what to do with. 
Emric responds, “It is not your truth to keep, it is your truth to tell. Tell Ohjan and Sovra, they will guide you. Do not speak of this to your mother or father as they are still outsiders.”
“Mawdra was also there when the Mother spoke to me. Mor’Renna does not leave her cave, so this speaks of great need. Renna told me that the Varkier, the Thierkiernon, and the Gorhund led the attack against Hunger.”
Emric does not respond to this. Instead, he tells me, “Thurgen Varkier was the last sitting Hularen Kier and that the Varkier line was thought to be lost at the end of the Great War. The vision you had, the markings you saw, those are the markings of a royal womb. You are Thurgen’s direct descendent. If your birthfather is found, he would have claim to the throne but you and your mother have a stronger claim to rule than the Thierkiernon. Kiern’Kirak was one of the homes of the Varkier and the last place Thurgen’s bones were thought to be laid. 
“The spotted and striped cat that you saw on Kiern’Kirak is called a Kier’marr (King Killer). They are resistant to most magics, masters of hiding, their fur is puncture resistant, their bite can puncture steel, and they are almost impossible to kill. The Varkier tamed and trained the Kier’marr for war,” Emric says.
Emric says he will speak with Ohjan and Mor’Sovra this evening. 
“Come to me tomorrow, Cara,” Emric instructs.
Eladia and I walk back to the house. Bronnen and Papa are out hunting in the forest around Ilyrian. Eladia takes Mama out to explore Ilyrian while I speak with Ohjan and Mor’Sovra in Ohjan’s study.
As I tell them what the Mother said in Mawdra’s presence and what I remember, and what Emric said, I ask, “Am I strong in the Varkier blood? How would we even know? I was all Uhlarn tree form after the Bonding Ceremony to the Mother.”
Ohjan and Mor’Sovra have a conversation I don’t understand, and they do not explain.
Ohjan tells me, “You don’t have to be Kiera. You can elect someone who is patient and balanced, who listens and considers before taking action, who does not want war and will keep peace with the empire, and who holds to the old ways.”
It sounds to me like he is describing himself.
“I could make you leader,” I offer.
Ohjan says nothing.
Mor’Sovra speaks up, “You are Varkier. You were born to be Kiera. If you give up this right, the right of your blood, you give it up for your children and theirs as well. Ohjan is a strong Elder but he cannot be Elder and rule Woodhome.”
Sovra looks fierce and I can tell she does not think I should give up this responsibility. Ohjan brings out a locked box and opens it. Inside are a number of items on a velvet cloth.
“These fetishes can help us try to determine how strong your Varkier and Uhlarn blood is, Cara,” Ohjan explains.
He carefully pulls out something delicate and precious. In his hand I see an acorn hat.
“You must seek yourself in this tiny item. It is part of an acorn top from the Tree of Naemora in the Homewood,” Ohjan says.
Sovra nods at me and I reach out to touch the acorn top. I focus on it and try to find the part of me that sings to the trees: Uhlarn. My hands turn brown and start to look like bark, my fingers lengthen and become almost claw-like. I become stronger and feel the change in my entire body. Vines sprout and reach for the acorn. The vines are covered in thorns. Sovra shows me what I look like in a mirror. I have leaves and branches for hair and my eyes are a vibrant green.
“Sheerdarr or Shadahn,” Mor’Sovra purrs. “This is the war form of the Uhlarn. It is a powerful druid form.
I smile in the mirror, and I look menacing.
“I look like the tree-woman on Kiern’Kirak,” I say. My voice is deeper and cracking like a tree.
Ohjan carefully takes the acorn top from my palm and Mor’Sovra instructs me how to leave the war form. I follow her instructions and return to myself again. Next, Ohjan hands me a different fetish.
“This is a catafass: a holding horn. It is a relic and made from many pieces of bone,” Ohjan says.
I carefully take the fetish from Ohjan. In my mind, I picture the giant cat in Kiern’Kirak. I picture Lysara powerful and running through the fields. My heart pumps, my breathing gets heavier and harder. This war form takes more effort, but it happens and it is more painful than the Uhlarn Sheerdarr. Fur sprouts all over my skin. My fingers lengthen and wickedly long claws grow. My bones lengthen, widen, thicken, and grow. I smell everything. I see every detail and hear the smallest sounds. The room is bright. 
Sovra shows me my image in the mirror again. I am muscled, powerful, and I look and feel ferocious. The mirror shows me as a lion-woman. My senses are more acute. I think again of the cat on Kiern’Kirak and how it could shift and change its fur. I change my fur to match my surroundings and swish my tail. I have the urge to hunt and run and kill. Ohjan takes the fetish out of my hand, and I shift back to my own form. This hurts, too, and takes effort. 
“Kier’marr, the king killer,” Sovra says softly and proudly.
Emric puts the fetishes back in the box before speaking.
“These forms prove you have the blood of both the Uhlarn and the Varkier. Emric hid the other half of your blood. He is guarding a truth, and he told you and Eladia to keep your teeth closed,” Ohjan tells us. “Have a good think on this, Cara, and consider the possibilities.”
I leave Ohjan’s study and put my boots on after stepping outside. Bormarr is waiting for me in the back garden. He walks with me into the woods. I watch the water at the waterfall before finding a quiet place at the edge of town. After some time spent in contemplation, I go visit Andolina and baby Malin who are staying with Ohjan’s bother, Dyurnok Voren and his wife, Jota. Keldoss, one of Voren and Jota’s sons. I ask to see Andolina and Malin. Jota gives me permission to come into her home.
“She is out back washing clothes,” Jota says.
I walk through the home and out the back to find Andolina. Malin is playing nearby. I help Andolina with the wash while we talk. After we speak for some time and I hold little Malin for a bit, playing with him, I leave to speak to the other keys. Roland is by himself in a house. He wants to see my notes and see the relic. Silas is sharing a house with Reynar. Silas asks for tobacco, new socks, and to exchange his gold for silver so he can trade for items in the market. 
Reynar still has Thurgen’s var’fascar. I tell him my line leads directly back to Thurgen Varkier. He says the mask or the magic in it does not work for him and that Thurgen wasn’t Ethragen but this is an Ethragen’s fascar even though there is no magic left in it. I ask Reynar to return Thurgen’s var’fascar to me and he does. Someone outside calls my name several times.
“No one knows I came here,” I say to Silas and Reynar. Silas stands and grabs his knives before stepping out. He returns a moment later looking puzzled.
“The trees are saying your name,” Silas says.
I walk outside and from a tree I hear, “Home, Cara, the Gorhunds.”
I do not recognize the voice. I nod at Silas and Reynar. I walk home and, on the way, I hear Mor’Renna’s voice, “Stay the course. The path you walk comes in steps. Watch your feet but stay the course. There are challenges ahead, child. Do not lose your way. Very soon, I will be able to aid you more but for now, float with the river.”
At the back of the house are 3 men and a woman standing with Ohjan, Mor’Sovra, and Mama. One man is a bald man in his 50s, his head is covered in glyphs woven to look like leaves. He has a braided beard and reddish hair. The other 2 men are younger and well-armed and the woman with them wears a leather dress and pants. Ohjan introduces the older man as Elder Jorel Uhlarn. It was his voice I heard speaking through the trees. 
Jorel bows, “Cara, this is my daughter Ohnarra and my 2nd son, Gellan (warden). Bruvass (Shield warden) is my nephew.”
They all bow, which is odd. It seems that even though I am not yet telling anyone I am Varkier, others have heard or why would they suddenly start bowing and saluting when they see me?
Ohjan says they may stay as their guests and speak with me. Mor’Sovra offers them food and drink and they respond very formally. The nuances and formality are beyond me. Jorel speaks in perfect innovar common so Mama can understand what is being said. Jorel is the Elder of the Uhlarn family. Jorel’s twin brother is the Dyurnok of Oakdelve.
Jorel explains to Mama the Uhlarn blood and ties to nature and the tests that can be performed to see if it exists in the blood of some of the Lost. Mama is Uhlarn and he tells us both that there are 30-thousand Uhlarn on many branches of the Uhlarn tree. Most live in and around Oakdelve and he tells us that we would both be welcome to visit or live there if we chose. 
Jorel asks me to describe what it was like taking the Shadahn war form (the tree woman). I tell him how powerful I felt and connected to all things. He smiles and invites us to stay in Oakdelve for a time so we can get to know this branch of our blood. 
“I can arrange it so your father and mother can travel via tree portal to and from Iron Hill and Oakdelve or Ilyrian,” he offers after I share my concerns that Mama and Papa have not decided yet where to live. He is going out of his way to make things easier on us given that Papa is an innovar and would usually not be welcome in Woodhome. 
“You can stay as long as you need, Cara,” Jorel offers. 
“Thank you, Jorel. I have to travel East to collect a shard,” I say.
I see something dark flash across Jorel’s face.
“The Uhlarns were Keepers of Naemora and the shards are pieces of the corrupted heart of Naemora. At Darasgar Peak (Fire Mountain), the Uhlarn made an oath to collect the broken pieces of the Mother and heal Her,” he tells me.
He asks a number of questions but I tell him there are things I cannot say out loud, truths that I know but cannot speak out loud because I have been warned that ears of our enemies may be listening, even here.
Jorel smiles softly and walks with me over to a Grandfather tree. 
“Through the tree, we can share memories. You can share your memories – those you are comfortable sharing. All you need to do is touch the tree, like this,” he says.
He places his hand on the trunk of the Grandfather tree and I do the same. It only takes about 10 minutes to share those memories I am comfortable sharing. Arch Druid Gulrian was at the ruin, the font of the Mother, when Bronnen and I used a relic and the blood of 3 keys to travel to the desert. Next, Jorel tests the strength of my blood himself. 
“Your blood is strong, Cara, but not strong enough to manifest form,” he declares.
He is very angry that Emric did not pass on the news of the shards to the Uhlarns but we don’t know that for certain. When we finish speaking, Jorel asks me to walk with him, his son, daughter, and nephew. We walk in the woods. 
“Ohnarra wants to get to know you because you didn’t grow up here in Woodhome. She is curious,” Jorel confides.
I smile. 
“The tree you said you touched in Western Woodhome, with the bark as smooth as skin, the one with a pulse – that was the pulse of the Mother. It is called a Bellaber tree, a Soul Tree. Soul Trees contain the souls of Hularens who have passed on and aren’t ready to cross over to the Mother,” Jorel tells me, pointing out a Soul Tree as we walk in the woods.
“I know that you are ‘touched,’ and that Emeric did not quiet the spirit. I know that you went to Mawdra’s cave not long after you arrived in Woodhome and the spirit is still with you. That is unusual. Perhaps you have been told that when Hularens are ‘touched’ by Rage Spirits, they go mad, slaughtering all near them?”
I nod. 
“She doesn’t harm me,” I confide. “Most of the time, Lysara sleeps.”
“I know that you are Varkier. The trees knew who you were the moment you entered Woodhome. ‘Uhlarn, Varkier’ they whispered to one another.”
He seems nice and friendly and patient, but I do not know him. I stay quiet, listening and watching. Jorel coaxes out a fairy for me to see. It looks like it is part squirrel or cat and covered in leaves. It is so cute and for the first time since our meeting, I smile. It has a tiny bow and quiver. 
“It is called a Merro, a tree sprite. We give them tiny stones inscribed with a blessing glyph which will keep their food from rotting, extending the storage and preservation of their food for twice as long. The Merro have 3 wives: a Spring Wife, a Summer Wife, and a Fall Wife,” Jorel explains. 
We continue talking as we walk. He seems to want nothing from me but for me to learn the Uhlarn side of my family. Eventually, we walk back to the Gorhund home. I talk to Ohjan for additional reassurance which I receive. I don’t want to leave Ilyrian or Bronnen or the Gorhund if I don’t have to. We may not share blood but I have lived here for 2 years, and I don’t want to live somewhere else. Ohjan assures me that I can live here with them as long as I like and no one can make me do anything I do not want to do. 
Ohjan does not want to rush the Day of Decision as Papa is likely to say no. He (Ohjan) and Jorel agreed on something that involves me. He will explain in more detail later but it also involves Dyurnok Voren. As if on queue, Voren walks into Ohjan’s office. 
“If you give your oath to Voren, it gives the Gorhund’s a bigger voice with the Arch Druids as you are not yet mated to Bronnen,” Ohjan explains.
I look between the two of them but say nothing, unsure of what to do. Ohjan senses my unease and uncertainty and asks me to walk with him. We walk quietly out of the house and through Ilyrian to a very special building that he has a key to. It is filled with Hularen relics. Inside, we stop in front of a painting of a woman holding a large snake.
“The Mother strangling a serpent,” Ohjan says quietly. “Her enemy God, Setharian the Dark Serpent, the World-Eater, Set.”
Ohjan shows me a number of items that the Gorhund have found and collected over generations. The items that they can identify as belonging to specific Gorhund families are returned to those families, but the rest are kept in this building for a time when they are needed. When we walk back to the house, Voren is gone. 
I walk upstairs to the room I share with Bronnen and check the scroll cases. There is one letter from the Arch Bishop that reads: “The Lord Emperor will return in 2 months and Papa will be expected to be in Travaghn on a specific date: 2 months and 5 days (19th of Dracos). An agent of the Lord Emperor may contact you. He has black hair, will appear incorporeal and shadow-like, and is extremely intelligent. The Lord Emperor expects you to comply without question and without pause. Progress toward making a stronger bond between Woodhome and the Empire.”
I burn the letter before responding with a letter of my own. After, I sit on the balcony in the quiet for an hour and a half. I see 4 hounds race off into the woods. I go downstairs and out back to the edge of the forest. I hear a low growl. I back up about 40-feet and the growling stops. I wait until Ohjan calls me back to the house.
“It’s not Bronnen or your father, Cara. It’s Spriggens. Go back inside.”
I do as Ohjan says and return to the room. I draw for an hour when a group of wrens land on the balcony, chirp, and fly away again. I walk to the balcony and see Jorel and Ohnarra outside waiting. I go out to greet them and we walk together to the market to eat and talk together. I tell them I was sketching before they came and that Mama was a talented painter. Jorel shows me a stack of drawings that belong to his son Nian. 
Our conversation covers numerous topics. Ohnarra asks what it was like growing up in the East and in Iron Hill. She asks about the people there and what I did. I tell her that I was Mama’s last child before my birthfather left. I had 4 older brothers and 2 older sisters and at least 2 of them were twins but I don’t know which because I learned a long time ago that it was too painful for Mama to talk about. I tell her that growing up as an only child, it was strange to come here and live among the Gorhund who had so many children. I tell her that Bronnen talks about how we will have at least 15 children, or 20, or 25 – it varies depending on the day and his mood and I can’t always tell if he is teasing or not. Ohnarra smiles and says that one of her sisters just gave birth to 7 babies at one time. This is common for Uhlarn women, to have multiple babies at a birthing and she’s not surprised that Mama had at least one set of twins. 
After we eat, I return to Roland’s so we can finish our conversation from earlier.
“The crystal shards, the dark shards, are necrotic energy from a dewormer used on the tree as a foci to draw in the energy from hundreds of millions of deaths. The dewormer is still active, still alive. The spell, with nowhere to go, backlashed causing the tree to explode and crystalize. The shards, are the tree, Cara. The darkness is what is left of the corrupted Mother. The shards, reassembled, could re-enact the dewormer and is why the Asha’kari want the shards. Either we finish the dewormer or dissipate the magic. If M escapes, it might complete the dewormer. The garden (Mor’Fang) holding M is failing and you need to try and fix it.”
I leave Roland’s and find Jorel and Ohnarra waiting for me. I tell them I need to speak with Ohjan and Jorel because I need to speak to Emric and I know he’ll be angry by what I tell him but he’ll be even angrier if I wait until tomorrow. Jorel tells me to sit and start from the beginning. He speaks to me the way a father would.
“I can’t, Jorel. It involves a truth that Emric has forbidden me to speak of to anyone (the cartouche under Travaghn trapping Hunger).”
Jorel and I go find Ohjan. Ohjan is in the living room working, writing. We wait patiently and I explain what I know, what I learned and that we need to speak with Emric. We walk outside and Bormarr is waiting for us. We walk together to Emric’s and as we walk, Ohjan and Bormarr speak without speaking. Before we reach Emric’s, Bormarr leaves. Jorel and I wait a short distance away while Ohjan speaks to Emric first. 15 minutes later, Jorel and I approach Emric who is sitting on a stump waiting for us. He is cooking a rabbit over a fire.
“Sit,” Emric says without looking up.
Ohjan and Jorel sit on either side of me.
“Emric, I need to speak to you but it involves a truth you told me not to speak of.”
Emric dismisses Ohjan and Jorel and we wait until they walk some distance away. When Emric nods, I explain what Roland told me.
“Some believe the shards can be cleansed of their necrotic damage… the Mor’Fang around Hunger’s cage is failing. We, I, need to try and strengthen it to prevent him from getting free to complete his dewormer – just like we strengthened the cage around the Great Wood.”
Emric asks of the Uhlarns told me that while the Uhlarn have tried numerous times to cleanse the corrupted shards that have been found, they have failed with every attempt and people have died as a result. The Uhlarn do not know how to cleanse the shards. He also thinks that the Mor’Fang beneath Travaghn is too unstable for me to attempt strengthening it as I did with the Mor’Fang in the Homewood, but he agrees that some can be sent in my stead to assess the cracks and the stability of the Mor’Fang imprisoning Hunger.
I listen to what Emric says and contemplate our next steps. He tells me the Uhlarn and the Gorhund agree that if there is to be a Kiera, she (me) must unite the people. 
“We cannot be divided. We cannot fight among ourselves or the empire. We must ally. The Hularen words you spoke to repair the stone of the Mor’Fang were Ethragen and Celestial. The Celestial can be explained but you are not Ethragen. The Stone Garden around the Circle of 9 failed long ago. The Arch Druids, Alveron specifically, will want to see if you can repair the stone and if you cannot, he will believe you choose not. It is not likely that they, some of the Arch Druids, will choose not choose to support a Varkier, or even a Kiera, as they (the Arch Druids) would no longer rule.”
I am surprised to hear Emric speak in such a way about the other Arch Druids considering he is one. I see Bormarr walk past us in the woods.
“Bormarr is a Gorhund “lost” to his form. This happens. This is why we do not think it good to walk around in the war forms because you can lose yourself in them,” Emric explains.
“The wood woman I saw on the Dragon’s Foot, on Kiern’Kirak, is she a Sheerdarr “lost” in her war form or is she something else? She told me to come back when I learned to speak properly. Or maybe she’s fey blood.” 
Emric says that the stone garden failing around Hunger’s cage is a truth that should not be shared. He tells me tomorrow is mine as he pulls off a bit of rabbit to eat.
“Who gave you the bone bracelet you wear on your ankle?” Emric asks.
“High Priestess Sharin gave it to me. She said it belonged to me, and I should never take it off. Neither should I let others see that I wear it.”
Emric laughs, “How does she know who you are?”
“What do you mean?”
Emric reaches over and clasps the bracelet, touches me with his other hand and chants quietly. The bone anklet grows warm, and I hear the roar of a dragon from all around. More dragon roars join the first and soon, multiple dragons are roaring. 
“The bracelet is dragon bone and the markings are of Thurgen Varkier. It would have belonged to Lysara, or Ahnira, or perhaps Renna, his wife,” Emric says before nodding for me to leave.
I leave Emric and walk back to Ohjan and Jorel. We walk together back to the house. They agree that Mama and Papa should also travel with us to the Circle of Nine. Ohjan says that 7 Gorhund will also come with us as an honor guard. Jorel will match that number with Uhlarn so both sides of my blood are represented equally. Back at the house, I grab a piece of paper and some charcoal and walk back outside past the bathhouse to sketch. The hounds shadow me.
I pick a spot with near a flat rock and draw Lysara as she appeared the first time I saw her. Then, I draw the Warrior sitting by a massive cage. I make my way back to the house before dark. When I show Ohjan, he identifies the sword Lysara carried.
“The sword is Jovokarn and it hangs in the armory,” he says.
I put the papers away and walk back outside where people are gathered. Bronnen and Papa brought back a deer and a number of pheasants. I help skin and prep the deer and defeather the pheasants. We clean up and then I go to the bathhouse to bathe. I return in time to help Mor’Sovra, her daughters, and Mama cook dinner. Papa is with the rest of the men. Mama asks Eladia what it is like to be a bird and fly. Eladia is happy to tell her what it is like. When dinner is ready, we carry all the food out to the table. We eat and talk and enjoy being together. 
Papa is relaxed and it is nice to see. He tells me that he knows about the Gorhund bloodline and traits. Bronnen told him and explained as much as he could. He even went so far as to show Mama and Papa what it means to have strong Gorhund blood and the form he can take. It is something they need to know and understand so they are not surprised if and when we have children. 
Ohjan explains that tomorrow will be a free day, meaning that we can do as we please or whatever we decide we need to do. The Arch Druids will want to speak to Bronnen and I at some point in the near future. I do not mention what Emric told me that the Arch Druids may not support a Varkier.
After dinner, I help clean up while Mama and Papa talk. When they finish, I bring them a drink. Mama goes to bed leaving Papa and I to talk.
“You have our permission and our blessing to marry Bronnen,” Papa says. “We can see how much you care for one another and how happy you make each other.”
After we finish talking, I leave Papa to finish his whiskey in comfortable silence. I walk upstairs to Bronnen’s room. Eladia is in here and they are talking quietly. The three of us talk about the Varkier line, discussing pros and cons, and that we have Mama and Papa’s blessing to marry. We also talk about a possible trip to Oakdelve. It is a long talk and we circle around many times when discussing the pros and cons of being Varkier, our duty versus our wants, the desires of the people and our own desires. 
Finally, Eladia goes back to her room and Bronnen and I go to sleep.

Dream 86: Timeran the Waif Shimmers
I woke up to the sound of crickets and the popping of a fire. I open my eyes. I am lying on my side near a cheery campfire. It’s not quite dark yet. I see someone else sitting on a moss-covered log near the fire. A small boy is carving a small piece of wood no bigger than his hands. I smile at the Waif and sit up.
“Hi, Cara.”
“Hello. What are you working on?”
“Lots of things. What are you working on?”
“I am learning who I am.”
He laughs, “That’s something we all work on, right? That never stops.”
There is an odd disturbance in the air shimmering around Him, almost like heatwaves.
“What,” He asks, “You have something to say?”
“Is this where my path was always leading?”
He laughs again, “Who said there was a path?”
“You did.”
“What I didn’t say is the road stretches out behind you. The road is there now because you walked it. Did you feel like there was an abundance of roads these last two years? Did it seem like easy traveling?” He smiles.
“No.”
“But look behind you in your memory. The road is long, isn’t it?”
“Yes.”
“It’s your road, Cara. You walked it but you didn’t walk it alone, did you?”
“No, You were always with me.”
He smiles, “And you were always with Me.”
“You shimmer, why?”
“I am no different than I ever was. It is not Me who’s changed. The others are very proud of you, did you know?”
“They said so on the field. She said it again that night at Father Bodin’s house. Mama’s back.”
I smile.
“That makes you happy, doesn’t it?”
“Yes, and You.”
“I always knew she would be back. Some things just take time.”
“Is this the choice You keep speaking of?”
He smiles again, continuing to carve the small piece of wood.
“There have been lots of choices haven’t there? Some of them weren’t very easy, were they?”
“No.”
“But you made them and now they seem fine, don’t they?”
“Yes.”
“You shouldn’t be here,” the Fox says from the tree line.
The Waif rolls His eyes. 
“I can go anywhere I want to. Go be part of someone’s fur coat somewhere.” 
I look toward the Fox’s voice and see a pair of eyes just in the darkness, low to the ground. The Waif picks up a small rock and throws it at the Fox.
“Pest.”
“You’re making a mess,” the Fox warns.
“Go away.”
“Is it the right choice, to become queen?” I ask.
“You’ve got it all wrong, Cara. When you became a girl, was it a difficult choice? Did you think a lot about it?”
“I was born a girl, it wasn’t a choice. I didn’t decide to become a girl, I just was. Am I being silly?”
“No, you chose Me.”
“Did you always want to be king?”
Porthios’s voice comes through the Waif’s mouth, “I wanted to matter. I wanted to create change. ‘Power and strategy are what you need to dominate the field.”
He quotes Himself.
The Waif speaks again, “This is My time. I think They miss you. He’s not wrong. What is a king or queen? You just decide stuff. I’m not here to tease you, Cara, though it is fun sometimes. You’re very worried all of a sudden though you weren’t when you ran away from Travaghn.”
“You needed me to leave.”
“Was that the only reason?”
“No.”
“The choice of power is not to be taken lightly. Leadership is an obligation to yourself and to others,” Porthios responds.
“I said it’s My turn,” the Waif yells. “He’s very pushy right now. He thinks We should be elsewhere. Seek a path, Cara, any path. He’ll make it work like always.”
The Waif sets the item He was carving on the moss log and disappears. I walk over and pick up a small piece of wood. He carved an intricate set of scales.
I walk back over to the bedroll and go back to sleep with the small, wooden scale in my hand.

**Summary of the Journal Entry:**
Cara spends a transformative day learning about her powerful bloodline, the responsibilities it entails, and the difficult choices she faces. After a profound morning prayer, Cara shares a divine message from the Mother with Emric, who reveals ancient secrets of the Varkier bloodline. Guided by her guardians Ohjan and Mor’Sovra, Cara taps into her dual heritage, manifesting both the Uhlarn war form and the Varkier’s lion-like “Kier’marr” form. As she grapples with the implications of potentially becoming the Kiera, Cara receives wisdom from the Uhlarn Elder Jorel, who offers insights into her heritage and provides an invitation to Oakdelve. Emric’s warnings about the Mor’Fang’s stability heighten the stakes of Cara’s path, and a mysterious dream brings her face-to-face with the Waif, who urges her to embrace her journey despite the weight of her choices.

- **Letter from Arch Bishop Sandlin**: A message from the Arch Bishop instructs Cara to comply with imperial agents as part of her growing influence.

Cara’s day is marked by a profound exploration of heritage, identity, and destiny, as she prepares to step into a role that may unite her people or reshape her world forever.

Read the following journal entry for my D&D character, Cara. Create a list of important items, locations, names, objectives and events. Each list should be a separate category. Include a summary of the of the journal entry: 11th of Solik, 2324 IC   11th of Solik, 2324 IC. Ilyrian

Wake, dress, and pray. I go downstairs to eat breakfast. Arch Druid Emric arrives just after I finish eating and I leave with him. On the walk back to his hut he tells me, the sword in my vision, the sword Lysara carried has two names. Jovo’karn is the ancient name and in old Hularen means Hammer (to) Slay and the more current translation comes from how its name is derived in current Hularen as Jovo’kiernen which means Hammer of (the) King.
“Seven families have claim to the throne but none as strong as the Thierkiernon. The Gorhund once married a kier,” Emric instructs. 
“But the Uhlarn were the most recent, were they not? Thurgen Varkier’s wife was Mor’Renna Uhlarn?”
“She was of the Uhlarn line, yes.”
When we reach Arch Druid Emric’s hut, we sit outside on tree stumps that ring a small fire. Emric produces a small bundle and sets it down on another stump.
“First, I need to divine your blood, your family,” he says.
I watch him pull out dried reeds, claws, bones, twigs, leaves, stones, and bark. When Emric holds the reeds to my skin, nothing happens, and the result is the same when he holds the stone to my skin. When he holds a piece of bark to my skin, it slowly transforms my skin to browns and creams and my arm resembles the bark of a tree. I stare in wonder at the transformation. When he pulls the bark away, my skin returns to its normal color and form. Many of the other items cause no change and I wonder if it is common for Hularens to take more than one form. I know they did once. He patiently tries every item, holding it to my skin to confirm what he seems to already know. The last item is a necklace of bones, fangs and claws. The claws and fangs curve in and look like the fangs and claws of a cat. When Emric holds the necklace to my skin, my fingernails lengthen and sharpen. I hear the old Hularen words of a war chant echo in my head. My sense of smell enhances, and my vision is wicked sharp. I feel strong.
“This is an older family bloodline,” Emric says.
“Whose?”
He doesn’t answer which I guess is druid for “you’ll learn soon enough.” Emric paints symbols all over my body. As he paints, I tell him about a different vision or dream when I woke up in an old forest on a bed of furs near a cheery fire. My belly was swollen with child, and symbols were painted all over me in blue paint. His eyes sharpen as I describe the symbols to him. As he works, he teaches me the words I need to repeat in the Pool of the Mother. The symbols take time and Emric is careful. There is a rhythm to the words and his work. It’s familiar and I know, I remember, this calls the Mother and it is similar to the war chant Lysara sings but this rhythm matches the Mother’s heartbeat.
When he is done with all the symbols, Emric tells me how to get to the Pool of the Mother. We begin walking passing through the middle of Ilyrian to the Pool of the Mother. As we walk, animals stop and watch us pass. When we reach the path to the Pool of the Mother, the ground is strewn with flower petals and the beginning of the path is marked with a single stone cartouche – the tip is broken off. I take off my boots and continue walking along the flowered path which leads through huge trees that line the path like columns in a temple. The birds fall silent as we walk and Emric continues to quietly chant. 
We reach a valley and in the middle are 4 standing stones with symbols carved all along the inside of the Mor’Fang stones. The tips are curved in, protecting what lays in the center of the stone garden. Lined in stones, shimmers a serene Pool of the Mother. All of Ilyrian is in the valley to witness my bonding to the Mother. Over half the people are wearing the black and blue of the Gorhund. I pull my gaze from the many faces and focus on the Pool of the Mother. Emric and I stop at the Pool of the Mother. Steps lead down into the water. Emric addresses all gathered with words that have been said thousands of time before, each time a child of the Mother is bonded to Her.
“Where there is one, there are many.”
The people respond in unison, “Where there are many, there is one.”
He names me “Carathul Yornlin Uhlarn,” Mama’s bloodline and I wonder. I reacted to two of the items. Uhlarn makes sense, Mama is Uhlarn, but the other? The old bloodline he doesn’t name. He is holding something back – what is it? He signals to the Gorhund woman to come forward so I may disrobe. All the Gorhund men face outward, and I am protected from many eyes. This is not normal for a Bonding with the Mother but I did not grow up here and this is fairly common for a Lost who was raised among the innovar with an instilled sense of modesty and embarrassment regarding the naked form. 
I quickly step into the pool of water which is pleasantly and unexpectedly warm. The water is clear and there is a layer of soft moss and mud at the bottom. My footsteps cause some of the moss to come loose and a blue-green algae fills the pool. Emric signals me to sit, and I lower myself down onto a flat stone in the water. I look up at Emric and his pupils swirl with a brilliant blue. The water smells of loam and roots and trees: deep and rich, bright and crisp. 
The Gorhund woman step back from the pool while the Gorhund men turn around to face the pool once more. I keep my focus on Emric watching for his nod. All eyes are on him and when he gives the signal, we all start to chant together. My voice is quiet and calm. I am not sure what will happen as everyone I have asked has said it is better to experience than to hear it described. I chant the words Emric taught me, my voice mingling with thousands more.
There is a black hole near me and as we chant, it begins to glow blue. The water in the Pool of the Mother begins to slowly swirl around me. The water grows even warmer, and I feel Her pulse, the soft heartbeat I have become familiar with when I commune with Her in the early mornings. The pool fills with blue light until all of the water shimmers and glows a brilliant blue light. Mother is here. We continue to chant, and the light grows even brighter, impossibly bright. The symbols on the Mor’Fang also glow blue and suddenly, I am somewhere else.
I look around me, aware that I am no longer where I was though I am still in water. Beneath me, as I look down, there is glowing blue water everywhere. I am surrounded in it, no longer sitting on a stone, but floating in water that glows a brilliant blue. There are no trees, no people, no stones, no Mor’Fang – just water and Her blue essence spreading out in all directions. I float in the middle of it all, flooded with peace, feeling Her massive, slow and steady heartbeat flow through me. 
Far in the distance is a disruption in the water. From seemingly nowhere, a giant waterfall appears and a surge of blue light 100-feet tall flows slowly towards me. As it gets closer, it becomes smaller and takes form. I watch as a figure steps out and looks exactly like me, but with swirling blue light. She has the same markings and the same flower crown. We stare at one another. She is silent and I stay silent out of reverence and awe. 
She raises one arm and it becomes a tree. She raises Her other arm and it swells with muscles and fur runs the length of that arm while the fingers lengthen and grow long, curved claws. One side of Her hair becomes branches and vines and leaves, and that side of Her face looks like bark. The other side of Her hair becomes a mane of hair, the ear grows a point, and that side of Her face is covered in fur. One eye turns brown and looks like a knot in a tree while the other turns golden and is slitted like a cat’s eye. She smiles and on one side, the cat side, I see upper and lower fangs. The change is from head to toe, one side the war form of the Uhlarn’s Sheedarr and the other… a large hunting cat.
The Mother clasps Her hands together, lacing Her fingers together: tree and cat. She holds this form for several heartbeats and then reforms back into an identical image of me. She surges forward and I watch as my mouth, Her mouth moves to form a word. 
I hear Her say, “Both.”
She passes beneath me, becoming mammoth as She changes form again, becoming a waterfall of glowing blue water. A huge chasm appears just feet in front of me and the water, Mother, hovers before me. She says the word a second time.
“Both.”
Her voice is a whisper but it thunders in my ears before fading away. She slides under me again and the water around me swells. She lifts me so high and so fast. 
In a single heartbeat, I am back in the Pool of the Mother, sitting on the flat stone in the middle of the pool, staring up at Emric who is still chanting. As I watch, the swirling blue in his eyes fades and the swirling blue glow of the water around me fades. The Mother pulses through me like a hammer striking metal and I feel the tremors of Her shake the ground around the pool.
I look around me and see Ohjan. I see the hound of the Gorhund in him – a powerful presence. I see Mor’Sovra and the hunting cat of the Varmarkuhn in her. I see Mama and she is blurry but alive, though muted. I look at Papa and he is grey and non-descriptive. So many Gorhund. So many others, I can see them: hounds, and cats, and birds, and trees, and bears, and others. 
I look at Emric and see a huge presence, a column of swirling blue enveloping him, swirling blue in his eyes. I see similar columns of blue in other druids and they all vary in intensity. I see the trees surrounding the Pool of the Mother and the trees see me. I feel them all and the trees feel me. I feel the harmony and symmetry of the stones around me and further away. I realize the chanting has stopped as everyone around me is watching me “see” for the first time with new eyes – Hularen eyes.
Behind them all, in the shadow of the trees, I see Mor’Renna and I hear her voice as clearly as if she were standing right beside me.
“One step closer. Well done girl. I am very proud of you.”
She steps back into the darkness of the forest and I lose her in the crowd. The Gorhund women encircle the pool once more while the Gorhund men ring them and face out so I can put the robe back one. When I am dressed again, I walk to the edge of the pool. As I step out, I hear muffled voices all around me. Spirits, I think, but their voices quickly fade. I look at my parents and they are staring at me wide-eyed because my skin looks like bark and my hair looks like vines. The form fades on its own.
We all walk back to Ilyrian in a procession with me at its head. People play music and sing as we walk all the way back to a bonfire. People bring food to share and dance as musicians play. We dance late into the night.
As the celebration winds down and people start drifting to their homes, Arch Druid Emric walks over to me.
“You have done well, Carathul. Tomorrow, walk Ilyrian and experience it all again for the first time,” he says. “Go home and rest.”
When I sleep that night, I do not dream.

Read the following journal entry for my D&D character, Cara. Create a list of important items, locations, names, objectives and events. Each list should be a separate category. Include a summary of the of the journal entry: 9th of Solik, 2324 IC   9th of Solik, 2324 IC. Ilyrian

Wake, dress, pray, and eat breakfast.
Later, Mama and Papa, Sovra and Ohjan, Bronnen and I sit in the living room and talk. Papa asks questions about the Ritual of Decision, the Bonding to Mother and Rebirth, the Ceremony of Mating, and more. Ohjan explains that Gorhund means “night hound.” He also explains their simple view of the empire. Ohjan says that when I told them of what was happening at the Eastern Citadel, the Gorhund deliberated on going to help Papa and why. They speak of a great number of topics including children we might have, where we might live, Porthios, and the Neighbor’s War. Some of the conversation is uncomfortable.
Ohjan says, “You (innovar empire) cannot steal what is not owned.”
Papa responds, “You (Hularen) cannot claim territory that you do not live on.”
That afternoon, I write a letter to Arch Bishop Sandlin.
“It’s critical to deal with the Hulean Lords in Thornwall. They have committed and continue to commit a number of crimes against the people of Woodhome. Their criminal actions go against Hulean Imperial law and reflect poorly on the empire. I am told that their actions breech the alliance between Woodhome and the empire. Their crimes include but are not limited to: gross inflation in price of goods, sell of black lotus, prostitution, and selling information and relics. This will go a long way to diminish hostilities between the people of Woodhome and the Hulean Empire.”
I send the message to Arch Bishop Sandlin using the scroll case. 
Bronnen tells me that Emric wishes to speak to us both at his place. We walk to Emric’s together. As we get to the bridge, Bronnen speaks, wondering aloud why Emric summoned us. I look up to see an old woman in her 80s staring at us. She has wispy, white hair and she is deeply wrinkled. Something must be wrong because I think she looks lost. I draw Bronnen’s attention to her.
“Orla,” Bronnen says, recognizing her.
We walk over to her.
“Hello, Orla. Mother’s blessings to you.”
She says nothing and continues to stare, unmoving.
Bronnen gently touches her arm.
“Orla, can we help you?” Bronnen asks, his voice filled with concern.
She blinks and looks at me, “Drumbeats. I hear them. You brought the drums.”
“Orla, where is Mannik?” Bronnen asks.
“The drums,” she repeats, “I hear them. You brought the drums.”
“Where is your son? Where is Mannik? Or Jada, your granddaughter? Why are they not with you?” Bronnen asks the old woman.
She stares at me, “Falling. Many will end up falling.”
Orla switches her gaze to Bronnen, “There is a lot of blood on your hands, Gorhund. You see but you do not see.”
Her words sound prophetic to me and I wonder if she hears the war drums that I hear when Lysara sings her war chant.
“Where is Jada, Orla?” Bronnen asks again, searching for her son or granddaughter in the people of the market. 
Orla looks between the two of us and she looks confused.
“You brought the drums,” she repeats softly.
We hear a whistle as a girl comes running up to us, 3 men in her wake. The left side of the girl’s face looks like she’s been beaten.
“Grandmother,” she calls as she runs up to us and wraps her arm around Orla’s shoulders.
“You brought the drums, I hear them,” Orla says as they turn and walk away.
Bronnen and I walk on toward Emric’s. A bird lands about 30-feet ahead of us and we stop.
“Who are you and what do you want?” Bronnen asks the bird.
The bird shifts form into Jehan, Bronnen’s brother.
“Walk carefully with Emric, Bronnen, something has changed. Emric called our father and uncle Voren to a private council. They have told no one anything except that Emric has demanded you and Cara be watched over. You are surrounded by 12 right now, all druids from here, Laneroc, and a few other places. Emric’s exact words were, ‘Not a breath or a step is taken by Bronnen or Cara that is not viewed by one of you.’ Also, you should know Loras Bovarr – he’s returned to his form,” Jehan speaks quickly and quietly.
“What?” both Bronnen and I ask, but for completely different reasons.
Jehan looks to me, “He was trapped in his war form for a month and had to be caged because he was so wild. He couldn’t return from his war form.” He moves his gaze to Bronnen before continuing, “But now, he’s himself again. Emric says the Mother is turning. Emric wants to take you both to the Council of Druids and the Circle of Nine Moons.”
Jehan’s concern for us concerns Bronnen, too. Bronnen claps his brother on the shoulder and nods before we walk on to Emric’s hut. Bronnen tells me not to worry, we’ll figure it out and he’s sure Emric will tell us why we are being watched. At the head of the trail stands a man I don’t recognize. He has silvery-blonde hair and almost green eyes, even the whites of his eyes are green.
“Conik,” Bronnen says in greeting and introduction.
“Bronnen,” Conik returns. “Carathul. I was waiting for you. I will escort you to Emric. He’s not in his house but in the grove of the Pool of the Mother.”
Beside Conik is a very large bear with shaggy, green fur. The bear stands 6 ½ feet tall at the shoulders and as I look closer, I realize the fur is green grass, moss, lichen, and leaves over a body of small trees, shrubs, and vines. The bear’s eyes are a brilliant solid green. 
“Conarok is of the Llandal line,” Bronnen explains. 
Druid Conarok smiles, “Carathul, do you want to know of your sons?”
I remember Ethalos Llandal, a Knight of Porthios, and his strange prophecies that not always come true. 
“No, thank you, Conarok. I will learn of my sons when I have sons,” I smile.
The bear gives a soft growl.
Conarok smiles in return and motions to the giant green bear, “This is Baeloc. He’s an Earthbear. Baeloc wants to meet you, Carathul.”
“Yes, please,” I say excitedly looking between Bronnen and Conarok. “I would like very much to meet Baeloc.”
Bronnen looks dubious.
“Stand very still and be quiet,” Bronnen warns.
Baeloc walks up to us both and sniffs intently. He leans close and rubs his giant head against me making me laugh. I place one hand on the side of face, and he makes a small chuffing noise. 
“He’s happy to mee you,” Conarok says, tilting his head. “Baeloc wants to know how we are covered in the scent of the Mother.”
“That is a truth we know but not one we can yet voice into the air,” Bronnen says.
Conarok nods and changes the subject, “Earthbears are creatures of the Mother’s wrath. There are only 7 left and 2 travel with druids.” 
It’s odd, being escorted around Ilyrian. Conarok dampens the sound around us and hides the path we take. Again, it’s odd that we shouldn’t be seen or heard but he doesn’t explain why. We walk together to the Pool of the Mother where Emric waits for us. We do not take the path but wind our way through the forest. We break through the trees and into a clearing. In the center is an almost round pool of water surrounded by stones and a stone garden. It looks like an underground well-spring. Just beyond the pool of water is a huge tree, even by Hularen standards. Standing on one of the roots is Emric. This tree reminds me of the giant desiccated tree in Sanctuary, but this one is alive. Bronnen and I stop where we are – we are not supposed to be near this tree.
Druid Conarok and Baeloc walk over to the massive tree and Emric. Hanging from the tree are bones inscribed with Druidic symbols. 
“Only druids are allowed here,” Bronnen whispers, his brows furrowed, “and being called here is not good.”
Conarok turns back to look at us both and says ominously, “It was nice to have met you while you lived.”
Conarok and Baeloc leave the area, walking into the woods. Emric steps down off the root of the giant tree and walks toward us. He looks tense.
“What have you done?” he demands.
His gaze is locked on me. I think quickly and tell him about Sanctuary. As I speak, I do not feel the ominous warnings Porthios usually sends when I speak to people of things I need to keep secret. He listens intently as I talk. When I fall silent, he walks to the Pool of the Mother and motions us over. In the water, we see the images of Bronnen and I standing over the swirling blue water of the Mother in Sanctuary.
“You force us to value your lives against the value of keeping this secret,” Emric says. “You are summoned before the Council of Druids. The things you have done cannot be undone and yet you travel with the Mother’s blessing. Do you know why?”
Bronnen shakes his head no.
Emric turns his gaze back to me and asks, “How did you reforge the Mor’Fang?”
I tell Emric how I did what I did. I explain exactly what happened and what words I said, a mixture of Celestial and words I did not know or understand (old Hularen). Bronnen adds in elements from his point of view of what he witnessed. Emric directs our view back to the Pool of the Mother and this time we see our reflections as we appear now. Around Bronnen and I is a pulsing blue light.
“The Mother is with you, She is in you both,” Emric explains. “The Mother and the Dark Mother can think of nothing but destroying one another. The beast that lays sleeping in the wood will not sleep forever. 2-million, their lives sucked like daggers through the Great Tree. 100-million innovar, their souls plunged through the Great Tree like spears. An evil that has slept because of the sacrifice of our people, for almost 10-thousand years now awakens.
“I have studied the keys and each is touched in their own way, passed down through their bloodlines. The Storm God may be the messenger, but it is the Mother who wants them gathered. It is why the armillary is needed to find them. They are the remnants of the spirits that escaped at the Mother’s maiming and returned to their bodies. Arch Druid Alvaron has many questions for you and it is he who summoned you to appear before the Council of Druids at the Circle of 9 Moons where your fates will be decided,” Emric says.
The look on my face must be one of terror because Emric’s face and voice soften when he speaks next.
“You are destined to be mated to one another. We will perform the Ritual of Decision, have your parents aligned by then so we may proceed. Cara, we will perform your Bonding to the Mother for your rebirth before we meet with the Council of Druids. Now, go home.”
Bronnen squeezes my hand, and we turn to leave. As we walk back to his home, Conarok and Baeloc join us. 
“The grove where you and Emric spoke, the tree is one of the 1st planted by the Hularen people. The druids cannot see the Mother touch but here in the grove, we can. Mor’Renna said you are touched (by the Mother) but She did not do the touching,” Conarok says.
I am not sure how to respond, “One of the Spiritwalkers of the Sumar also said I was touched by Mother.”
The way Conarok said it though, emphasizing the word “she” would lead me to think that the Mother did not bless us which could only mean that Porthios did unless the Mother is keeping Her own secrets. When we are safely home, Conarok and Baeloc wander off into the woods once more. 
Our parents are at the table out back. Papa shows me how he revised my letter to the Arch Bishop but it sounds wholly like Papa and not like me at all. The list of items Papa has written in regards to an alliance between Woodhome and the Hulean Empire is… most definitely written from the perspective of a loyal Hulean Imperial Commander though many of the points are mine. Papa suggests we propose and agree to the following:
	Agree to be allies of mutual respect.
Woodhome will not subjugate themselves to being ruled by an outside force.
Woodhome will not field men to lands outside of Hule.
Woodhome will agree to common and legitimate trade and common defense of all Hulean lands.
Woodhome will agree to come to the aid of the Hulean Empire in conflicts on Hulean soil against foreign threats.
Woodhome demands independent sovereignty but will agree to discuss the finer points of laws between the teo peoples. 
Woodhome will not open the entirety of the borders of their land to free travel both for the safety of those who live in Woodhome and for those who do not.
Woodhome will open common trading ports.
Woodhome will not tolerate spies or acts of aggression and are willing to meet those terms in both directions.
Woodhome will not teach outsiders our magics but we will aid the Hulean Empire with our magics.
These are terms all of Woodhome would agree to if the Hulean Empire acts as better neighbors. 
Request Arch Bishop Sandlin send a Porthion priest to act as Judiscar in Thornwall (for the Hulean merchants living in Thornwall).
I promise Papa that I will consider the items on the list and his other suggestions. Bronnen explains to our parents what happened and what was said. The conversation shifts to lighter topics: painting, gardening, hunting, Iron Hill, languages and how absurd innovar common can be, and sleeping in trees.
After our talk, I show Mama & Papa the bathhouse. Bronnen walks with us. As we walk back, we hear a bunch of bird-like noises and then little beings imitating our speech. In our path is a pile of blackberries and raspberries. I scoop them up into my hands to share with Mama, Papa, and Bronnen. 
“Limericks,” Bronnen says. “There are several of them here. My mother welcomes them to the garden, a number of fey, really. She has the most fey in Ilyrian but more have arrived since Cara has been here. Limerik’s bless the gardens and for them to communicate with us and leave berries for us – this is a great blessing, indeed. Limerik are flying fey who hunt bugs and snakes at night and cultivate gardens.”
Both Mama and Papa are surprised that fey are not only real but exist here in great numbers. Bronnen and I point up into a nearby tree so Mama and Papa can catch glimpses of the Limerks. 
Back at the house, Mama and I help make dinner and we all eat together. Arch Druid Emric joins us and engages Mama and Papa in conversation and tries to answer all of their questions and alleviate their concerns. Emric acknowledges the challenges and risks of Bronnen and I marrying but makes a long speech about love and commitment and tells them they have raised me with those strong examples.
Emric also addresses their concerns about Porthios saying, “No one will stop Cara from following the Storm God. He was reckless as a man marching here, and as a god in choosing Cara to do what she has done. But no one will stop her from following Him.”
Emric speaks very highly of me and my utter loyalty to Porthios.
“She (Cara) goes to war with an army, an army of one: the Storm God. How many Hulean Imperial soldiers or Woodhome warriors is one Storm God worth?” Emric asks.
I think Papa agrees with him, given how angry he is with Porthios. Emric talks about why Bronnen and I should marry, why we are good for one another, how our children will hear 3 times as well as innovar children, and how they will be able to see in the dark. He tells Papa we have to be at the Circle of 9 Moons because Bronnen and I changed something that will have repercussions for a long time. 
After dinner, Mor’Sovra pulls out a large box and Bronnen brings out a keg. The keg is seamless, unbanded, and uncarved. The box holds long fluted, spiraled glasses etched with vines and animals and rimmed in silver. There are 6 glasses and Mor’Sovra pulls out all 6. The keg holds a glowing blue-green liquid called “Yur’teen” which translates to “Earth wine,” it is also called the “Elixir of Three.” 
“The barrel of yur’teen was given to my father’s father as a gift long ago. The secret of the making was lost to most, and it is a highly guarded secret passed down through the families. It is saved for the most meaningful moments,” Ohjan explains. “When you first came here, Cara, and the land accepted you, word spread, and you are known as “the girl who came home. This yur’teen celebrates your return and your mother’s, your bond to Bronnen, and the uniting of our two families. To family, to friends, to kin,” Ohjan toasts.
We all raise our glasses to the toast and drink the yur’teen. The taste feels like magic as a tingling warmth spreads quickly through our bodies. It is exquisite. Our vision improves for a moment, and we can see clearly in the dark. I see winged creatures in the trees. Two tiny fey men are hauling an acorn along a branch. I see the hounds laying among the trees ringing the glade. Fairies dart in tiny flashes of light. My sense of smell is heightened as is my hearing. Everything is alive. Mama and Papa are shocked and amazed and I am enthralled by the experience. We put our hands on the earth, and I feel Her presence, Mother’s heartbeat. Mama feels Her, too.
We take a second drink. There is another flush of warmth, and I hear and feel a low hum in the stone table. Papa can feel this, too. I feel an order and harmony to everything and everyone around me. After dinner, Mama & I bathe. We are ringed by the Gorhund hounds, all 8 of them. When we walk out again, the 8 has increased to 14. The largest has something in his mouth: a necklace with the glyph I made with Mawdra in her cave. I take is from Bormarr but he doesn’t budge and even prevents me from continuing to walk until I put the necklace on. As soon as I put the necklace on, the hounds fan out. I feel the medallion pulse with the Mother’s heartbeat. 
The hounds escort us back to the house and I see Mor’Sovra standing out back waiting for our return. Mor’Sovra has a small snack waiting for Mama and I and we, three, sit down to eat and talk and drink a cup of warm tea before going to bed. I forget all about the medallion. 
Upstairs, I check the scroll cases and there is a letter from Arch Bishop Sandlin. He asks how Mama & Papa arrived in Woodhome and if they are well. He relays that the Lord Emperor wishes to speak with Papa regarding the citadel and what transpired there. He asks what our plans are for the next month and for a copy of the words spoken at the stone I rebuilt so they may be studied. He instructs me to understand the mindset of Woodhome and to ascertain the people of Woodhome’s frame of mind. The Arch Bishop also directs me to arrive in Lodonen’s Field outside of 2 Forks to journey East and retrieve something I put away. 
“You will not be alone. Please tell your parents they can rest comfortably as you will travel there in the company of royalty. Do not be late.”
I respond to Arch Bishop Sandlin’s letter and then burn it after I have answered all his questions. I add the ideas Papa had written for Thornwall. When I open the scroll case to send my letter, I find a second short message waiting for me which reads: 
“Speak these words now: Be’horat senu’than Aremus contass le’morol deta’ka’tien.”
The words are neither Celestial nor are they Hularen. I tell Bronnen about the message. He nods at me, indicating that I should do as the message instructs and say the words. When I do, my vision blurs and darkness swallows us up. I feel exhausted. My arms and legs are so heavy and tired. I cannot move but I am so relaxed. From the darkness, I hear a voice I do not recognize. The voice comes from behind me.
“I am not here to harm you, but I have no time for chatter. I am only here for limited moments and my form does not allow me to do what must be done. I am not your Arch Bishop, obviously.”
The voice belongs to a man. A hand with long slender fingers comes in front of my eyes. The hand is transparent, and I feel power radiate out of his closed fist.
“I am not here to harm you,” he says.
The magic disappears. I am still hazy.
“Are you hearing me?”
I nod.
“Good.”
He points to one of my penknives.
“Pick up that knife and cut your finger. Enough for 17 drops of blood, then drop the blood on a piece of paper. Roll it up and return it through the scroll case.”
Terrified, I do not move. 
“I do not have time for your suspicions, girl. Your blood is a necessary component. Your enemies are my enemies. I am here to aid you, and you will not speak of my presence here. Do not force me to coerce you.”
I try to turn my head to see who is speaking but I cannot.
“Do not make me repeat myself. If you were to see me, I would wipe your memory of the last 3 years. If I were your enemy, child, you would be dead and I would take your blood easily.”
The only part of my body I can move is my right arm. I pick up the knife and use it to cut my finger. I set the knife down and pick up the paper, counting 17 drops of blood.
“Never do this again for anyone else,” he instructs. His voice is sharp but wispy. “Good. Refrain from entering the wood. Refrain from going anywhere near the cartouches beneath Travaghn. The soul there will un-make you. Avoid any travelers from Rustin – there is a corruption there – and avoid anyone with almond skin from the East. It is unlikely you will hear my voice again. If you do, comply.”
I hear him say something in Draconic and the words from the message disappear.
“I know you keep secrets, Hularen. I am not a secret, but you do not know me, and I was not here. If you speak of me, you will face Morvic and Hyrkass alone. 
I think to myself that he must be a Seul and he reads my thoughts. 
“Yes, child, I am but I am not. You are one of a handful that knows I am here. Breech my confidence to your peril and all who walk this land. Now, say the words that you understand and that you agree.”
I nod my head, tears pooling in the corners of my eyes.
“I understand. I will not speak to anyone of you,” I whisper.
Words appear in water on the desk. Again, they aren’t Celestial or Hularen or even Draconic. They must be Seulean:  Avarum Aremus.
“Speak the words,” he instructs.
“Avarum Aremus.”
He disappears and with him, the darkness disappears, and we can move again. I watch Bronnen, worried, but he is breathing, and I realize he is asleep. I send the paper with my blood on it through the scroll case to Arch Bishop Sandlin. Bronnen wakes up not long after. 
I remember the amulet and tell Bronnen about it and the hounds. I reach for the leather band around my neck but to show him, but the leather cord and amulet are gone. Bronnen suggests that perhaps I dropped it outside and didn’t realize it. We go downstairs together and search for it. Bronnen calls for Bormarr. Moments later, he appears with the others. 
“Bormarr, you gave Cara a medallion.”
Yes.
“Did it come from Mawdra?”
Yes.
“Will it cause her harm?”
No.
“You made her put it on?”
Yes.
“Why did you not tell Ohjan outsiders were in our territory?”
Bormarr looks confused at that question. Bronnen tries a different question.
“Mawdra is not Gorhund, why let her in? Why give Cara something?”
Cara is pack, Mawdra is not. Bormarr whines
“It doesn’t matter if you agree. Since when do you disobey Ohjan?”
Bormarr whines again.
“Was there magic on the amulet?”
All the hounds paw the ground before touching their muzzles to the earth.
“The Mother?”
Yes.
“The Mother wanted Mawdra here?”
Yes.
“You’re sure?”
Yes. Bormarr growls at Bronnen.
“Ohjan will not be pleased when I tell him, you know that.”
Bormarr growls as second time.
“It’s not an argument. We have to tell father.”
All the hounds growl.
“Why? Does the Mother not want anyone to know?”
Yes. Bormarr sends 2 of the hounds to retrieve something and we wait 15 minutes for them to return. When they do, something speaks from the darkness. It’s dark but I can see a small creature with green hair, long green ears and a tiny hat. It speaks in Sylvan to Bronnen.
“Mawdra delivered the ward to her. The Mother wished it to be so. She (the Mother) wants it quiet until the Harvest Moon.”
“Why,” Bronnen asks.
“Unknown. You have the blessings of the Mother,” the tiny fey says before flying off.
“That is a Pixen,” Bronnen says. “Ken’shall’la” is Sylvan for “Mother.”
Bronnen and I retrace my steps from the bathhouse back to the house to see if I dropped the amulet, but it is nowhere to be found. The hounds walk with us, guiding us along the exact path Mama and I took. We get almost to the house when Bronnen stops and squats. He picks up a small fragment of braided leather cord. It is old and hard and breaks into pieces between his fingers. The amulet is gone. 
That night when I sleep, I do not dream.

[ASSISTANT]
### **Summary of the Journal Entry:**
On the 9th of Solik, Cara continues to uncover deep and complex connections to the Mother and her role within the Hularen people. After receiving ominous prophecies from the seer Orla, Cara and Bronnen are summoned to the Pool of the Mother by Emric. There, they are informed of their summons to the Council of Druids at the Circle of Nine Moons due to their actions in reforging the Mor’Fang and their ties to the Mother. The day is also marked by mysterious encounters with powerful entities, including a cryptic and threatening Seul presence demanding Cara’s blood for unknown purposes. The Mother’s influence looms heavily, as does the secrecy surrounding the events of the day, further complicating Cara’s already tangled fate.

---

### **Important Items:**
- **Medallion from Mawdra**: A mysterious glyph-inscribed amulet given to Cara by the hounds, linked to the Mother and intended to remain secret until the Harvest Moon. It later disappears under unexplained circumstances.
- **Yur’teen (Earth Wine)**: A rare, glowing blue-green elixir reserved for special occasions, enhancing senses and granting profound clarity of connection with the Mother and the surrounding environment.
- **Letter to Arch Bishop Sandlin**: Cara’s correspondence outlining proposed terms for peace and cooperation between Woodhome and the Hulean Empire.
- **Scroll Case and Blood Ritual**: Used to send 17 drops of Cara’s blood to an unknown Seul entity through Arch Bishop Sandlin, at the being’s threatening insistence.
- **Fragment of Braided Leather**: Remains of the medallion’s cord found near the house, hinting at its mysterious disappearance.

---

### **Key Locations:**
- **Emric’s Grove**: The location of the Pool of the Mother and the ancient Hularen tree. This sacred place is reserved for druids and holds deep spiritual significance.
- **Market**: Where Cara and Bronnen encounter Orla and Jada, and witness Orla’s cryptic prophecies.
- **Bronnen’s Home**: A central hub of family discussions and interactions with both human and fey visitors.
- **Bathhouse Path**: The path where Cara and Bronnen retrace steps to search for the lost amulet.
- **Lodonen’s Field (mentioned)**: Destination instructed by Arch Bishop Sandlin for Cara to retrieve an important item.

---

### **Key Characters:**
- **Cara (Carathul)**: Struggles with her growing responsibilities, ties to the Mother, and the mysterious demands placed on her.
- **Bronnen Gorhund**: Cara’s partner, who supports and guides her through the day’s challenges while mediating between her and his family.
- **Arch Druid Emric**: Summons Cara and Bronnen to address their actions with the Mor’Fang and prepares them for the Council of Druids.
- **Ohjan and Mor’Sovra**: Bronnen’s parents who discuss the bonding of the families and guide Cara’s integration into the Hularen traditions.
- **Orla**: An elderly seer who issues cryptic warnings about drumbeats, blood, and falling.
- **Conarok (Druid) and Baeloc (Earthbear)**: Serve as escorts to Emric’s grove, revealing more about the Mother’s touch and Earthbears.
- **Seul Entity**: A mysterious, shadowy figure demanding Cara’s blood for unclear but urgent purposes.
- **Mawdra**: Indirectly involved through the delivery of the glyph-inscribed amulet to Cara via the Gorhund hounds.

---

### **Objectives and Goals:**
1. **Prepare for the Council of Druids**: Cara and Bronnen must attend the Circle of Nine Moons, where their fates will be determined due to their actions in reforging the Mor’Fang.
2. **Understand the Mother’s Influence**: Cara must unravel the mystery of why the Mother and other forces are acting through her and her companions.
3. **Maintain Secrecy**: Cara must keep the amulet, the Mother’s plans, and the Seul’s visit hidden until further clarity is provided.
4. **Forge an Alliance with the Empire**: Cara crafts terms for peace and collaboration between Woodhome and the Hulean Empire, balancing loyalty to her people and her roots in the Empire.
5. **Strengthen Bonds with Family and Fey**: Cara continues integrating into Hularen culture while managing relationships with her parents, Bronnen, and the Gorhund.

---

### **Notable Events:**
1. **Orla’s Prophecy**: The seer cryptically warns of drumbeats, blood, and many who will fall.
2. **Encounter with Emric at the Pool of the Mother**:
   - Cara and Bronnen are told they are summoned to the Circle of Nine Moons for judgment.
   - Emric questions Cara about reforging the Mor’Fang and reveals the Mother’s presence in both Cara and Bronnen.
3. **Seul’s Demand for Blood**:
   - Cara is forced to comply with the shadowy figure’s orders to send her blood, hinting at darker forces at play.
4. **Yur’teen Ceremony**:
   - A ritualistic celebration of Cara’s return, bonding to Bronnen, and the unity of the families, marked by heightened spiritual connection.
5. **The Amulet’s Disappearance**:
   - The Mother’s plans and secrecy surround the glyph-inscribed medallion, which vanishes despite its importance.
6. **Pixen’s Message**:
   - A tiny fey confirms the Mother’s intention to keep the amulet and its significance secret until the Harvest Moon.
7. **Letter from Arch Bishop Sandlin**:
   - Cara receives instructions for her next journey and answers questions about Woodhome’s mindset and alliances.

Cara’s journey intensifies with the Mother’s influence, growing political tensions, and mysterious forces demanding her compliance. Balancing her loyalties and uncovering hidden truths becomes increasingly critical.

Read the D&D 5e description for the Zone of Prayer. Based on the description, create a prayer for my fictional D&D character, Cara, who is a Priestess of Porthios: You create a magical zone that guards against deception in a 15-foot-radius sphere centered on a point of your choice within range. Until the spell ends, a creature that enters the spell's area for the first time on a turn or starts its turn there must make a Charisma saving throw. On a failed save, a creature can't speak a deliberate lie while in the radius. You know whether each creature succeeds or fails on its saving throw.

An affected creature is aware of the spell and can thus avoid answering questions to which it would normally respond with a lie. Such creatures can be evasive in its answers as long as it remains within the boundaries of the truth.
Show Attribute List
Attributes
Zone of Truth
2 Enchantment
Casting Time: 1 action
Range: 60 feet
Target: A 15-foot-radius sphere centered on a point of your choice within range
Components: V S
Duration: 10 minutes
Classes: Bard, Cleric, Paladin
You create a magical zone that guards against deception in a 15-foot-radius sphere centered on a point of your choice within range. Until the spell ends, a creature that enters the spell’s area for the first time on a turn or starts its turn there must make a Charisma saving throw. On a failed save, a creature can’t speak a deliberate lie while in the radius. You know whether each creature succeeds or fails on its saving throw.
An affected creature is aware of the spell and can thus avoid answering questions to which it would normally respond with a lie. Such a creature can be evasive in its answers as long as it remains within the boundaries of the truth.

### **Prayer for the Zone of Prayer**

*Priestess Cara kneels, placing her hands upon the ground as a soft glow of power begins to emanate from her fingertips. She speaks with a voice clear and resolute, calling upon the power of Porthios.*

---

**"O Storm Lord, Keeper of Winds and Guardian of Truth,**  
I invoke Your name in this sacred moment,  
Let the currents of honesty blow freely in this space.  
Strike down deceit with the force of Your thunderous voice,  
Illuminate falsehoods with the lightning of Your justice.  

Within this circle, let no shadow of lies remain,  
No veil of treachery hide the wicked intent.  
Guide our words to echo only sincerity,  
And hold us to the unyielding honor of Your storms.  

May all who stand in this light know Your gaze upon them,  
And may Your storm rage against all who would betray.  
Porthios, Stormbringer, bless this zone with Your eternal truth.  
By Your tempest’s breath, so let it be."  

---

*As Cara completes the prayer, the area glows faintly with a radiant blue hue, and the storm's faint rumble can be felt in the air, a sign of Porthios' presence.*

[ASSISTANT]
Here is a prayer tailored for Cara, a Priestess of Porthios, invoking divine authority and truth to align with the Zone of Truth spell:

---

**Prayer of Porthios’ Light**  
*"Stormlord, hear your servant’s call. In your name, let no shadow conceal the truth."*  

O Porthios, Stormbringer, Guardian of Honor,  
I call upon your unwavering light,  
To pierce the veils of falsehood,  
And anchor truth within this sacred space.  

Let your thunderous will resound here,  
Shaking the hearts of the deceitful,  
Breaking the chains of treachery.  
By your power, let no lie be spoken,  
And no truth be twisted in your sight.  

As the storm cannot be hidden by clouds,  
Let clarity reign in your hallowed presence.  
Grant me your wisdom to discern what is veiled,  
And the strength to uphold what is revealed.  

This I ask, with heart steadfast and purpose clear,  
That your justice be done,  
And your voice heard in this realm.  

*"By the storm, by the truth, by the light of Porthios, so let it be."*

--- 

This prayer can be spoken as part of casting **Zone of Truth** to invoke the divine presence of Porthios and align Cara’s spellcasting with her role as his priestess.
