Read the following journal entry for my D&D character, Cara. Create a list of important items, locations, names, objectives and events. Each list should be a separate category. Include a summary of the of the journal entry: 8th of Solik, 2324 IC 8th of Solik, 2324 IC. Stonehill, Father Aladin Bodin’s Home, Travaghn & Ilyrian 

Wake, dress, and tell Bronnen the dream I had. As I describe the house, Bronnen says it is his grandfather’s house. I have not been inside the house yet so I couldn’t know what I know. Bronnen is acting odd.
I pray before checking the scroll cases. There is a response from Arch Druid Sandlin which reads:
“If you need this person, then acquire them by whatever means necessary. The law is a guideline. Do what you must. Try not to cause an incident between the church and the Empire there. Return to Travaghn after. Do not be late.”
Bronnen and I eat breakfast together. Bronnen is still acting oddly. I ask him if he also dreamed last night and he says he did. 
Bronnen’s Dream:
“I don’t think it came from Porthios, Cara, and it wasn’t pleasant. The dream was long. I was fighting in a war. There was a lot of death. There were 20 in my war band and they were all people I knew and the people I knew were dying. I think it was the memory of an ancient one and I think the Mother sent the dream.
Bronnen quotes in Ancient Hularen and then translates, “We will bathe in the blood of our enemies until we have no blood left to bleed, for that is all that is left to do. We will slay all that breathe and walk, all that infest our home. We will become the nightmare so that others can find the dawn.”
“The full dream spanned 5 weeks long. 5 weeks in a single night.”
Bronnen holds out his hand and when I take it, I feel a pulse and get a terrible vision: screaming, pain, death, darkness, and fire. Sheer terror and hell. I see eyes popping out, intestines spilling from bodies, faces clawed off, bodies ripped apart. Bronnen’s dream was a nightmare. I jerk my hand away. The pulse felt like the Mother but different, forceful instead of light, and fleeting.
We finish breakfast and clean up. We walk back to the barracks after locking up behind us. It’s cold and windy. We approach the guardsmen, and I ask to speak to the Marshall. A runner is sent to request an audience and minutes later, we are waved over. A guardsman who is 6’2” and bearded lets us in past the gate. Inside, there are even more soldiers today. I see one man in black plate head straight for us. There are a number of black plate armored men in here – Dragon Guard. The man that approaches us asks why we are here.
“I am Cara Yornlin, Priestess of Porthios, and I have come to act as Judiscar to prisoner Silas Shevarn. Arch Bishop Sandlin expects us to return by tomorrow at the latest.”
Another man, older with grey hair and wearing Imperial armor walks up. The silver etchings on his armor mark him as being from Travaghn. He is in his late 50s or early 60s and his closely shaved, mostly white hair still has patches of brown.
He introduces himself, “I am High Commander Landross. The Militant Commanders report to me that includes Militant Commander Yornlin. I should send you home to Iron Hill. If you are there, your father is more likely to return.”
High Commander Landross walks us into the closest room and we talk while we wait. Close to 10 minutes pass before Marshall Greeland looks up from his desk and motions us forward. 
“Silas Shevarn is here and is being held for 9 counts of murder.”
“As a Porthion Priestess, I will act as Judiscar for Silas Shivarn. A Zone of Truth will prove one way or another whether his actions resulted in 9 counts of murder or if his actions were permissible under Hulean Imperial Law.”
Marshall Greeland and High Commander Landross look at one another and then step out of the room. Bronnen and I wait alone in Marshall Greeland’s office for almost 20 minutes. As we sit and wait, I feel the scroll case vibrate twice, one almost immediately following the other. They read:
“High Commander Landross – be very careful. Very powerful ally and equally powerful enemy if upset. I confirmed you were sent there to Stonehill and that we, the church, need Silas Shivarn. Be gentle of speech and leave in good standing.”
“Cara, answer me now.”
Before I can respond or even burn the notes, we hear the door open. I have just enough time to put the notes back in the scroll case. High Commander Landross walks back in and sits very close to me, studying me. High Marshall Greeland returns to his seat at his desk and watches me closely. A third man walks in and he, too, watches me.
“How old are you, Yornlin,” High Commander Landross asks.
“I am 19 years old, High Commander.”
“Does your father know you left Travaghn? Does he know where you are, what you have been doing?”
“Papa knows I left Travaghn, High Commander, but I do not know if he knows where I have been or what I have been doing. I have tried contacting him many times, but he is busy fighting orc at the Citadel, or was.”
He studies me intently. All three men do and the silence stretches on until High Commander Landross breaks it.
“If you can prove he’s (Silas) not a murderer, you can take him to Travaghn.” High Commander nods at the 3rd man before returning his gaze to me, “You will answer that man’s questions. He’s an agent of the Empire and will report back to the Lord Emperor.”
I look over at the 3rd man and watch as 3 more men in black armor file in behind him. The Agent of the Empire is 5’10” tall and has black hair. He looks like an ordinary dock worker or livery man, but I know he’s not. Marshall Greeland and High Commander Landross stand up and leave the room. The Agent of the Empire asks a barrage of questions. He focuses on Papa’s dereliction of duty and abandoning his post at the Citadel after the war with the black orc to search for Mama’s missing body. He also focuses on the death of Mama. He’s cruel but effective, inciting emotional responses to detect any dark infection (corruption) but Bronnen and I are not infected with corruption and we pass this test. The Agent of the Empire and the 3 men that came with him leave Marshall Greeland’s study. 
Bronnen and I also leave the study and walk out into the yard, careful to stay out of the soldiers’ way. After a few minutes in the cold, brisk air, Bronnen hears movement in Marshall Greeland’s office. We return and find him behind his desk. He looks up and tells us that a guard will accompany us down below ground to the cells to speak with Silas. 
When we are downstairs, I walk over close to the bars of the cell Silas is being held in, careful to stay back out of arm’s reach.
“Silas Shivarn, I am Cara Yornlin, Priestess of Porthios and I have been sent by Arch Bishop Sandlin to act as your Judiscar. Do you understand my purpose?”
Silas looks at me, stands up from the stool he was sitting on, and walks over to the bars of his cell to get a better look.
“You’re a wee sprite of a thing, naught much more than a girl,” Silas says, his accent thick and unrefined marking him as being from the East. 
Some of his words are clipped and show a lack for formal education. His stance is relaxed, and his voice is gruff but not hard or cold or filled with anger. There are wrinkles at the corners of his eyes and mouth – a man whose smile reaches his eyes. I smile at him because I like him. 
“I am young, yes, but I am also capable and qualified to perform the duties and responsibilities of a Porthion Judiscar. I am more than I appear, Silas. I will perform a Zone of Truth – are you familiar with this prayer?”
“Aye, I am familiar,” Silas responds, his shrewd eyes dancing.
“The guard will remain as a witness to the testimony you give and the answers you give to the questions I ask. The Zone of Truth will ensure you do not lie. I implore you, Silas, to answer my questions as refusing to answer my questions will be considered as an attempt to deceive or evade the truth. As Judiscar, there must be no doubt as to your guilt or innocence. It is important, Silas, as you will only be released into my custody and care if you are found innocent of the crimes you are accused of. Do you understand?”
The twinkle leaves his eyes and Silas stands up straight. 
“Aye, Priestess, I understand. If you say I’m innocent, I go with you.”
“Yes. If I, by Hulean Imperial Law, find you innocent of the crimes for which you stand accused, you will be released into my care and custody. I will take you somewhere safe where you will no longer be hunted. If I find you guilty, you will remain here and await your execution for murder. Do you understand?”
“Aye, Priestess. Say your prayer, ask your questions, I’ll answer them.”
I look from Silas to Bronnen and then the guard before bowing my head and praying in Celestial for the Zone of Truth invocation.
(Add prayer for Zone of Truth)
To prove that the Zone of Truth is active and in place, I first ask the guard a number of simple questions instructing him to answer the first truthfully, to try refuse to answer the second, and to then try to answer falsely on the third. He does as I ask and is satisfied that the Zone of Truth is in place. I do the same with Bronnen so he may also experience what the prayer feels like. Then, I turn my attention to Silas. During the 10 minute interrogation, Silas answers all my questions and even volunteers relevant information. I keep the topic narrow, focusing on the crimes he is currently being held for: 9 counts of murder. 
Silas admits to being part of the bandit raiding party that stopped and attacked a merchant wagon traveling North from Aletherin (Far Port) to Lehn’s Port. The bandits expected to take their typical haul: food goods, small items to sell or trade, weapons or clothing, jewelry and coin. What he and his group did not expect was that the escort with the caravan were trained mercenaries. This was unusual and indicated that the cargo being moved was valuable, necessitating professional guards. What Silas and his group did not expect was for the mercenary guards to fight so violently and fiercely to protect the cargo. Silas expected a fight, but not death, if it could be avoided. They were bandits, not murderers, until the moment they found themselves fighting for their lives. 
Silas and his group prevailed but not without losses and when the dust settled, they had killed 8 mercenaries and the wagon driver. When they uncovered the cargo in the wagon, they found 8 crates of black lotus, 20 stone per crate. That is 160 stone-worth of black lotus, illegal to buy, sell, or trade, or transport within the border of Hule by Hulean Imperial Law. Silas’s companions fled the scene, but Silas remained behind intent on destroying the black lotus. He poured flasks of oil on the crates, topped them all with dried wood and grass he collected from near the road, and then set it all ablaze. 
Silas’s words all ring with truth. There is no hesitation, no attempt to evade or leave out bits of information. He speaks calmly, giving as much detail about the event in question as he can, the memory of that day seared in his mind. After that day, Silas tried to reform his life. He left the bandits, moved far away, and took another name. He lived a quiet life, carving wooden items that he sold and traded but his deeds followed him in the form of Judiscar intent on finding Silas and executing him for murder. 
I consider Silas’s account before rendering a decision on his guilt or innocence. My contemplation is not necessary, I know Hulean Imperial Law, but I let the silence fill the cells for several heartbeats. 
“Had the cargo been legal, Silas, I would find you guilty by Hulean Imperial Law of 9 counts of murder, rampant banditry, and willful and criminal destruction of property. If this were the case, I would carry out your execution myself. However, Hulean Imperial Law is clear on the manufacturing, possession, transport, trade, and selling of the illegal substance known as black lotus. The cargo being transported in Hule along Hulean roads was illicit and illegal by Hulean Imperial law. The mercenaries guarding the cargo and the driver transporting the cargo were committing crimes against the Hulean Empire and its people. The merchant who secured the services of the mercenaries and driver and who procured the black lotus paid to have it transported under armed guard was actively committing a crime against Hule and the Hulean people and whether he is known or not, is culpable. As such, by Hulean Imperial Law, the deaths of the 8 mercenary guards and the driver, though perhaps avoidable, were justified. 
“As a Priestess of Porthios and serving in my capacity as Judiscar for the Hulean Empire and representative of Porthios’s judgment and justice, I find you not guilty of 9 counts of murder. If you agree to serve the Porthion Church and leave with me in my custody and care, you will be released immediately. Do you agree to these terms, Silas Shivarn?”
“Serve the Porthion Church?” I watch Silas consider this for a moment before nodding his head, “Aye, Priestess Cara, I agree. I’ve done many things in my life; this will be a new experience.”
I smile and nod at the guard to unlock Silas’s cell. When Silas walks out and stands next to me, I can take his full measure. He towers over me at 6’4” tall and is built like an old grizzly bear. We collect Silas’s personal affects, and he changes into his own clothes before we walk upstairs together, Bronnen and I in front followed by Silas and the guard. Upstairs, a Corporal escorts us to the front gate and Silas is given a Writ of Freedom stamped with the Hulean Imperial Seal. 
We go straight to Father Bodin’s home saying nothing. I unlock the gate and then lock it behind us once we are through. We walk silently and quickly across the small courtyard to the door. I unlock the door and let us inside, locking the door behind us as soon as we are inside. I smile at Silas.
“You must be hungry. I’ll fix you something to eat,” I say as I point to the dining table and walk into the kitchen. A few minutes later, I bring out a platter filled with a selection of meats, sausages, cheeses, fruit and bread. Then I bring out a pitcher wine and a jug of water. I sit across from him at the table as he eats.
“There is something unusual about you Silas. You can do something that no one else can do,” I say.
Silas looks up and brushes the side of his nose with a finger.
“I get this feelin’, Priestess. When something or someone is “off,” I get this feelin’. I can’t quite explain it, I’ve always had it, as long as I can remember. I can smell the bad on others before they get too close. It’s not really a smell, you see, but more of a feelin’, a tinglin’, an itchin’. The older I got, the further away I can smell when something or someone is off. At first, miles away, then a day or two. If trouble is headin’ my way, it gives me time to get away or prepare for what’s comin’. I can see ghosts, too. There are some in here, Priestess.”
“Cara,” I say, “You can call me Cara.”
“Alright, Cara. What’s next? What am I to do for the Porthion church?”
“Next, a bath, Silas. We can discuss the rest later.”
I show Silas to the bathing room and to a bedroom he can while we are here. After Silas bathes, he comes back downstairs to mend the holes in his socks. As he works, his head comes up.
“There’s something out there, Cara,” Silas says, pointing in a direction. 
I walk to a window and look out, searching. Across the way in a neighboring house, I see Yi’kar staring back. 
“Bronnen, he’s waiting for me and the stone.”
Bronnen reluctantly agrees to trade the bit of stone to Yi’kar for my mother. We start to walk to the house together to meet Yi’kar but I hear his voice in my head.
“You go forward, the rest remain there.”
I repeat Yi’kar’s words to Bronnen.
“No,” Bronnen replies and gestures for me to continue on.
We take a few more steps when I hear Yi’kar’s voice in my head a second time, “If I wanted you harmed, I would have done so. I don’t want to kill your friends.”
I repeat his words to Bronnen and we stop and talk. Bronnen finally agrees to hold back so I can go on alone to speak with Yi’kar. I walk across the street, through the open gate, and into the open door. Inside the front room, a fire is burning and two children are frozen in play. A man sits in one chair frozen in place, pipe in his hand with a curl of smoke hanging still in midair. A woman sits in another chair, darning the sleeve of a shirt, needle and thread suspended in the air. I close the door to keep out the cold.
Yi’kar holds out his hand. I walk up to him, place my hand in his, and we disappear, reappearing in a second story bedroom somewhere else. On a bed is a fine map beautifully detailed and masterfully rendered. 
“Your father is currently searching for your mother in Branlen. Your mother is hidden at the edge of town. Her body will be found without wounds, dead but not undead. The men guarding her, his men, will be found confused but unharmed,” Yi’kar explains.
I pull out the small chunk of Mor’Fang and help him affix it to a staff binding it in place with leather thongs. Yi’kar shows me an image of someone moving so very fast, leaping across roofs. The figure looks in through a window at 4 sleeping men and Papa. The figure is Mama. I watch her climb through an open window and into an empty bedroom. She moves silently, opens the bedroom door and slams it shut, waking Papa and the men with him. Yi’kar releases her and I hear her fall. The vision goes black.
I look up at Yi’kar and smile, tears of gratitude swimming in my eyes. He kept her safe. Mama’s dead but he kept her safe and kept her from the enemy and now she’s returned to us, returned to Papa who will have her resurrected. Yi’kar disappears and I walk out of the house, closing the door behind me. I walk back to Bronnen and Silas and we return to Father Bodin’s house. I lock the gate and once the door to the house is locked behind us, I explain what happened. 
With Mama safely returned to Papa, the bit of stone given to Yi’kar, and Silas in our custody, we decide not to stay the night at Father Bodin’s house. We gather up our gear and packs and travel to Travaghn using the portal. Bronnen, Silas, and I appear in another circle in a round room – the correct round room, the teleportation circle outside of Travaghn. We walk up the ramp and answer the Dragon Guard’s questions about who we are and why we are here and Silas presents his Imperial Writ of Freedom. 
Bronnen, Silas, and I take a wagon from the main gate to the Porthion Temple on 2nd Tier. About 3/4s of the way through 1st Tier, the wagon stops and a hooded figure in a brown cloak approaches the wagon. Under the hood, I see a half-Elven face. He knows my name and I confirm who I am. He nods at someone and sits up front with the driver. We continue on but instead of taking us to the Porthion Temple, the wagon moves away from the Temple District and toward the Merchant District. We pass through the Merchant District and into the Housing District where the Guild Leaders houses are and where the Merchant Guards are posted. 
The wagon stops at a large house and drives around to the side of the house. The cloaked half-Elf opens the door, looks at me and says, “My benefactor awaits you.”
Bronnen looks dubious and suspicious but Silas doesn’t react. He doesn’t feel anything bad, so we climb out of the wagon and follow the half-Elf to a servant’s door. A maid answers the knock and calls the half-Elf Jeneroc. 
“Fetch Senechal Kobrin,” Jeneroc tells the maid. 
5 minutes later, a man in green and gold livery comes to the servant’s door. Kobrin is in his early 40s, has a neat, trim beard, and shoulder-length hair. The insignia on Senechal Kobrin shows the Silk Guild. He motions us to come inside and we follow him inside through a huge kitchen, down a hallway, through a door and into an inner courtyard. We walk across the courtyard and through a door on the far side, and down a series of steps, 3 stories down into a very large room filled with hundreds of bottles of wine which goes two stories up. 
Senechal Kobrin does a very Hularen thing: he breaks bread, dipping it in salt. If that wasn’t enough, he speaks to Bronnen and I in Hularen. 
“I am Seras Kolfass. I was told to bring you here,” he explains.
Bronnen glances at me and offers, “The Kolfass family – Kolfass means cut fast), live in the North (of Woodhome).”
Seras Kolfass continues, “You have been summoned home, the two of you. I will arrange transportation to the wood. The Druids and Ohjan have summoned you home and you must go tonight. You must arrive one hour before dark at the livery of the Dented Cup.”
Seras Kolfass escorts up back to the servant’s door and out. The wagon is gone. Bronnen, Silas and I walk to the Porthion Temple and inside the sanctuary. It is empty. I sit in a pew and pray, waiting for an acolyte or priest to walk into the sanctuary. After about 15 minutes of prayer, a priest approaches us. I recognize him and he escorts all three of us below to Arch Bishop Sandlin’s study. He is inside sitting behind his desk furiously writing. 4 chairs are lined up on the other side of his desk when normally there are only 2. He stops writing long enough to motion to the chairs. Bronnen, Silas and I walk over quietly to the chairs and sit down. 
“Hello Carathul, Bronnen Gorhund, and Silas Shivarn. Would you mind terribly if I spoke alone with Cara for a little while?” Arch Bishop Sandlin asks though it is not really a question. 
Bronnen considers for a moment before nodding. I watch as he and Silas walk out of the Arch Bishop’s study and close the door behind them. A minute later, the Hulean Imperial Scribe walks in and sits down. 
“The Lord Emperor will no longer tolerate secrets from you, Cara,” the Arch Bishop says.
I tell the Arch Bishop what has happened the past few days. I do not name the Mother but I do speak of the “Corrupted She.”
“Cara, your loyalty is suspect, and the Lord Emperor does not trust you. I have taught you better than this. I expect better of you,” Arch Bishop Sandlin chastises me.  
The Imperial Scribe leaves Arch Bishop Sandlin’s study leaving us alone together. He talks about the Hularens and tells me what he and the Lord Emperor know about them.
“Porthios has told both the Lord Emperor and I not to delve into their old gods. You need to bring a message from the Lord Emperor, Cara: Allies must reciprocate trust. We must agree to terms and be confident of intent. Woodhome should not confuse the Lord Emperor’s willingness for peace as an unwillingness to protect Porthios’s people.”
We speak of Bronnen (Elkin), Silas and Roland. 
“The Lord Emperor wants Roland returned to the Empire to be held accountable for his crimes but he is willing to allow Roland to remain in your custody until he is no longer needed for Porthios’s purposes.”
Arch Bishop Sandlin says that at some point we will need to return to the ruin near Havershire to get the shard Jeggred and I sealed up. 
“Olen Marwood will be close by at a new fortress being built on the Torc. He will have with him a case you can use for the shard.”
Our conversation is cut short by Lord Emperor Greyhawk’s voice. I turn around and see him in the Arch Bishop’s study, standing near the fire. He’s dressed in a blue, black, and silver tunic, black breeches, and black boots. He proceeds to tell me what I will and will not do. I remain silent as he speaks. He is furious.
“Woodhome is a powerful beast and we don’t know on which side she’ll fight,” the Arch Bishop says.
The Lord Emperor leaves Arch Bishop Sandlin’s study the same way he appeared, magically. The Arch Bishop finally sends me off to speak with High Priestess Sharin in her study up in one of the towers. She looks so very old now, like she’s aged 10 years in the last 6 months. Her white hair is down and she’s wrapped in a thick, heavy blanket and sitting in front of a roaring fire. She smiles at me when I walk in. I make her some tea. 
In her left hand she holds a silver Lieutenant’s braid. On a nearby table is a scroll with the Imperial Seal and a blue silk ribbon with black edges – it is a bereavement scroll for a fallen soldier. It is for one of her grandsons. He was in the 2nd and died leaving behind a wife and 2 children.
I hand her my 3 journals, and it takes her an hour to read them. She looks at me.
“Get me Sarmain’s journals where he found one of the dark shards 193 years ago. You cannot, you won’t find it. This information was lost because he did not write it down. You need to include far more detail, Cara. We have taught you better and there is no excuse. One day, perhaps years from now, a girl just like you who is facing difficult choices may need to read your journals and learn from you.”
“There are things I cannot write, Sharin. Porthios says there are things that must remain secret.”
Sharin points to a bookshelf and tells me how to find the hidden bookshelf behind it. I find a catalogue of books numbered 1-37. 
“Bring over book 37. Open it and tell me what you see.”
“It is an empty journal.”
Sharin smiles, “Place your hand on the cover and recite the Canticle Prayer.”
I do as she says, reciting the canticle.
“Good. Now open the book. This book, 37, is your Book of Secrets and only you and I can open it.”
I close the book and put it back on the hidden bookshelf. Sharin tells me of the Baylorn – undead spirits of Elves. 
“The Baylorn are good, Cara. Not all undead are evil and the Baylorn is one such.  I have guidance for you, Cara. The shards should not be returned to the Empire or taken to Woodhome. They must be taken to the woods near the Fire Mountain and nowhere else. Once you have one, it must be taken directly there – no exceptions. ‘Those who come before you leave a path you must follow. It is my job to mark the path.’”
Before I leave, High Priestess Sharin gives ma an anklet or a bracelet made of bone. It is ancient and yellowed and caved into it are tiny Hularen symbols and the runes are carved into tiny scales (bracelet of NoWhere).
“Tell no one in the church that you have it. Put it on and never take it off, Cara. It belongs to you.”
She watches me closely as I remove my right boot and pull the anklet over my foot until it rests on my ankle. The bone is tight and inflexible and painful to put on, but I manage and pull my boot back on. 
I leave High Priestess Sharin’s study and then lead Bronnen and Silas out of the church. We walk to the Dented Cup on 1st Tier. At the gate, Silas gets a feeling about one of the guards – the one sitting next to a barrel with an apple in one hand and a long, thin Elven knife in the other. He has black hair and is carving columns into the apple like it is a building. The irises of his eyes are almost black. He looks bored but watchful. He wears a dark blue short sleeved tunic, brown breeches, and boots. He’s muscular but athletic and with a fair complexion. He looks normal. 
I quickly sketch the man and send his likeness and a brief explanation to the Arch Bishop using the scroll case. We wait at the livery almost 20 minutes for a reply, not wanting to walk into a trap. The scroll case vibrates and I pull out a short message from Arch Bishop Sandlin. 
“This man is Shar, one of the Emperor’s elite and a Shadow Dragon. A good person to go to if you are in trouble and have access to him.”
A man with reddish-brown hair and goatee walks over to us. He says quietly in Hularen that we are early. 
Bronnen nods, “Our business is done, I thought it best to be early.”
The man nods and leads us to our horses. Our escort is one of 2 Hularens who are well-built men and probably warriors. Bronnen tells them that Silas is coming with us. They don’t argue but they don’t look pleased as they get Silas a horse. We ride through 1st Tier and out the gate. We ride along the Southern by-road toward Silver Lake. We ride until dark and get to a copse of tree where we unsaddle the horses. 2 druids step out from the trees. One creates a mist while the other opens a tree portal for us to walk through. When we step through, we walk into a wood and a small campsite near a campfire. Silas immediately pulls his knives loose.
“Something’s here,” Silas warns.
Two trees step forward – Ents. Out of the woods step more Hularen men and 4 hounds. One of the men is Ohjan and he is flanked by 4 Gorhund wardens.
“Put your knives away, Silas. We know them. We are safe,” I say.
“We will move swiftly, now,” Ohjan says quickly and quietly. 
The druids create another tree portal. Ohjan whistles and the hounds charge through first. We step through into a clearing which is 30 yards in diameter with 3 fires burning bright around the tree we step through. 
“What is wrong?” Bronnen asks his father as we walk swiftly past the fires. 
Across from the tree portal we see a line of druids, wardens, hounds, forest guardians, and Awoken trees. There are 40 people here watching who comes through the tree portal, ready to kill anything that comes through and shouldn’t. Ohjan says nothing.
“Bormarr is here,” Bronnen says, his concern tinging his words.
Ohjan nods and stays silent, turning to watch the tree portal.
“Father, what is wrong?” Bronnen asks again.
“Reach out to Bormarr, my son, and you can tell me if something is amiss or not,” Ohjan instructs.
“There is nothing here, Father.”
Ohjan instructs all watching the portal tree to watch it until morning to ensure nothing comes through that shouldn’t. We follow Ohjan as he walks through the glade.
“Some time back, a dor’ja’mar came through a portal into the wood. A dor’ja’mar, Cara, is a dead mage or dead wizard (lich) and it found its way into the wood. It followed a traveler through the tree portal, crossed paths with Spriggens and killed a number of them. A surviving Spriggen alerted the Wardens. The lich was destroyed at Hier’holt, North of here, near Thornwall. The dor’ja’mar was not Hularen. It killed 12,” Ohjan explains.
We walk back to Ilyrian and to Ohjan and Sovra’s home. The large outdoor table is almost full of people. Mor’Sovra greets us and I am surprised to see Mama and Papa here. I run to them and wrap them both in strong hugs before introducing them both to Bronnen.
I look to Ohjan and he answers my unspoken question, “Isharahn Gorhund, a warrior and druid, discretely followed your father and brought him and your mother here to Ilyrian where they beseeched the Mother to return your mother to us.”
I am so very happy. Mama, Papa, Bronnen and I exchange stories after introducing Silas as the newest key. Silas is shown to a home where he may stay, and food is brought to him. When telling our story, I do not say the Wind Mother’s name, or her title and I do not speak of Sanctuary. Bronnen speaks around Sanctuary, too, saying it is a truth we know but not one we own.
The Arch Druids have requested to see Mama and Papa. Ohjan asks my parents to stay for a few days, a week, preferably. Ohjan wants to try and reinforce peace between Woodhome and the Empire using my marriage to Bronnen. Papa says he and Mama can stay in Woodhome for a week. While the Gorhund family takes a walk together to speak privately, Mama, Papa, and I talk to one another.
When the Gorhund return, Bronnen comes back and invited my father to hunt with him. Papa accepts. Eladia walks over to me, a concerned look on her face.
“Something is wrong with Sarana. The journey took a toll, and she slipped into a coma. We brought her home and we are taking care of her but she has not woken up in nine days,” Eladia says. 
I go upstairs and find Sarana in her room. She looks so peaceful. I sit down on the edge of the bed, hold her hand and talk to her. I tell her everything I told my parents and Bronnen’s family outside. I don’t even hear Eladia walk in behind me but when I fall silent, she speaks.
“The ghost Bronnen sent her to find was not a ghost but an Orb of the Spirits in Serenathall, an Elven ruin. Sarana was drawn to it. We fought orc and undead and orc again. She went to sleep the day after she picked up the orb which is filled with ghosts. The Arch Druids want to see you and Bronnen, Cara. That’s unusual. 
That night, I do not dream.

### Summary of the Journal Entry

Cara recounts a series of important events, interactions, and revelations across Stonehill, Travaghn, and Ilyrian. She helps free Silas Shivarn from charges of murder using her role as Judiscar, demonstrating her ability to navigate Hulean Imperial law and her commitment to justice. After securing Silas, she meets with powerful figures like the Arch Bishop Sandlin and Emperor Greyhawk, gaining insights into political tensions and divine mysteries. Cara also reunites with her resurrected mother and father in Ilyrian, strengthening familial ties and celebrating with the Gorhund family. However, the mystery of Sarana’s coma introduces a new thread of danger and intrigue tied to an Orb of Spirits.

### Important Items

- **Small Chunk of Mor’Fang**: A shard given to Yi’kar to secure Cara's mother’s return.
- **Imperial Writ of Freedom**: Document proving Silas’s exoneration.

- **Orb of the Spirits**: An artifact linked to Sarana’s coma, filled with spirits and connected to Serenathall.
- **Hidden Journal (Book of Secrets)**: A personal journal accessible only by Cara and High Priestess Sharin.
- **Bone Staff with Mor’Fang Fragment**: Crafted for Yi’kar as part of their bargain.

- **Stonehill**: Father Bodin’s home and the starting point of Cara’s journey.
- **Travaghn**: The political and religious center where Cara interacts with Arch Bishop Sandlin and Emperor Greyhawk.
- **Serenathall**: An Elven ruin connected to the Orb of the Spirits.
- **Ilyrian**: The Gorhund family’s home and a sanctuary for Cara's family.
- **Hier’holt**: The site of a recent battle with a lich near Thornwall.
- **Portal Clearing**: A defensive outpost where druids and guardians repel threats through the tree portals.

- **Mor’Sovra**: Bronnen’s mother and matriarch of the Gorhunds.

- **Investigate Sarana’s Coma**: Determine the effects of the Orb of the Spirits and help Sarana recover.
- **Prepare for Marriage**: Align familial and political approval for Cara and Bronnen’s union.

Read the following journal entry for my D&D character, Cara. Create a list of important items, locations, names, objectives and events. Each list should be a separate category. Include a summary of the of the journal entry: 7th of Solik, 2324 IC. Stonehill

Wake, dress, and pray. I walk downstairs and cook breakfast, cleaning up as I work. Bronnen comes downstairs and calls me over to a window. I walk over and look out to see Father Bodin and Father Gayluss outside holding their holy symbols aloft. There are burnt bodies all around them on the ground.
“They weren’t there last night,” Bronnen says.
I walk over to the front door, but it’s locked, not with a key but with magic, and I cannot open it. I try to open the windows, but they won’t open, either. None of them. Bronnen and I are locked inside Father Bodin’s home. I walk back into the kitchen and finish preparing breakfast. I set the table and bring out the food and kafir. Moments later, Father Bodin and Father Gayluss come inside.
“The wards took care of the attackers,” Father Bodin confirms. “Two of the bodies were Adonis: highly skilled killers who practice the Dance (of Death). They are from the Western Islands, West of Rustin. They do not employ their skills for coin so finding two here should give us all pause. I will travel West to gather information and see if the Asha’kari have infiltrated the Adonis or if they are potential allies. The other men with him were all Rustani.”
After we eat, I give Father Bodin 3 sketches I drew of him, Greyhawk before he was emperor and king, and Porthios before he ascended. Father Bodin has something for me, too. He gives me a scroll case almost identical to the one Arch Bishop Sandlin gave me. He also hands me a piece of paper detailing names and their cyphers. The names of contacts and their corresponding locations include: Aletherin, Treetop, Travaghn, Southmarch, Stonehill, Northmarch, the Solarian Vale, Lehn’s Port, and a few other places.  
“When you write the cyphered name on a piece of paper, your message will send to that person. You must be on this plane to send the message and the Great Wood is still a barrier,” Father Bodin instructs.
He then hands me a small leather pouch. Inside is a single key and a slip of paper.
“The pouch is heavily warded and attuned to two people: you and me. It opens only one lock, the front door to my home here in Stonehill. My home and everything in it is yours, Cara. Use it whenever you want,” Father Bodin tells me.
The slip of paper is marked with the runes needed to travel to the portal in his house from any other traveling circle as well as from the portal in his house to the traveling circle in Travaghn.
Father Bodin has something for Elkin (Bronnen), too: a pair of metal gloves with segmented claws. The gloves are Hularen.
“They were given to me to give back to the Hularens,” Father Bodin explains. The Sumarac had them. They were unearthed during an incursion of their lands in one of their old places. They are still enchanted.”
I clean up from breakfast and say goodbye to Father Bodin and Father Gayluss before they leave. Bronnen and I decide to stop at the Broken Fence first to check on Esthera and her kin. I lock up Father Bodin’s house and we walk to the Broken Fence. It’s very cold this morning. Owen is at the door and lets us inside. Lanerass Keln is behind the bar and Esthera comes out of the kitchen where she was baking bread. We greet one another as Owen resumes his station by the door. 
“The militia was called up when some of the city guard disappeared at the barracks along with the Acting Marshall,” Lannos tells us. “They came back about 4 hours later, some of them wounded. This was yesterday and we are still in the dark as to what happened or where they went. Kernos, the wheelwright, said that 3 caravans came into Stonehill over the last 3 weeks.”
Lanerass points to 2 men sitting in the tavern. One is older and, bald, and a bit dirty. 
“He owns the livery near South Gate. He can tell you who boarded horses in the last week or two. His name is Barly Pethmarr. He only drinks bitter ale,” Lanerass offers.
Barly Pethmarr looks to be in his 50s and has a sour expression on his face. Despite his tired appearance, he is clean shaven. He wears a leather apron over a grey tunic.
Next, we go speak to Acting Marshall Greeland and ask for him at the gate outside the barracks. We wait for about 15 minutes before we are let in. The yard is filled with soldiers and guardsmen carrying arrows and spears and checking armor. They are very busy. We are escorted by a Master Sargent and as we walk, I see 4 Corporals, 4 Sergeants, and 3 Lieutenants. There are way too many senior officers here in Stonehill, more than there should be for the size of town and the size of the barracks. We only had 2 Lieutenants in Iron Hill. Something is very off but it’s not the men or their uniforms. They are all in Stonehill colors and emblems, but their main armor is Imperial and there are some in 9th Legion armor. I also notice there are too many horses here for the livery.
We walk to a private room with the Master Sargeant. 
“I saw what happened on the Plains, North of the Great Wood. I was there and I witnessed what you did. What do you need, I am willing to help if I can,” he says. 
“Do you have a list of all the people who arrived or departed from Stonehill over the last 3 or 4 weeks, Master Sargeant?” I ask.
“2 caravans, 9 individual riders, 2 wagons, and 3 groups of riders arrived in Stonehill over the last month. One of those caravans has already headed South again and the other leaves tomorrow. Some of the riders have also already traveled back South, the rest are here for another 2 weeks. The wagons are non-guild merchants with small goods for trade. 3 bounty hunters arrived and turned over a prisoner, a bandit, who is currently being held in a prison cell. The rest who have come and gone from Stonehill were all replacement soldiers, guards, and a few couriers.”
“Who is the prisoner,” I ask.
“Silas Shivarn, also known as Silas the Serpent, has 9 counts of murder and 22 counts of highway robbery,” the Master Sargeant explains. “The bounty hunters were paid 2000 gold for his capture. He’s set to meet the Emperor’s justice in 3 days. Judiscar Tiberan Cardoss (Tiberon “the Terror”) requested to be at his execution.”
Judiscar Tiberan “the Terror” Cardoss is an expert manhunter and has been doggedly pursuing Silas Shivarn for decades. Silas has somehow always managed to escape capture, slipping away just before Tiberan can apprehend him. No matter how many times Silas has changed his name, his location, his appearance, staying on the right side of the law for years, Tiberan always manages to track him down and Silas evades him, disappearing days before Tiberan arrives.
“I would like to speak to the prisoner, please,” I request.
I am led down by another soldier. Behind a heavy oak door is Silas Shivarn.
“Silas? My name is Cara. I would like to hear your story if you are willing to tell it.”
“Don’t see no harm to it,” a man’s voice says. “I was born in the East, it’s no longer there. Theronvarn was the town, not too far North o’ Halegrove, a horse ride North o’ that. I was 12 or so when Theronvarn disappeared. That was 62 years ago (that makes him 74 years old). Bandits came along and killed everyone. Oh, 9 or 10 of us escaped. The bandits had magic an burned Theronvarn down. Hard t; breathe when you’re on fire, but you know that.”
I peak in the door wondering how he knows that I would know what it feels like to be on fire. Silas Shivarn has a white mustache and a long white beard.
“I’ve a way of knowin’ things, felt the burn. Can sense it, too. Since I was a wee one. I knew the bandits were comin’. I tried t’ warn my pa but he was in his cups an didn’t listen. Almost everyone died. My gran always said I was born with a gift. Don’t know ‘bout that but guess it’s true. I committed my crimes when I was young. Me and others didn’t run South with the survivors, we ran North. Me and 3 others ended up in the middle of nowhere. No water. No food. We was picked up by Tegarus Blackhorn. He was a bandit lord. Larissa made it a year and some months after hard use. One of our friends didn’t like it an Blackhorn killed ‘im. I stayed with Blackhorn for years until he and most of his crew were killed. 3 of us survived. One of the merchant guards from that caravan spied me an tol’ me t’ pick up them bodies, take a horse, an ride hard away.
“That’s what I did. I rode North cuz the merchant guard rode South. I kept up my banditin’. One day I spied 2 wagons with 9 guard. Me an my 4 attacked. The wagons carried lotus. We killed all 9 men. I had been drinkin’, see, an didn’t pay attention to my nose. Those 9 men were workin’ for someone else with a name. Posters showed up with my face on ‘em saying I had murdered them but not what they had done. One of the men we killed was some high-rank’s kin. 
“Well, I cashed in an moved West. Tiberan caught up to me twice. I found a little place, has a potato patch an’ carved wood. I’m a good wood carver. I sold toys, bowls, plates, spinnin’ wheels. If I could carve it, I sold it. Took the name Silas Carver an’ lived in Molin’s Valley for 35 years or such. All quiet ‘til one day 2 men come along and killed my apprentice, good boy he was, an I killed them two. 3 or 4 weeks later, men came lookin’ for me and I waited for ‘em. Tired of runnin’ I was and my lady didn’t look at me after I killed the other two. Afraid of me, she was, an I couldn’t bear it.”
Lord Thelain put a bounty of 10,000 gold on Silas’s head. Why would Lord Thelain, a Lord in the Vale, put a bounty on Silas for killing 9 men in the East more than 30 years ago who were trafficking in Black Lotus?
“My gift ran in the family. I never had children, so it dies wit’ me. One way or ‘nother, I’m leavin’ this cell. I smelt the darkness yesterday. It’s happened twice afore, once in Jaks Hill. What’s comin’ won’t be good,” he warns.
I promise Silas I will return in the morning, leave the cell, and return to Father Bodin’s home. I write an encrypted letter to Father Bodin telling him about the key, where he is, our need, and my reasons to request a stay of execution, including how he spent the last 35 years farming and carving wood. I write down Silas’s story as he told it, including all the details he gave me. I want Father Bodin’s advice. I put the letter in the scroll case and feel it vibrate as soon as the lid is closed.
Bronnen and I eat lunch.
“If a Zone of Truth proves the merchant guards Silas killed were fighting to defend a shipment of black lotus, then that renders the charge of murder as valid killings on behalf of the empire. It’s still killing but would not be considered murder. I might have to prove the killings as justified but that still leaves the crime of banditry if Silas and his band attacked first. Though, if the cargo was black lotus, it complicates things. I would need to know whether the lotus was destroyed, left, or taken to be sold or traded,” I explain to Bronnen as we eat. “If Father Gerrus, acting as a Judiscar, could give Sargeant Arynn, who was a killer, a different path to follow, perhaps I could do the same for Silas. I could offer penance for banditry and killing by serving the Porthion church but only if I can prove the killings were justified.”
Later that afternoon, Bronnen pulls the two-handed sword and stands like one of the men in my vision, one standing next to a Hularen king (Thurgen), to his right (Gorhund).
“Jovokarn,” Lysara says and I know she means the sword. 
I repeat the name of the sword to Bronnen. I spend the rest of that afternoon and evening sketching the recent events of our journeys while Bronnen carves, and we talk. After dinner, we bathe, make sure everything is locked up tight, and sleep.

Dream: Pixins, Silkies, & Children
I stare out at a lush and verdant green wood with little leather-winged Pixins and children playing with Silkies. I stand in a warm kitchen, looking out a window. There is flour on the table, and I smell bread baking while a roast turns on the firepit. A blue-grey basin bowl is filled with water, and I am washing vegetables. I hear the patter of feet, children’s feet, followed by peels of sparkling laughter as they play. The large oval window looks into a two-tiered garden at the back of the house with steps leading to the 2nd tier. Little green and blue bowls filled with sugar water are scattered about the vegetable and herb garden.

### Summary of the Journal Entry
On the 7th of Solik, Cara deals with a mysterious attack outside Father Bodin’s house, receives critical magical items and intelligence, and investigates the situation in Stonehill. She learns about Silas Shivarn, a notorious but morally complex bandit held for execution, and begins to unravel his story. Her investigation leads her to consider whether Silas’s actions were justified under Hulean Imperial law and if she can offer him redemption through service to the Porthion Church. The day ends with Cara sketching, reflecting, and sharing moments with Bronnen, followed by a dream filled with magical imagery of Pixins, Silkies, and children.

- **Sword "Jovokarn"**: A significant weapon tied to Hularen history and associated with the name Lysara.
