Read the following journal entry for my D&D character, Cara. Create a list of important items, locations, names, objectives and events. Each list should be a separate category. Include a summary of the of the journal entry: 6th of Solik, 2324 IC   6th of Solik, 2324 IC. Northern Sumarac Plains & Stonehill

Wake up and roll over to look at Bronnen but he’s not here. Spiritwalker Meroth is here and awake, speaking to the fire. Father Gayluss is also here but still asleep. I reach out and touch the spot where Bronnen was sleeping next to me and feel for his warmth, but the space is cold. I quietly dress trying not to disturb Spiritwalker Meroth as he chants, and walk outside looking for Bronnen or his footprints. I find his footprints which are half filled with fresh snow. He is headed East but I don’t see Bronnen. To our South, stretching from horizon to horizon is a wall of trees – the Great Wood (Homewood). 
I go back inside our makeshift shelter made of snow and ice. Spiritwalker Meroth is still chanting, staring into the fire and Father Gayluss is still sleeping. I move quietly back to my spot and pray before eating cold rations. I watch Spiritwalker Meroth and listen to his words, unable to understand him. Father Gayluss wakes and prays before eating his cold breakfast. I pack up my things and Bronnen’s and roll up our bedrolls. Father Gayluss also prepares to leave and when Spiritwalker Meroth stops chanting, we break camp.
The three of us head East following in Bronnen’s tracks. Spiritwalker Meroth leads, and I follow in his wake, Father Gayluss only steps behind me. While we walk, I recite the prayers I need to learn when I assist Father Gayluss. We walk unbothered for almost half an hour when Spiritwalker Meroth stops. I look the direction Spiritwalker Meroth is facing and see a figure jogging through the snow toward us. Bronnen comes from the South, from nearer to the Great Wood. When he reaches us, I pull our packs around and hand him a flask and some food. Then, I dig out a small area and build a small fire for Bronnen to warm up. The face paint that hides his tattoos is completely gone. We wait for him to tell us what he saw.
“3 men on foot ahead of us tracking Bodin,” he says. “Early this morning, around dawn, they cut into the wood, and didn’t even pause. There was a man in the wood watching them. He stayed hidden, they didn’t see him, but I saw Sumarac markings. Father Bodin’s scent and tracks continue East.”
After an hour, I put out the fire and we set off running. Spiritwalker Meroth chants and a path is made in the snow. His every footstep forces the snow aside and we pick up speed, running for 3 hours across the Sumarac Plains. Spiritwalker Meroth slides to a halt.
“Nyhoon,” he says. 
We hear a voice ahead of us and seemingly out of nowhere, we see a line of creatures 10-feet tall. Their faces are rotted and eyes are empty. Behind them I see 2 vampires, a ghost and a bone golem. They were waiting for us. The bone creature yells something we do not understand. 
“Nyhoon,“ Spiritwalker Meroth repeats, “undead Sumarac Reavers and a Spectre of Obzdelt.”
Spiritwalker Meroth jerks me to him, “Finish,” and throws me to a stone. He then throws Father Gayluss to the stone. He says to Bronnen in Hularen, “the stone.” He smacks the staff with the stone and it vibrates. The stone next to me grabs at me – it hurts – and throws me into the snow face first. Father Gayluss and Bronnen land right next to me. Some distance to the West, we hear Spiritwalker Meroth’s horn sound long and deep. I stand up and look back to the West. A snowstorm comes into view and bright flashes streak toward it, exploding. The fight is 200 yards West of us. We continue running East after Father Bodin, not expecting to see Spiritwalker Meroth again. As we run, I recite the words, all of them. 
We run up and over a rise and standing in front of us is a Sumarac Warrior. He’s alive. Behind him is a second Sumarac and the markings on the second man’s face are carved. Next to the second Sumarac is a third and a fourth. They speak in Sumarac, which I do not understand. Bronnen answers them in Sumarac. The first walks forward and speaks in Hularen, addressing me.
“What is your name, girl?”
“Carathul.”
“The Storm King says there is glory to found here. You speak His words?”
“I do, I speak Porthios’s words.”
“I am Vordoon Thunfier, the Pack Chieftain of the Blackwolf Clan. This (the 2nd man with scarification tattoos) is Spiritwalker Orja and he speaks for the Ancestors of the Blackwolf.”
I pull the two letters from Father Bodin out of my pack and hand one to Pack Chieftain Vordoon and Spiritwalker Orja of the Blackwolf Clan. They read their letters from Bodin and speak to one another in Sumarac. I watch their faces, listening to words I do not understand.
Spiritwalker Orja looks at me and nods, “Little sister.”
Pack Chieftain Vordoon motions toward the other two men with him, “Rhugan Wulfhun: Slayer of Bargoss and Killer of 9 Wyrvens. This is Saga Thragfall, Reaver of the Blackwolf.”
Both men nod at me.  Behind them are their mounts: 2 large horses and 2 huge winter worg.
Vordoon nods at me, “Come, Hularen, lead us and be swift.”
I turn to Bronnen, “Run.”
We set off again with the 4 Sumarac, running East, snow flying in our wake. After 45 minutes, we reach the hole where the cartouche exploded. The hole is massive and deep, at least 60-feet in diameter and trees all around the immediate vicinity are dead. Trees beyond are knocked down or leaning precariously. Hundreds of birds circle overhead, all kinds: wrens and sparrows, hawks and eagles, crows and ravens, and so many more. They are in a frenzy, weaving and whirling, calling and squalling. Smoke billows up out of the hole. On the outer edge of the crater stands the lone figure of Father Bodin who is on the side nearer the Great Wood.
“We need to reach Father Bodin,” I say.
Something moves in the woods and Vordoon roars. Several figures come running out of the woods, exploding against a barrier we cannot see before they reach us. The shadowy figure half concealed in the trees raises a white hand and the light in the area begins to darken.
“Kaz’na’thene,” Greed commands.
More creatures swarm at the edge of the trees. A massive wave of roiling darkness and corruption, too many to count. I hear the Asha’kari’s voice in my head.
“Come.”
A moment later, I am standing at the edge of the tree line. I don’t remember moving. I couldn’t have moved so far on my own, so quickly. I smell rot and disease, decay and death. 
“Give me Morvicar and your people may live in peace. Your efforts, valiant as they are, serve no purpose. You avoid an end I do not seek. Give me Morvicar. Give me vengeance and justice and I will leave all of your people be. You are nothing to me. Force my hand and bloodshed will be upon your head. A wash of life that has no purpose other than to slow me for I will bring him to justice, Cara Yornlin. That your people use him as a weapon means nothing. You will relinquish him to me, and he will stand before the old gods and answer for his crimes.”
I cannot see the Asha’kari’s face; he hides in the shadows of the trees and roiling darkness, but I know his voice. He is calm and well-spoken and if I didn’t know who he was, I might believe his words. Two glowing blue eyes gleam and I feel immense power.
“Lies,” I tell myself.
“I am not the architect of your despair, priestess. I am only an enemy if you make me one, but know this, Cara: I will wade through the bodies and blood of all your kind until none breathe air. I will rend their souls that nothing remains beyond this life for them if you do not stand aside,” Greed promises.
Behind me, I hear someone chanting in Sumarac and something yanks me back from the wood.  I am disoriented and I still feel his power. I am not sure if I was physically or mentally there.
“Give him nothing, Little Sister,” Spiritwalker Orja growls.
I try to be nice, my words civil and courteous but Greed’s demands and threats only increase in vitriol and viciousness until he pushes too far.
I yell at what I believe is the Asha’kari Greed, “You will never get your father back! You will never get vengeance or justice! I will never give you what you want!”
Creatures pour out of the woods. The Asha’kari grows to 80-feet tall and I still believe it’s Greed, it’s his voice. I stand firm, refusing to retreat out of fear at the waves of darkness and corruption swarming our direction as I continue to scream at the Asha’kari I think is Greed. 
“You want me to believe you will let us live in peace? You want me to believe you will be satisfied when Hunger is held accountable? Your words are lies. ‘Father, I come after you. I come to take for myself all that you are. I come to claim for myself all that you failed to claim.’ Those are your words, the words I believe. You speak to me of justice? You wouldn’t know justice if the gods themselves placed it in your grasp! You speak of vengeance as though it is a virtue, yet all you seek is consume and destroy! You are hollow. You dare threaten my people, Mother’s children, with extinction, and yet you cower in the shadows of your own wretched nature. You dare to threaten my people, the Storm God’s children? I am the light in the darkness! You will not have Hunger, not now, not ever! You will have nothing but the ruin you have sown, and I will see to it that your name is spoken only in curses and warnings to those who would follow your vile path. You think you can wade through rivers of Hularen blood? Then come! You will find the rivers too deep, too wild, and filled with Mother’s wrath and a rage you cannot quench!’
My voice carries above the roar of the creatures pouring from the woods, my faith in Porthios and the Mother a bulwark against the encroaching dark.
“This is not your land, and you will find no home here beyond your prison. You wanted a priestess to stand aside? You have one to stand against you instead! Strike me down, if you dare, but know this: my army stretches from one horizon to the next and your army will break upon it. I am Carathul of Hular; I am my Mother’s daughter. I am Carathul, Priestess of Porthios; I am my Father’s daughter. I am the bright storm, and your time comes to an end!”
My chest heaves. Rage hammers in time with my heartbeat like war drums. Madness to challenge an Asha’kari even when its power is diminished even when he, himself, is trapped like a wounded animal with a leg caught in a trap. My faith borders on fanaticism. Any sane person would think me unbalanced but all those standing with me roar and beat their chests and weapons together. 
The voice that responds is soft and menacing.
“I am Slaughter. I will destroy you, Carathul, but not before I rip apart all those you love, tearing pieces of them away in front of your very eyes. They will suffer but your suffering will be endless. Do you think your defiance means anything to me? Do you think your fleeting courage, your mortal indignation, holds power here? I am the end of nations, the devourer of hope, the flame that consumes the world entirely. I will feast on it all. You deny me vengeance? You deny me justice? What do you know of justice, child? You claim to serve a God of Storms but even He will abandon you before I am done. Justice is nothing but a weapon, a tool, and it is mine to wield. Do you think your God can save you? Do you think the soil beneath your feet will not turn to ash? The forests you call sacred will burn. The rivers you cherish will run red with the blood of your kin. Your precious mother will weep as I consume her, leaving nothingness in my wake. This land will be a remembrance to all the folly of standing against me!”
My heart pounds, but I know I need them close, the creatures of corruption and darkness. I need them close before I slam this trap shut. The Asha’kari screams back, and Father Bodin’s body goes rigid as blackness pours out of him and into the hole. The scars on my right arm tingle. The shadows around him writhe, alive with his hatred, seething with his malice. The creatures of corruption slow and stop before reaching the barrier, waiting. We are all waiting.
“You dare speak to me of denial? I have been denied for millennia, trapped and forgotten. I have watched your kind parasites leeching off power that is mine! You will beg me to end this, Carathul. You will cry out for the mercy you so arrogantly withhold, and I will laugh as I grind your people into nothingness. Not even your memory will remain. The power will be mine, and this land – this entire world – will bow before my might, or it will burn. Cling to your pitiful path. Stand against me if you must, but I promise you, your screams will echo long after the last of your kind falls, long after the land is unmade. I will reduce everything you love to ruin, and when the land is empty, when silence reigns over the ashes of your defiance, I alone will remember your name as the one who dared to defy Slaughter – and failed.”
Bronnen takes a step forward, one step behind me and to my side. I hear him chanting in old Hularen – a war chant. The tingling in my scars increases and I feel the Mother start to wane. As we watch, one of the creatures of corruption steps forward to test the barrier and finds it can get through. It roars and the wave of creatures charge forward. I raise my hands, Porthion holy symbol held high, and scream out the chant in Celestial. Bronnen fires two arrows at Father Bodin, hitting him in the chest both times, knocking him back and the darkness pouring out of him ceases.
I continue to scream the chant, enraged. My voice grows louder and stronger – I am the storm. Pack Chieftain Vordoon of the Blackwolf roars out, slamming his weapons together, and deep horns blow. From nowhere comes a horde of Sumar. Spiritwalker Meroth Dreadstaff with a Sumarac horde, all of them screaming and roaring as they charge the wave of evil and corruption sweeping towards us. 
East of us, from the corner of my eye, I see one man in full plate, and he summons a legion of men/ Portals open and through them pour Hulean shock troops. I continue to roar my chant, standing my ground, determined to do what needs to be done as the creatures continue to pour out of the woods. I yell out over the cacophony of noise, my voice heard above all else. The ground thunders and shakes behind me with the horses and winter worg running at full speed. Hulean Imperial soldiers and Sumarac warriors charge past me on either side, straight into the monsters and corrupted creatures. 
As I finish the chant, a burning, tingling sensation starts at my feet and races up through my body, along my arms, and out my fingertips. I scream in pain as blue-white lightning builds and cracks and pours out of me in a massive blast from my hand. The blue-white lightning circles around Bronnen and me. My hair rises and floats in the air as the liquid lightning forms into the shape of a massive dragon more than 400-feet long. The dragon rears up and charges, diving down into the crater where it explodes. Blue-white lightning pours back out of the hole in a wall of searing, sizzling, blue-white light striking into the woods.
A swirl of colors follow: reds, blacks, yellows, and whites flare before turning blue and flow back into the crater, picking up shards of stone as they go, recreating the stone obelisk that forms part of the Mor’Fang encircling the Great Wood. The shards of stone hover in place, the stone obelisk cracked and broken. Blue-white lightning rings the stone, sealing the cracks and binding the shards together, all but one small piece. Then, the lightning streaks out from the stone, hitting the horde of corrupted creatures and dark monsters, and annihilates anything and everything in that field corrupted by the darkness, leaving the Sumarac and Huleans unharmed. Thousands of creatures, hundreds of thousands, melt and disintegrate into dust. The blue-white lightning destroys the vileness of the corrupted horde.
I hear the voice whisper, “Your suffering will be legendary. All that you love will suffer.”
I kneel on the ground from the pain. Weakness washes over me and I know I am seriously wounded but I am not done, we are not done. I look up to see Father Bodin laying in the snow. High Prince Shirok Leighon stands in front of me forming a human shield. I watch as the Sumarac horde tears into what is left of the creatures. Bronnen fires his bow as fast as he can, arrow after arrow flying and striking true. We outnumber what remains by 5 to 1. I struggle to my feet determined not to faint. I join the fight, calling down Lightning, striking as many as I can, expending prayer after prayer while Shirok ensures nothing comes close to me. We fight until nothing is left. When all our enemies have fallen, I turn my gaze to Father Bodin.
“Bronnen, Bodin.”
Bronnen nods. He and I walk past the stone cartouche to retrieve Father Bodin’s body. Shirok readies his mages and archers in case more come out of the woods. The Sumarac ready their javelins and throwing axes. Bronnen checks Father Bodin and nods his head indicating he is still alive. It’s unnerving to be this close to the wood. The darkness is angry with me – I can feel it and all the hate is directed at me. 
“’Ware the line you cross, child,” a voice says from the woods. 
I haven’t heard that voice before. Bronnen and I look in the direction of the voice and see 2 figures in the wood. One is the oldest elf I have ever seen. It is his voice we heard, soft and gentle, his words are a warning not a threat. Next to the ancient elf is a Sumarac.
“Do not come near the warding line again or he will kill you,” the elf warns.
Bronnen and I drag Father Bodin’s body back beyond the barrier of the Mor’Fang. I look up Father Ardin Gayluss who has put on a pair of silver manacles. Past him, I see Father Braddock. We shackle and manacle Father Bodin, not taking any chances. His breathing is shallow and his pulse faint. Bronnen removes the two arrows sticking out of Father Bodin’s chest. We heal the wounds and Father Bodin writhes, screaming in agony. He’s not dead. His eyes are solid black. His veins are black. 
“We need a patch of soil free of snow,” I say.
A mage helps clear the snow with a spell. I pour the rock dust in a circle around Father Bodin, making sure the circle is unbroken before tamping it down with Bodin in the center. 
“A Circle of Exorcism,” I explain knowing the Sumarac are watching intently. 
I spike down the candles and then spike Father Bodin’s chains into the ground so he cannot thrash around and break the circle. I pull out the incense and holy water. Father Gayluss checks my work while Father Braddock heals me and restores my strength and constitution.
Father Gayluss casts a Prayer of Warding and Father Bodin’s body arches painfully into the air. When the prayer is finished, Father Bodin’s body rests on the ground within the circle once again. He turns his head my direction and looks right at me.
“Cara.”
I don’t answer.
“Cara, this isn’t necessary. Let me go.”
I remain silent.
“Cara!”
I jump slightly and clamp my teeth shut.
“I will trade you, child. Destroy this circle and I will give you the spirit of Sarana, the child who died slaughtered on the plains. Free me and I will give you your mother. Defy me and I will rip their souls to shreds. You have 3 seconds to answer. 1, 2, 3.”
I hear screams, terrible screams of agony and suffering. Sarana’s screams mingling with Mama’s. Tears well up in my eyes but I hold them back. The corner of Father Bodin’s mouth curls up into a sneer.
“I will give you the soul of the father you adore. Remove these shackles and I will give you the soul of your oldest friend, Myra. Defy me and I will boil the blood in their veins. You have 3 seconds, Cara. 1, 2, 3.”
More screaming fills my mind. I hear Papa yelling in torment mix with Myra’s keening wails. The tears I was holding back spill silently down my cheeks.
“The 3rd Brigade, those you call brothers and uncles.”
Their roars and howls add to the screams. My lip trembles and I dig my nails into my palms.
“Iron Hill, your neighbors and friends, all who live there – I will send a plague.”
Whimpers and moans are punctuated by sobbing and shrieking. A sob escapes my lips as I fight the images that come with the sounds. It’s not real, it’s not happening. It is a lie. Father Gayluss continues his preparations for the exorcism. Red splotches appear all over my skin. My eyes and throat begin to burn.
“Your family, your home, your friends – you would sacrifice them all? That is worthy of an Asha’kari. Perhaps I will keep you as a pet. Your faith?” His voice changes and I hear my own coming from his lips, “What is a god without followers?” He changes back to Bodin’s.
I stay silent, the red splotches spreading, and my vision blurring as I begin struggling to breathe.
“You know I will burn Travaghn to the ground. You have seen it. Would you save them? 1, 2, 3.”
High-pitched screeching fills my ears, and I choke on the acrid smell of burning bodies. I feel the searing heat on my skin. Smoke fills my nostrils. 
“Thank you, child, you have done so much good for me. Proceed with your chants. Thank you, Carathul, Destroyer of Hule. I will rip the Hularens apart and annihilate their souls. I will tear them to pieces and consume all.”
Father Gayluss splashes holy water on Father Bodin. The screaming stops, the pain recedes, and I can breathe.
“Name yourself, creature,” Father Gayluss demands. 
“I am all that was and is,” Father Bodin says.
Here, in this moment, I realize I was screaming at the Corrupted Mother, not Greed. She possessed Bodin. She speaks through him now. I sliver of Her, the tiniest sliver, escaped Her cage. My eyes widen and She smiles cruelly at me.
“No,” I whisper as the icy fingers of horror wrap around my heart.
Father Gayluss begins to chant, and the circle begins to seal with golden lines. A glyph forms beneath Bodin’s body. The Sumarac move away and the Huleans stay a respectable distance but within spell and arrow range. I move into position and at Father Gayluss’s signal, Father Braddock and I begin to chant the Prayers of Exorcism together. Bodin becomes more and more uncomfortable as we chant. He starts to thrash and jerk.
“I will take your womb, Carathul. Stop this.”
Searing pain explodes in my abdomen. Through sheer force of will I stay standing and keep chanting. The pain is intense but I don’t stop.
“I promise you will never bare fruit in this world – nothing but pestilence and putrescence will grow in your womb. It will hurt but you will survive. Your children will survive; unliving in life, undying in death.”
I don’t stop, tears flowing unbidden as pain tears through my womb. I feel it rotting and desiccating within me. I keep chanting. He turns his attention to Bronnen.
“I will make you frail and weak and diseased.”
I watch in horror as Bronnen stumbles and squints, aging and withering in front of my eyes. I don’t stop. The manacles crack. I reach across, careful not to break the circle, and hit Bodin hard in the head with my holy symbol. He smiles and it is chilling.
“1, 2, 3, 4, 5,”
Bronnen falls to one knee. Bodin laughs and begins to chant the Prayer of Exorcism with us. Father Gayluss stops chanting. He looks across at me.
“This is no possession. You know him best, Cara.”
This is the Corrupted Mother. I keep my eyes on Bodin and reach for the Mother. I can feel Her pulse, it’s Her.  Her laugh bubbles up out of Bodin and She blows Bronnen away. In an instant, I hear Spiritwalker Orja of the Blackwolf and Spiritwalker Meroth Dreadstaff. Now they know what I know – She is out.
“Flee, Little Sister. It is not your place to deal with this!” Orja instructs.
They stand outside the circle. The Spiritwalkers tell Shirok to take his Southlanders and leave. Shirok sends the army away before he walks over to the circle to stand near me. I can’t move, I won’t leave Bodin or Bronnen. Spiritwalker Orja and Spiritwalker Meroth begin chanting and casting. They both speak different words and make different gestures. I watch as the manacles around Father Bodin’s feet break and Bodin stands. Something I cannot see pushes Bodin back to the ground, pinning him in place.
Bodin speaks in Sumarac. The Spiritwalkers speak louder. High Prince Shirok drags me back to stand by him. The Corrupted Mother summons the Nyhoon. Shirok whistles to summon the Sumarac warriors. I put my holy symbol back on, pull my shield around, draw my sword, and pull the visor down on my helmet. Clumps of snow begin to rise all around us. 
Shirok turns to Father Braddock, Father Gayluss, and I, “Stay back and heal, nothing more. Do not draw their attention.”
Shirok steps forward and pulls out a long-spiked mace. The Spiritwalkers yell into the heavens. The Dark Mother rises again and Bodin stands in the circle. He starts to speak and Orja responds, hitting him hard with something I do not see. The snow breaks open and hands claw at the ground. The Sumarac ride back our direction looking confused.  Father Gayluss is still trying to figure out what is possession Bodin. I turn my gaze to Bronnen and he doesn’t look good. I cast a Prayer of Healing giving Bronnen the strength to warn Shirok that the Nyhoon do not die. 2 charge Shirok who leaps at them both and attacks, hitting both. I watch as they break apart and disintegrate. I count the heartbeats waiting for them to reform.
From behind me, a voice asks in Hularen, “What are you doing here?” 
I turn around to see a very tall Sumarac standing directly behind me.  
“The Dark Mother has possessed Father Bodin and She has summoned the Nyhoon.”
“I am Shunta, Spiritwalker of the Douth’Rujva. You should not be here.”
I watch as he walks over and joins the other two Spiritwalkers. He yells, his voice ringing out over all the noise. I hear a roar from far away to the West and turn to see a form quickly growing in size, doubling and doubling again, over and over as it runs. It looks like a black, boiling, roiling cloud with 2 huge red eyes. When it reaches us, I see an impossibly giant black bear. It roars and the ground shakes. It rears into the air, towering 50-feet overhead in the air. One massive paw slams into Bodin, knocking everyone down. The bear roars again and shakes the entire area as everything goes dark.

Dream 83: It’s Not About Smart
I wake, opening my eyes to see dust and dirt suspended in the air. The ringing in my ears is loud and I cannot hear anything else for several heartbeats. Then, I hear a muffled voice. I blink, trying to see through the fine spray of dirt and snow and dust. I see the Waif. I blink and nod at Him. He says something and I shake my head, rubbing at my ears. He laughs and I can hear Him.
“His bark is worse than His bite, and His bite is bad. (Ulsoc)”
The Mother (Woman) is here, too. “You’ve done well, Cara.” She is standing near the hold.
“We knew you would do right,” the Waif grins.
“We didn’t know, we hoped,” the Mother says softly.
“I knew. She’s smart, this one,” the Waif brags.
“It’s not about smart, well planned and lucky,” the Warrior says, standing opposite the Waif.
“One of the keys is in Stonehill,” the Waif quickly blurts out, His mischievous smile spreading across His face. 
“Hush, now,” the Mother warns.
The Waif smiles and winks, “He’s not gonna recover from that anytime soon.”
He glances at the wall of darkness South of us in the Great Wood. I look up at all of them from where I sit on the ground. There are bodies laying all around me, unmoving. A fine powder of dust and dirt slowly descends around us all, blanketing armor and cloth, leather and fur.
The Mother squats by the hole and peers in, “You’ve done well, Cara. Now is a time to learn and rest.”
“The blow has been dealt. The strategy has not been followed completely but it was effective,” the Warrior confirms.
“What does it matter? It worked,” the Waif counters.
The Warrior stays silent. I try to stand and it’s too much, so I remain where I sit. 
“Now is a time to learn, Cara, rest,” the Mother repeats. 
“The evil is contained, the ruse worked,” the Warrior says.
“Not without cost,” the Mother says as She continues to stare into the hole.
“Yes, but that is the way of war. There are costs,” the Warrior says.
“And she unleashed Yardrasok (Rage),” the Waif offers, grinning, as if anyone forgot.
“Enough.” The Warrior walks over to me and leans down. “You did well, Little Priest. The war is far from over. It hasn’t even started but this battle was important.”
“On more fronts than one. One of the beasts has awoken, 3 remain, daughter. Their times will come,” the Mother says.
“Gather they key. He has recently come to Stonehill. Swipe it quick, then Southwest. You have other things to attend to,” the Waif directs.
“Home,” I whisper.
“Not everything is…” the Waif starts to reveal.
The Warrior claps Him on the back of the head.
“Don’t be overconfident, child. Rest if you must. Every sword put in your hand is a spear in your enemy’s. You’ve done well, now wake,” the Warrior says as He gently pats my cheek.
I blink. I am sitting on the ground. My chest hurts. The ringing in my ears is so loud it drowns out all other sounds. A shower of fine dust and dirt hangs in the air, slowly falling to the ground. Bodies lay all around. High Prince Shirok lays near me. I watch as he moves, sits up, then stands. I watch his mouth move knowing he is speaking to me, but I cannot hear him. I rub my ears and shake my head to let him know I cannot hear him. I try to stand but cannot.
A little further away, Bronnen sits up. I look slowly around me: Father Gayluss, Father Braddock, the Spiritwalkers, the Sumar… all are beginning to rise. Bronnen walks over and helps me up. There is a crater where the Circle of Execution was. Father Bodin’s body lays within, crushed. The crater is roughly paw-shaped. High Prince Shirok slides into the crater and checks Bodin’s body before sliding a ring off his finger and onto one of Father Bodin’s. I watch as bones snap back into place, glad that Father Bodin is not awake or aware. 3 minutes later, Father Bodin sits up.
Someone heals us and my hearing is mostly back. Bronnen’s hearing is messed up, too. Spiritwalker Shunta speaks in Sumarac to Shirok and tells him he must leave. Shirok nods. Bronnen and I help him and Father Bodin out of the crater.
“Where do you need to go, Cara, we can send you wherever you need to be,” Shirok offers.
“We need to be in Stonehill, High Prince.”
Father Bodin thanks Father Gayluss and Spiritwalker Meroth for coming before asking Shirok to send us back to Stonehill. Shirok pulls out a wand and a moment later, Bronnen, Father Bodin, Father Gayluss, and I appear on the balcony in Father Bodin’s house. We walk downstairs together and sit at the table. Father Bodin pulls down a bottle of wine and 4 glasses.
“I was possessed for almost a year, it began almost a year ago, this piece of the plan. I allowed it, let it happen. The vitality potions weakened and limited their effects over time. The 3 men chasing me “caught” me near the Gap. I hoped our enemy would possess me. The only way we could breech the magic ringing the wood was from the outside. I destroyed the stone so I could be possessed. I used a relic near the stone, a relic that I stole from a Bloodmage who had torn Red Larch apart looking for it. I thought I would be possessed by the Asha’kari, not the Corrupted Mother. The stone is re-forged, the weak spot strengthened. The Asha’kari will have to work harder, now.”

Bodin says he needs something from Father Gayluss.
“A trip to Aletherin to find Jedarin Darr and secure his help to find who is supplying Blood Mages from there.”
“Father,” I ask, “when was this plan made: for you to become corrupted and destroy one of the Mor’Fang cartouches?”
“I planned this 84 years ago,” he says before explaining the details. “You have three tasks, Cara. 1. Find and gather the keys. The fifth is here. 2. Find and gather the shards & send them to Druids in Woodhome. 3. Find and stop the Asha’kari’s minions. These three things will aid us, but the outcome is not certain. This little ruse has bought us time but we do not know how much.”
That evening, after Father Bodin and Father Gayluss go to bed, Bronnen and I talk, covering many topics. In the middle of our conversation, we are interrupted by a small voice. We both turn to look and I see a boy about 14 years old standing in the open front door with 3 large men surrounding him. Neither of us heard the door open, which is unusual, and we know the front gate is locked. 2 of the men look like former soldiers and all three are armed and armored. 
“Pardon me,” the young boy says again, “I don’t mean to intrude. That’s her. I need to give something to you.”
“Who are you?” I ask.
“Colin. Collin Willune. I grew up in Hillcave, South of Karas,” he says. 
Colin has blonde hair and blue eyes. He’s a good-looking boy and dressed as a commoner in traveling clothes. On his back is a small child’s sized bow and quiver.
“I am supposed to tell you: none of us walks alone,” the boy says.
I smile and nod knowing the boy for a Porthion Chosen, “The road is long, but you will not walk alone.”
Colin nods in return. One of the men pulls out a very long, silver sword.
“He says you’ll need it,” Colin says.
“What is it and where did it come from?” I ask.
One of the men with Colin explains, “The boy dreams. In one dream, he found a crack in the stone. He climbed down and found something really important to him. The next morning, he followed his dream and found this.”
“You are like me,” I confirm.
“That’s Rhaegus,” the boy says. “He saw the Storm God, too. And that’s Kylass. Jada, she’s my friend, she’s like us. There was another but she’s gone now.”
“We shouldn’t know each other’s names, Colin. It helps to keep us all safe,” I say softly. 
He nods solemnly. “I’m supposed to tell you…. You need this (the sword) to find someone hidden where there’s water – not the ocean – like a pond or a lake. I saw you, you go to the water, really dark water. You stand at the water with the silver sword. That’s all I know. We need to go now, Cara.”
Bronnen walks over and takes the sword from Rhaegus.
“Do you need any supplies while you are here? There’s plenty of food,” I offer.
“Nah, we’re good. We have someplace to be.”
“Walk in His light Colin.”
“You, too, Cara. Walk in His light.”
I watch them turn to leave, closing the door behind them.  I get up and lock the door. I look out the window and they are gone. 
“The sword is Hularen, Cara. Do you know the place he described?”
“No, I don’t think so. Do you?”
“No.” 
Bronnen and I go find a bed in the servant’s quarters. We push the beds together. I am exhausted and sore and there are too many images in my head.
We sleep.

Dream 84: You Are a Paradox Unto Yourself
I hear the door open or close, I’m not sure which. I set up and listen closely for movement. I hear nothing but the door to the servant’s quarters is open and I know we closed it behind us. It’s still dark. I feel for Bronnen and find him sleeping soundly next to me. I am dreaming.
I hear feet walking outside the door and down the steps. I reach for Bronnen to alert him, but my hand goes through him. I climb out of bed and walk to the open door. There is no one there, the hall is empty as are the stairs beyond. I go downstairs to the kitchen and find the door open. In the kitchen, the pantry door is also open. I walk through both and find the door to the dining hall open. It’s still dark in here, too, but not so dark that I cannot see because the front door is also open. 
I walk to the open front door. It’s not snowing. A sliver of the moon hangs in the sky but when I peak outside, I see snow on the ground and one set of footsteps lead away from the house. The footsteps are not booted. I follow the footsteps to see where they lead and perhaps who made them. It’s cold and my breath frosts creating frozen plumes around me. The footprints lead to a stone in the yard and on it sits the hooded figure of the Mother (woman) in a long blue-black robe. Her fine-boned fingers are laced together, Her hands clasped in Her lap. 
“You’ve done well, Cara.”
She said this twice earlier today in the aftermath on the Sumarac Plains. To say it now, a third time must be important. I walk closer but not too close even though I really wish to see Her face. 
“You have secured a victory. The enemy remains imprisoned.” She pauses and I wait. “You did not believe yourself capable of such things yet here you are. This next cycle will see many roads walked and many trying times. You are a paradox to yourself: you forever seek the sunny afternoon but you are a beloved daughter of the storm. You have found success in your obedience; you must seek joy in your diligence. Listen to those you trust but you must also listen to yourself. The heart cannot healthily face darkness with courage if it is weighed down by worry. Careful that the weight of your burdens to not weaken you. A burden must be carried and then set down. It is the only way you may find room for more. We are always here, Cara. You are Chosen but you will need to hear Our voices in many places now and you will need to listen to your own voice. Another season of preparation, perhaps. You are young but you have been given the tools: use them and do not waiver in your diligence.”
I feel a hand on my right arm. I turn around and see a black furred figure. It stands 6’4” tall and golden eyes stare down at me. The large head leans down and growls. The black hound shakes me and the image fades.

I wake to find Bronnen standing next to me, his hand on my arm, shaking me lightly.
“Cara.”
I begin to shake from the cold. It’s so cold and I am outside. He picks me up and carries me inside, kicking the door closed, and sits in a chair in front of the fire with me still wrapped in his arms. My feet and hands are numb. My ears, nose, fingers and toes burn after a few minutes as heat rushes back in. When I am warm once more, Bronnen locks the door and carries me back to bed.

Cara and her companions navigate the perilous aftermath of a dark ritual involving the Corrupted Mother and undead forces. Cara encounters powerful allies, ancient spirits, and overwhelming darkness. Through faith and resilience, she helps seal a fracture in the mystical defenses of the land while confronting the Asha’kari Greed and the Corrupted Mother. Despite significant personal cost and trauma, Cara emerges as a key player in the unfolding battle between light and darkness. The journal concludes with Cara receiving cryptic guidance in a vision from divine figures and encountering a boy named Colin, who delivers an ancient Hularen sword with prophetic implications.

Wake up and find Bronnen still next to me, laying on his side. I don’t know how long he’s been awake, watching me sleep. He smiles and greets me good morning. We sit up. Spiritwalker Meroth is staring at the fire, his mouth moving silently. Bronnen and I eat breakfast with Father Gayluss. After, Father Gayluss and I pray together and then we prepare for the exorcism and banishment, repeating the rituals and the prayers together. Bronnen wraps the shard of stone in a maroon cloth Yi’kar gave me. When Spiritwalker Meroth stops chanting and nods at as, we pack up and put on our armor before breaking camp.
We walk East, Bronnen scouting ahead, Spiritwalker Meroth ahead of me and Father Gayluss behind me. Father Gayluss and I continue to practice the 3 Prayers of Sihluss for the Rite of Exorcism and Banishment. We walk practicing the prayers over and over. They are complicated and complex, the cadences and rhythms are unfamiliar. These prayers are not meant for senior clergy, long and very advanced but this is what we need to do, so Father Gayluss is doing all he can to ensure I am prepared. 
The wind is constant and unforgiving. My feet and hands are numb. My ears burn. We stop for lunch and build a fire for warmth. We all work to build a snow wall around us to protect us from some of the wind and keep the fire burning. After an hour, we continue walking East, Father Gayluss and I reciting the prayers over and over. An hour before dark, we make a new camp building walls and a ceiling out of compacted snow. Once our small snow cave is built, we construct a small fire. The heat of the fire will melt the snow on the inside just enough to form a thin layer of ice, keeping out more of the wind while keeping in more of the warmth. As we work, I recite the prayers to myself. We eat dinner together and talk quietly while Spiritwalker Meroth silently chants.
Sleep without dreams.Read the following journal entry for my D&D character, Cara. Create a list of important items, locations, names, objectives and events. Each list should be a separate category. Include a summary of the of the journal entry:

Read the following journal entry for my D&D character, Cara. Create a list of important items, locations, names, objectives and events. Each list should be a separate category. Include a summary of the of the journal entry:  2nd of Solik, 2324 IC. Stonehill 

When I wake, Bronnen is not in bed. He’s sitting by the fire. I walk over and sit in his lap, running my fingers over his forehead.
“I had a dream,” he says, “something important is coming and it will decide the path forward – a moment – there are two paths, and one is much worse than the other.” 
I dress, pray, and check the scroll case. There is a brief message from Arch Bishop Sandlin.
“Continue your search, it is important. You cannot be seen, magic protects you, why? I will check in again soon.”
I make breakfast for Bronnen, Father Gayluss, and I. We come up with a strategy to leave Father Bodin’s house without being seen. We create fog and leave by a second story window in the music room. We drop down into the fog and snow. Bronnen casts Pass Without Trace and we start walking toward the barracks. The Marshall is expecting us and we are admitted in. We are led back and through the barracks and down a flight of stairs. 2 guards are speaking with Acting Marshall Captain Greeland. We are not taken to the jail but to a room the Alchemist is using. We walk through and into the room. Marshall Greeland sits at a small table. 
He gets up to greet us and walks us to the jail cells where lady Esthera Keln waits. There are 2 guards outside her cell. Her hands are bound, her fingers are also bound, her feet are shackled, and her mouth is gagged. When she sees me, she looks instantly relieved to see two Porthion priests acting as Judiscars. I ask for her gag to be removed. I pray for Zone of Truth and prove to Marshall Greeland that a lie cannot be told by asking him to answer my questions falsely. When he is satisfied, I proceed to question Esthera Keln about the murders and Elder Sayden. She answers every question quickly and truthfully with no attempt at deception or withholding. Marshall Greeland releases her. 
“I think Breck and his employer are behind these murders,” Esthera declares.
“Colton Breck,” Acting Marshall Greeland states.
“Yes.”
“Elder Sayden is his employer?”
“No, not Elder Saydin, his brother Lord Saydin of Travaghn. Colten Breck was in the Broken Fence and Owen saw him where he shouldn’t be. Colton Breck is in the employ of Lord Saydin. Lord Saydin would have killed his brother, the Elder, over some family disagreements to profit from the raised taxes to the Sumarac. But as I opposed him, Elder Saydin failed 7 times to pass the tax. This would have made his brother very angry, perhaps angry enough to kill his own brother and point the murders in my direction. This way, he could remove two problems in one go,” Esthera says.
“I have had two guards on Breck since you first mentioned him, Lady Keln,” Marshall Greenland confirms. “He was at Judley’s this morning eating breakfast.”
Lady Esthera names the Elders she suspects of being bribed by Lord Saydin: Tinneran and Burlan – they were in favor of the Sumarac tax increase. The tax would have doubled the profits in favor of Hulean lords in both directions. The tax would have doubled on items sold and traded to the Sumarac as well as doubled the amount Sumarac had to pay in order to trade or sell to the empire. It was unfair and would have gone directly against Imperial Trade standards. 
When Esthera is let out of the cell, we walk to a small room where she can change back into her clothes. Acting Marshall Greeland steps outside the room as does Bronnen and Father Gayluss. When Esthera and I are safely inside and alone, I hand her the letter Father Bodin wrote and addressed to her. She reads it and burns it.
“Trust no one but those you have letters for, Cara. Everyone else, do not trust, except for Elkin, Sandlin, and the Grey Bird. The Porthion temple here is safe. Father Bodin’s home is safe. Berlain’s Warehouse, it’s on the East side of Stonehill, he’s in trouble and we need to make haste. I will meet you at his home and send you on your way,” Esthera says.
She changes clothes and gets read for a battle, putting on her Imperial Mage robes, component pouch, and wand bracer filled with wands. She straps on her Spellbook and pulls on tall leather boots.
“Check Berlain’s Warehouse. If he’s there, do not kill him but kill anyone else there. If he’s not there, return to his house and hurry East.”
Esthera leads us to a door in the alchemy room.
“Kendrin, my things, please,” Esthera says to Alchemist Kendrin.
Kendrin is old with white hair and a white beard. He is missing two fingers on his right hand and part of one on his left hand. He gives Esthera two bottles of potion which she gives immediately to Bronnen.
“Throw them at anyone odd,” she instructs.
We walk up and out to the waiting guards. Esthera’s head is on a swivel and so are ours. We set off in a carriage back to the Broken Fence. 
“The former Marshall was Harshall Higgin. He rotted from the inside out, we aren’t sure of the cause. Feral people started killing like in Travaghn. The attacks seemed random and all the people who instigated the attacks were all people who had been gone from Stonehill for one reason or another, travelers visiting family or merchants and traders but nothing other than having left and returned to Stonehill connected them. Father Rulin was still alive then. Bodin started stockpiling goods a year and a half ago. He gave me scrolls and spells to learn. There was an explosion 7 months ago and we couldn’t discern the cause. Then 3 months ago, Bodin told me to prepare for trouble and gave me a drawing of you, Cara. Two weeks ago, Bodin had his usual weekly meal at the tavern and told me ‘it’s coming, now.’ His eyes were strange. He left a scroll on the table and left without another word. A week ago, 3 men were killed. One was Elder Saydin and I’m almost certain one of the others was Father Rulin.”
She talks quickly on the short ride to the Broken Fence Tavern and Inn. We go inside and the tavern is packed with people. Lanerass is here and Esthera walks straight to him, we follow in her wake. Kieli is with him. We go to their private room to talk. She has a piece of the stone garden. She hands it to me.
“This is for Yi’kar,” Esthera says. 
I take it suspecting Father Bodin gave it to Esthera to hold for me. This piece is meant to go to Yi’kar. 
“The three men hunting Bodin aren’t men. They don’t eat or drink or sleep. They don’t bathe or relieve themselves,” Esthera explains.
Kieli tries to imitate their accents. Father Gayluss jumps in giving more examples of accents until Kieli recognizes one and says it’s close.
“A’kari,” Father Gayluss says. “Three A’kari, here.”
We walk back out to the tavern. Near the bar is a tall man, he must be close to 6’10” and looks Sumarac. Esthera and Lanerass begin addressing all the people in the tavern, many of them family and friends. She tells them all I acted as Judiscar, performed a Zone of Truth and proved her innocent of the charges of murder. Bronnen, Father Gayluss, and I leave the tavern as she speaks and the Sumarac watches us go. I wonder if he is one of the two Sumarac names Bodin addressed his letters to. 
We walk to Berlain’s Warehouse and hope Father Bodin is there. No one bothers us on our way there. We pass a dead body in the street, stopping only long enough to ensure the person is no longer breathing. The corpse is cold and rigid and covered in snow. We keep moving and find a second body. Both men are, were, town guards. We round a corner and find 7 more bodies. This time, they are a mix of town guards and citizens. All of them cold and rigid, all of them covered in a dust of snow.
2 strange looking creatures come out. They are huge and stand close to 7-feet tall. They are undead Sumar (nyhoon). They attack and the fight is on between the three of us and the two undead Sumarac warriors. Each time we are close to killing one or the other, they somehow heal themselves.
A voice behind us yells, “You cannot kill what is already dead but they can kill you.”
I glance behind me long enough to see the Sumarac from the tavern. He starts yelling words in Sumarac, holding up his black staff as he does. The air shimmers behind him and a 10-foot tall Sumarac made of transparent blue with 2 spectral birds circling his head appears. The transparent Sumarac flings two huge axes our direction.
I yell at Father Gayluss and Bronnen, “Down!”
Both spectral axes fly past and hit the undead Sumarac, knocking them both back 20-feet. The spectral Sumarac roars, and his axes come back to him as the ground around us shakes. I call lightning and move out of the way of the spectral of Sumarac. One of the undead Sumarac attacks the Sumarac of the staff and we continue to fight the undead. The Spectral Sumarac rips apart one of the undead Sumarac warriors, hacking it into 4 pieces before ripping the second one in half. The spectral Sumarac roars and the ground shakes again. 
The Sumarac with the staff heals himself and then pours a yellow powder on the corpses of the undead Sumarac warriors. I watch as their bones fall apart. Bronnen and I hold our ears from the screeching noise that follows, and their bones disintegrate. The Sumar and Father Gayluss are unaffected by the sound. By the time the bones disappear, my ears are bleeding. I pray for Mass Healing for the 4 of us. 
“I am Meroth Dierston (Dreadstaff), Spiritwalker of the Stone Raven Clan.”
He speaks in innovar common which is very good but his Sumarac accent is strong.
“I have a letter for you from Father Bodin, Spiritwalker Meroth.”
I hand him Bodin’s letter. He reads it, glancing at me, before speaking to Bronnen in Sumarac and then Hularen. Bronnen nods but does not translate what was said. He picks up Father Bodin’s scent in a nearby building. After a quick search, we find food and empty potion bottles. They smell similar to healing potions but slightly different, too, and remind me of the potions Roland was taking. There are almost a dozen bottles here, far too many.
“Whatever these potions do, they are not a cure. They may hold back a corruption, like Roland’s,” I say, glancing up a Bronnen. “They help but the help is only temporary.”
“You cannot cure death with your potions,” Spiritwalker Meroth Dreadstaff says.
Bronnen tracks Father Bodin to another building. I find a barrel with Father Bodin’s blood on it. Beneath the barrel is another glyph. Once again, only I can see it. The glyph looks like a ward and it would have kept him safe until he was found. 
“He’s gone East,” I say.
Bronnen says we are at least half a day behind him. Bodin was here, waiting for us. 
“East to the Plains of Menoc,” Spiritwalker Meroth Dreadstaff says. 
I point out the glyph to Father Gayluss. He touches it and disappears. I take Bronnen’s hand and have Spiritwalker Meroth Dreadstaff touch Bronnen before I touch the glyph. Lightning crawls up my arm and we disappear. We are on the balcony of Father Bodin’s home. He must have come here after the fight, but we don’t find any blood. We go into the main bedroom. One of the bookshelves is moved. We find a cache of items and whatever may have been in the shelves is gone. We check the rest of the rooms, and nothing is amiss upstairs beyond the bookshelf and the closed bedroom door. We go into the open study and find 2 new empty bottles lying on the floor. We missed him by hours. 
“I suspect Lady Esthera’s part is done – she gave us what we need.”
I hold out my hand to Bronnen and we all link hands this time before I touch the glyph I see in the corner of this room. It is new and was not here yesterday. As I reach for the glyph, an almost transparent figure appears wearing bloody Hulean armor.
“If you are seeing this, if you are here, then the time has come. You will find me beyond, likely. Time is very short, and our timing has to be perfect. I’ve left instructions to each of you. Vordoon, you do me honor by being here. Meroth, Gaylus, thank you, if you are here. Your faith and your friendship will not go unrewarded. What comes next is an end to watching and waiting and a time to strike a blow. Know this: none of us may survive to do so but should we, we may still not survive the blow we strike. All is as the Storm Father wills. On this day, a blow against the enemy may be struck, whether we survive or not is of less importance. To the Sumarac who are here, this will be the first time in thousands of years where you may soak your blades in the blood of a true enemy. Only one must come forward, only one must travel on. The rest of you do so of your own free will. Cara, find me if you can. I hope you have come prepared. Should you succeed, the Father wishes you to let the enemy know who you are but not until the end. Time is short, the sand falls. Swift, now.”
His images twitches and a ghostlike face, not Father Bodin’s, shifts and moves. The face looks similar to Lysara’s but it is not hers. The image of Father Bodin fades. I touch the circle. Light flashes, lightning crackles, and we are suddenly somewhere else. It’s very cold here and we are surrounded by snow and ice. We all look around but we don’t see any footprints. 
I look up at Spiritwalker Menoth Dreadstaff, “Is this the Plains of Menoc? Do we still head East?”
He says nothing. I climb a rock to get a better view of where we are while the Spiritwalker does… something. 20 minutes pass. All around me I see ice and snow and very few landmarks.
Finally, Spiritwalker Meroth Dreadstaff speaks, “These are the Rocks of Jobruhn. We will find them all along this way heading East. There’s a town to the East and beyond are the Plains of Menoc, where the elder stone exploded.”
“That’s our direction,” I confirm.
He gives a slight nod, “We will wait here for an hour.”
Spiritwalker Meroth Dreadstaff turns North toward the Sumarac plains and stands still. I see his mouth moving but I do not hear any words. We wait here for almost a full hour before he yells out for all to hear, “Doonfier! Doonfier! Doonfier!” The wind carries off his words and he goes still and silent once more. We wait again. I continue to search the area, looking as far as I can see but I see only an empty sea of white obscured for moments by fog and low-hanging clouds. 
Finally, he says, “We leave now.”
We head East through the snow and ice and the killing cold. I am glad Bronnen and I bought Sumarac fur coats before we left Stonehill. There are lumps under the snow which we walk around. 
“Piles of old bones,” Spiritwalker Meroth says. “Do not touch them. They carry on them the taint.”
Bronnen asks, “Where do they hail from?”
“They are Karnath of the Undarr. Urdinlara went this way,” Spiritwalker Meroth says by way of explanation. 
Bronnen tells me that Urdinlara is Sumarac and means Storm Walker. Father Bodin, among the Sumarac, is the Storm Walker. Spiritwalker Meroth Dreadstaff leads our little party, and we follow in his wake. The snow is 2- to 3-feet deep in places. We walk past the rocks into a sea of white, keeping wide of the bone piles. The wind is merciless and constant. Ice forms quickly on my armor, even under the heavy Sumarac furs. We trudge East for 5 hours before Spiritwalker Meroth stops.
“You will die if you travel at night,” he says to us. “We will make camp here.”
He shows us how to make a shelter of formed blocks of snow. We dig down to the earth and create a snow wall around the shelter to further insulate ourselves from the cold. Our shelter even has a domed roof formed of snow and ice. The shelter we make is just large enough for the 4 of us to sleep in with a small fire. With the roof, it’s dark but there is a central hole in the ceiling just big enough to allow smoke from a fire to escape and for fresh air to enter. Inside, the wind is blessedly gone. Bronnen creates an alarm spell for the camp, and we build a fire. I take off my armor and oil it liberally before kitting it up. 
“You know the Bodin how?” Spiritwalker Meroth asks me.
I explain how I know Father Bodin.
“You came here to sacrifice your life, why?” he inquires.
“Porthios sent us here. He asked us to be here so I came,” I reply.
He asks Bronnen the same question and Bronnen responds, “It needs to be done.”
“Why did you come with us, Spiritwalker Meroth?” I ask in kind.
“Urdinlara is a rare breed among your people,” he looks at Father Gayluss, not Bronnen and I when he says this. “He gives his word and keeps it. He gives and expects nothing back in return. He is known to our people in the South as the White Fox and Storm Walker. He is an ally to us so I have come but it is not his place to strike at Death. Not his fight.”
Spiritwalker Meroth asks Father Gayluss the same questions and he answers.
“I have been here before. I led people East and killed a rogue mage. My name is known among the Sumarac,” Father Gayluss says.
“What do you do, Elkin of the South?” Spiritwalker Meroth asks Bronnen.
“I am a Warden of Woodhome.”
“Your family has many names?”
“Yes, back to the beginning.”
“Tell me your story,” Spiritwalker Meroth says to me.
I tell him leaving out very specific parts. He listens without interruption, Meroth and Father Gayluss, both. It’s a long story and takes more than an hour for me to tell it.
“You need to learn how to tell stories. It is a good story, Cara – it needs a good telling. We are on Blackwolf lands. The spirits of our people are quiet at your presence. They do not call to kill you; they watch and wait. And odd thing for a Stonelander,” again, he looks at Father Gayluss.
We eat as we talk before bedding down to sleep.

Dream 82:
I open my eyes knowing I am dreaming. I stand on a snowy plain. It is not snowing and there is no wind. Ahead, about 30 paces away, is a large oak-bound door. Squatted next to the door is the Waif. The door is in the middle of nowhere and attached to nothing. 
“Hi, Cara.”
He leans against the door.
“Hi.”
He looks at the door. It’s carved with square pyramids, their points out. Otherwise, it is plain. There is a handle on the right. I reach for the handle. 
“When you’re done, be sure to come back.”
The Waif blows into His hands. He’s not smiling but He doesn’t look serious, either. He’s neutral, which is odd. I smile and nod at Him. He nods, too, and looks a little wistful and a little sad. I turn the handle, open the door, and step through. The world has changed.
I step out on an earthen embankment. To my left, the earthen embankment steps down with Hulean Imperial Soldiers on each embankment. To my right is a partially built stone wall and behind it, I can see the ocean. There are so many tents, and people running to and fro. They look tired, weary and dirty. This is the North-eastern Citadel Papa is helping to build and protect.
50 paces away stands a loan man on the palisade. By his cut and stance, I know it’s Papa. I walk toward him.
“Papa.”
“Good morning, Little Priest. They didn’t come this morning. Likely they’ll come at dusk or early next morning. We need to prepare. We can expect attacks from the South-west and North-west. If they can keep us from sleeping, they’ll use that advantage. We need to hold our magic, though. The first wave, we need to dawn them in. The main bulk will come after.”
“Lord Commander.”
“Yes, Suress.”
“I have the heavy shield in the North-west – 4 companies like you asked. 3 in the South-west, the 4th and 5th as spears in the North-west. Our middle is a little weak, sir.”
“Yes, it’s my hope to draw them to the middle. The walls of the palisade are steepest there but my guess is the bulk will come against the North-west…” Papa continues giving orders and I wait patiently.
He turns his attention back to me, “They’ve hammered at us for 2 months straight. We’ll have to worry about the plague soon. The main push will come soon. The middle is our weakest spot – we need to seal that breech as quickly as possible.”
“It is a lure,” I say.
He looks down at me and winks.
“Nothing excites a predator more than weakness. We lure them in, then snap! The trap closes and we make them pay for every step. We cut the heart out of them. Come, Little Priest.”
I follow him down to the front palisade. Hidden behind the 1st layer of logs is a 2nd set of spiked logs. The halberdiers are just waiting for the moment to lift those logs to seal the breech. The archers and catapults are all pointed in this direction. 
“This is a cage,” I look up at Papa and see that he is pleased. He has remade the Iron Hill kill box here in the North-east Citadel.
“Every enemy you ever face, child, will look for a weakness. What’s the smartest thing you can do?”
“Show them one, show them what they expect to see.”
He taps his nose.
“Now, prepare yourself. Your mother’s waiting.”
He points and I walk the direction he indicates to a tent with a door. I step through and enter into a wooden hallway. A man in heavy Porthion robes stands here. I see him in profile before he turns toward me. He has redish-brown beard and hair and very familiar eyes: Father Gerrus in disguise. I hug him and he hugs me fiercely back.
“It’s good to see you, child. I wish it were under better circumstances.”
Father Gerrus takes my holy symbol off, lifting it over my head, and wraps it around my hand before handing me a vial.
“Stay calm and stay the course. Remember, we are not just saving a life, we are trapping an enemy, too.
“Yes, Father.”
We turn and walk together down the hall.
“We must stay completely in harmony,” Father Gerrus instructs.
I nod again.
“And whatever you do, do not waiver. Your fear must belong to you today. You must master it for fear will be the weakness that will destroy you here.”
“Yes, Father.”
“You remember what to do if the creature starts to incant?”
“Strike them, twice, hard with my holy symbol.”
He nods, “Are you ready, Cara? Truly ready? It would be better for me to go on alone if you are not.”
“No, Father, I am ready.”
“Alright, go on in.”
I walk through the door, bracing myself for what I might see and step back out into the snow. I glance back and the door is closed. The Waif is here waiting and we stare at one another in silence for several minutes.
On the wind, I hear a voice, “Ever smith folds and hammers a blade. Fire and steel, hammer and sweat, tempering the blade over and over. It’s not until the blade is tested that its worth is known,” the Warrior says.
“Cara.”
I turn back to the Waif.
“Do you remember who you are?”
I nod, “I remember.”
“Do you?”
“I am yours.”
“Don’t forget to let them know that.”
He puts a blue gem in my hand and folds my fingers over it.
“Now go.”
He points into a wall of darkness. I turn and walk toward it. A section starts pulsing. I walk faster. It pulses. I run through the snow and raise my hand, my holy symbol wrapped in one and the blue gem clutched tightly in the other. I hear the thunder of hooves behind me. The blackness looms over me. I scream out as something hits me, coursing through me and explodes in white around me.

I wake. I am laying down, a hand on my chest holding me in place. Bronnen is looking at me. Everyone is awake and staring at me.
“You were yelling,” Bronnen says, “Do you remember what you called out?”
“No.”
“Part of it was Celestial,” Father Gayluss explains, “the other was…”
“Not,” Spiritwalker Meroth jumps in.
Father Gayluss repeats the Celestial words, “I enthrall and command you, I bind you and I banish you by the laws of heaven. This is not the Prayer of Banishment, Cara, this is something completely different.”
Bronnen looks at me, “the rest was very similar to our chants, the ancient ones.”
Bronnen lets me up and I write down my dream, retelling it as I write to Bronnen, Father Gayluss, and Spiritwalker Meroth Dreadstaff.
Bronnen tells us he had a brief dream, too.
“I was told, ‘Don’t miss. If things go bad, don’t miss. Kill him.’”
“I also dreamed,” Father Gayluss offers but does not explain his dream. “I brought two pair of silver manacles for hands and feet with me. I took them from Father Bodin’s house.” 
I look them over when he shows us. They are covered in runes, unfamiliar runes. They are neither Celestial nor Hularen. There is a strange magic on them, too, a myriad of colors but mostly blues and greens. The magic on the silver manacles is Hularen but old and probably Ethragen. 
We go back to sleep.Read the following journal entry for my D&D character, Cara. Create a list of important items, locations, names, objectives and events. Each list should be a separate category. Include a summary of the of the journal entry:

### Summary of the Journal Entry:
Cara, Bronnen, Father Gayluss, and Spiritwalker Meroth Dreadstaff continue their journey toward the Plains of Menoc, preparing for a confrontation that could decide the fate of their mission. Cara experiences a dream filled with divine messages and prophetic visions, reinforcing her role in the unfolding events. Bronnen, Father Gayluss, and Spiritwalker Meroth also have significant dreams, signaling divine intervention and guidance. The group faces harsh conditions, learns survival techniques, and grows closer as they share their stories and roles in the unfolding prophecy.

---

### Important Items:
1. **Scroll Case:** Contains messages and instructions, including one from Arch Bishop Sandlin urging Cara to continue her search.
2. **Silver Manacles (Runed):** Brought by Father Gayluss, these ancient Hularen items bear unfamiliar runes and magical properties, possibly Ethragen in origin.
3. **Blue Gem:** Given to Cara in her dream by the Waif, symbolizing divine intervention or a key to her mission.
4. **Holy Symbol (Porthion):** Used in banishment rituals and a significant tool in Cara’s divine mission.
5. **Maroon Cloth (Wrapping for the Shard):** Protects a shard that is part of the group’s preparations.

---

### Important Locations:
1. **Stonehill:** Starting point of the day’s events, including Father Bodin’s house and the barracks.
2. **Sumarac Plains:** A desolate, snowy expanse the group must traverse.
3. **Rocks of Jobruhn:** A significant landmark marking their path toward the Plains of Menoc.
4. **North-Eastern Citadel (Dream Location):** A fortified outpost under siege, connected to Cara’s father.
5. **The Waif’s Door (Dream Location):** A mysterious, freestanding door that transports Cara between visions.

---

### Important Names:
1. **Cara Yornlin:** Protagonist, tasked with leading her group and fulfilling divine missions.
2. **Bronnen:** Cara’s companion, scout, and protector, receiving guidance in his dream to be decisive in battle.

7. **The Warrior (Dream Figure):** Provides wisdom about perseverance and the importance of preparation.
8. **Father Gerrus (Dream Figure):** A disguised ally preparing Cara for the challenges ahead.
9. **Urdinlara (Storm Walker):** A title for Father Bodin among the Sumarac, signifying his role as an ally and rare individual.

### Objectives:

2. **Prepare for the Confrontation:** Master the prayers and gather tools like the silver manacles to aid in the mission.
3. **Interpret and Act on Prophetic Dreams:** Use divine messages to guide decisions and strategies.
