Include a summary of the of the journal entry: 1st of Solik, 2324 IC   I wake holding Mama’s holy symbol – it wasn’t a dream. I tell Bronnen. Bronnen goes to find an armorer so he can darken my Porthios armor. I pray while he is gone and write down the dream that was not a dream. I check the scroll case and read my bible until Bronnen returns. He’s been gone close to half an hour when I hear something or someone at the door trying to get in. I quietly slide off the bed and get my bow, nocking an arrow. I wait at the far side of the room, my eyes fixed on the door, listening for the smallest sound. I hear the latch again followed by silence. I go back to reading my notes, keeping one eye on the door and the bow in my lap.
15 minutes later, I hear the lock click and someone knock. I put down my notes and pick up the bow again. Then, I hear Bronnen’s voice speak in Hularen.
“It’s me.”
I unlock the door and open it, bow still and a single arrow still in my hand. He has pots of dye that will darken my armor.
“It will come off,” he assures me, “but not in rain or water.”
We do our best to disguise my armor and shield using the dye and strips of dark leather. We pack up our gear and go downstairs to eat breakfast and speak with Lanerass Keln. It’s still early morning and very quiet in the Broken Fence Tavern & Inn and it is mostly empty. At the bar are 3 men sitting on stools and a different bar keep is behind the bar. The bar keep is in his 50s with grey hair and a short beard. He gets us chunks of meet and a small wedge of cheese and something to drink.
“Where is Lanerass,” Bronnen inquires.
“He had to step out. I’m just watching the tavern for him while he’s gone,” the man says.
I look around and notice the kitchen is close, Kiala is not running about and Owen the Sumarac is not here. Something is wrong. 15 minutes later, Owen comes in with an old woman on his arm. Her white hair is pulled up into a bun. She is about 5’6” and looks to be in her late 70s or early 80s. The men at the bar call her “Lady Keln” and I recognize she must be Dobrin Keln’s widow, Arana. Despite her age, her eyes are sharp, and her voice is steady when she speaks.
“Owen,” she says, “clean the bar and get the fires going. This won’t do, we have guests.”
“Lady Keln, is Lanerass going to sell the inn with all that’s happened?” one of the men at the bar asks.
Instead of answering them, she shoos them out of the bar. Once they are gone I ask her what has happened.
“There’s been some trouble this morning,” Lady Arana Keln responds but she doesn’t elaborate. 
I look over to Owen. One eye is almost swollen shut and his knuckles are torn open and bloody. Owen brings over two bowls of porridge.
“I can clean your wounds, Owen,” I offer.
He gets mighty upset with my offer.
“Mama will be back, she’ll do it.”
He’s upset, like his mother is gone. I scan the room and in the shadows against the wall is an Imperial Guard’s helmet. One side is bashed in and covered in blood. Bronnen and I suspect Lanerass and his wife have been arrested. We finish eating just as someone begins banging on the tavern door. Owen gets to the door and admits Uncle Theyan who has arrived with 2 boys. 
“Ma, is it true?” Theyan asks Lady Keln.
“No, of course not, but they have taken her to the jails. Go home, Theyan, and do not raise more trouble.”
Theyan nods to her but tells his sons to stay behind and help their grandmother. 
“Father Bayerthin is the family priest, priestess. If we need healing or guidance, we’ll seek him out,” Lady Arana Keln tells me. “But if you should like to speak with him, he’s usually up at the church. Might let him know what happened.”
Bronnen and I leave to go find the Porthion temple and speak with Father Bayerthin. It’s a lovely morning and snow gently falls. It’s the first day of the New Year   and usually a day of celebration. We follow Lady Arana Keln’s directions to the Porthion church until we find it. We walk up to the doors, open them, and step inside. It’s not too big or too small and looks like it will seat about 30 comfortably or 50 at a squeeze. There is a graveyard out back. The church is empty but a moment later, a door towards the back opens and a man who I assume is Fatherr Bayerthin walks out.
“Excuse me Father,” I say, “I am Priestess Cara, and we are looking for Father Bodin. He’s missing and I was sent to find him. I have asked his friends, but no one has seen him. Do you know where I might find him? He needs my help, and I must get to him soon.”
“Bodin?”
“Yes, Father Aladin Bodin.”
“Bodin isn’t a priest, he’s a groundskeeper.”
That catches me off guard. 
“Are you Father Bayerthin? Lady Arana Keln sent me to speak with him, she said he might know where Father Bodin has gone and that Father Bayerthin might also need to know what happened to Lanerass and Esthera Keln.”
“Father Bayerthin is also missing. I came here looking for him but found the church empty and Bayerthin gone. Do you know anything about his disappearance?”
Again, I am caught off guard by this information. 
“No, Father. We arrived only yesterday and stayed the night at the Broken Fence.”
“Cara. We don’t know this man. Who are you,” Bronnen asks?
“I am Father Ardin Gayluss. Why were you sent here to search for Father Bodin?”
“Father Ardin Gayluss,” I explain to Bronnen, “is one of the most traveled Pilgrims of Porthios and one of the reasons I wanted to become a Pilgrim. He is also one of the first priests to visit the mud towns.” 
I am quite amazed to be standing in front of and speaking to Father Gayluss. 
I look back to him and answer his question, “I was sent here to search for Father Bodin,” I look up toward the heavens, “and I go where He sends me, Father. Porthios said I must find him and help him, so I have come here to what our Father asks.”
Father Gayluss, however, is not convinced.
“There are many who are older, wiser, and have more skill than you. Why send you to help Bodin?”
“I do not question Him, Father. He tells me where I am needed, and I go. It is not for me to question Him why He sent me instead of another, but if our Father sent me, then I am needed.”
“He also teaches us to question, sister. We should not follow blindly like sheep to slaughter.”
“Yes, Father,” I say, not bothering to explain myself. Those who know I am Chosen, know and those who do not… I am not to explain who or what I am. “If you need further confirmation, you could ask Arch Bishop Sandlin.”
He raises an eyebrow.
“Father Bodin’s house is 4 blocks East and 1 block North of the temple. Meet me there in 3 hours,” Father Gayluss instructs.
Bronnen and I return to the Broken Fence Tavern & Inn to see if Lanerass Keln has returned. When we get back to the tavern, no one is there outside of Lady Arana Keln and one girl. They are trying to prepare for the lunch rush. I create food and water to help them. 
“Laneras may be trying to speak with his wife at the jail or perhaps speak with Acting Marshall Captain Greeland. Esthera was arrested and accused of murder because she is a mage. They think she killed 3 men,” Lady Arana Keln confides in Bronnen and I but the heat in her voice lets us know that the charge is baseless and irrational. Something is very wrong.
“They say Esthera burned three men to a crisp, that she snuck out in the middle of the night, found 3 men on the street and summoned magic burning them where they stood. She’s not got a black heart, and it would be impossible for her to sneak out and Laneras not hear her. He knows something bad is coming. I think he’s taken Kieli to an old friend’s house South of town: Barlin Indale. Laneras thinks someone is coming for him and his family but he doesn’t know why.”
Lady Arana shows us on a map where Barlin’s house it located. 
“Maybe you can help Lanerass and his family while helping Father Bodin,” Lady Arana Keln suggests.
Bronnen and I head back out to see if we can find Barlin Indale and Lanerass Keln at a house on the outskirts of town. Bronnen and I find the house without difficulty. We knock on the door and Lanerass answers just enough for us to see each other. Before either of us can speak, 3 men appear behind us from out of nowhere. One of them looks like a ranger but the other two look like bandits. One of the bandits lights a sack filled with something and hurls it at us. I don’t even wait for the sack to land and erupt filling the air with caustic smoke. 
I pray for Call Lightning and hit all three of them, killing the 1st brute. The leader attacks me and he’s fast. Bronnen charges and attack. The second brute throws another fire pouch. The first runs away screaming something about “Kurgass.” 
I call down lightning a second time and kill the 2nd brute. The leader heals with a potion and attacks Bronnen. Bronnen heals himself and attacks back.
I call Lighting a third time and the leader tries to run away. Bronnen and I both attack him with our swords as he tries to flee. We run after him and Bronnen fires two arrows but both miss. His eyes are stinging from the smoke. I call Lightning and kill the leader. 
I grab the leader by the boots and drag his corpse back toward the house. To clear the air of the acrid smoke, I pray for Sleet Storm to put out the fires and flush away the smoke. The house Lanerass is in is on fire. I pull Laneras and Kiele out of the house and perform a Prayer of Healing for all 4 of us. I check the bodies and find 16 copper on the 2 brutes. They both wear low to medium quality weapons. On the leader, I find a strange ring with a tiger’s eye, a nice quality great sword, 60 gold, and an iron key. 
“Whoever is framing my wife sent these men. One of the Elders must be involved. They found my wife’s loadstone on the road near where the 3 men were killed. My wife is a descendant of Lord Kelgin Windamere, the 1st Founder, one of the original founders of Stonehill. My wife does transmutation magic, she’s not a murderer,” Lanerass Keln tells us. “Elder Saydrin was killed with two strangers. Saydrin and Esthera oppose one another to raise taxes on the Sumarac. That is well known in Stonehill. Saydrin is for raising taxes and my wife is opposed. Saydrin’s brother is a merchant Lord in the Vale and he wanted the taxes raised.”
“What does this have to do with Father Bodin?”
“I know who is after Bodin,” Lanerass says.
Lanerass marks a cabin on the map where we can find him and Kieli.
“I will take my daughter here, it’s safe. They (the Marshall) are going to think I did this.”
“No, he won’t. I will go speak with him now and tell him what happened,” I tell Lanerass. “I will try to speak with Esthera, too.”
Bronnen and I go see if we can find Acting Marshall Captain Greeland. We stop to buy 2 Sumarac fur cloaks and they are well worth the price. We walk to the guard barracks to see if they can point us to Captain Greeland as we are here to speak to him on the matter of Esthera Keln. A guard goes to relay the message while we wait. He takes us inside when we tell him there was an attempt on Lanerass Keln’s and his daughter Kieli’s life. This room looks to be used as an office. The man sitting in a chair is Captain Greeland, Acting Marshall. 
“Acting Marshall Captain Greeland, I am Cara Yornlin, Priestess of Porthios and this is Knight of Porthios Elkin. We are here to speak to Esthera Keln. We understand she has been arrested on suspicion of 3 murders.”
 “The alchemist on retainer to the Imperial Guard is sure it was lightning damage,” Captain Greeland says.
I nod. 
“That may be true, but Esthera is not the only mage in Stonehill.”
“There is other evidence.”
“Yes, so we understand. Let’s come back to this in a moment, Captain Greeland. We also need to inform you that only minutes ago, 3 men attempted to murder her husband, Lanerass Keln, owner of the Broken Fence and their daughter, Kieli Keln. The 3 men managed to burn part of Barlin Indale’s home in the process. Elkin and I killed the 3 men, saved Lanerass and Kieli Keln, and I put out the fire before it completely consumed Master Indale’s home. We left the bodies laying near the house and came here to inform you of the incident. We believe this is not coincidental and the Keln family is being targeted,” I explain. 
“I cannot allow you to speak with Esthera Keln now,” he says.
“We’ll return, then, to speak with her when there is a better time.”
Acting Marshall Captain Greeland breathes out a heavy sign. 
“I am Acting Marshall because the previous Marshall rotted to death while he was alive,” Captain Greeland admits. “The alchemist on retainer to the Imperial Guard is sure it was lightning damage.”
Bronnen and I lead 5 guards to retrieve the bodies of the 3 men who attacked us trying to kill Lanerass and Kieli. Then, we find Lanerass and Kieli at the cottage, taking care to make sure we are not followed. Bronnen sets a quick pace. We check on them both and they are okay.
“I did not get to speak with Esthera, but I will try again,” I tell them. “Do you need anything?”
“No, priestess, we will be fine.”
Bronnen and leave to meet Father Ardin Gayluss at Father Bodin’s home. His house is in the older part of Stonehill, the original bit. The houses here are built for defense and Father Bodin’s home is a large 2-story stone house with an outbuilding. The gardens and buildings are completely walled in with heavy iron gates offering the only way in and out. The iron is rusted and one of the gates is already open, perhaps Father Gayluss is already here. Several statues in the garden are broken but the plants do not look overgrown or dying from neglect. One statue is a bearded human with a number of scars on his face – the Warrior – and he looks angry. The house is large, too large for one person to live in.
More than one set of footsteps lead in and out of the garden, clearly visible in the snow indicating they are recent. Bronnen and I draw our weapons and approach cautiously. A figure steps out of the shadows along with 2 odd skeletons carrying odd blades. Their bones sound like grinding stones and they move with speed. 
Bronnen fires his bow, but it does little. He drops his bow and pulls his sword. I pray to Turn Undead and the two skeletons closest to us start to turn away and run. Their armor is very odd. While the first 2 skeletons turn away and run, two more advance. I pull my sword and summon Lygoth. One of the skeletons closest to me roars something at me in some language I do not understand and the fight between us commences.
Between swords strikes, I pray and Call Lighting. The skeletons are over 6-feet tall and move so quickly. I kill one of the skeletons and Bronnen kills the other. I start hunting one of the skeletons that ran away trusting Bronnen to go after the other. Lygoth comes with me, and we find the skeleton in one of the rooms of Bodin’s home. Lygoth hits and explodes around the creature, lightning sizzling and crackling until nothing remains of the skeleton. Bronnen attacks the remaining skeleton and the figure hits him with a green beam of energy. Bronnen flies back into the stone wall but not before killing the skeleton. 
We both take potions and heal. We turn our attention to the figure. It points a wand at us. I pray for Shatter once, then twice before Bronnen hits him with a sword strike and kills him. Bronnen and I have to heal each other again. Bronnen destroys the Necrotic Wand and we remove the heads of the skeletons and this undead creature. We leave the skeletons outside and I bring the one inside out, then we bring the robed figure inside, placing its head in a bag and keeping it far from the body. The Necrotic Wand was a branch of wood oozing with pus and corruption – it’s Her, the Corrupted Mother. 
We do a quick check of the ground floor and find the back door open. The ground near the door is blackened and there are bits of charred bones scattered nearby. Perhaps the remains of another skeleton. We secure this door and the front door and then continue searching the house room by room. The table in the dining hall is set for 10 people. A nearby small room has a spindle for weaving and trophies hang on the wall.
A second small room looks like a sitting room. There are paintings all over the walls. We pass a closed door that has a glyph on it, and I leave it alone. We find Father Bodin’s study and on the floor is a Porthion symbol surrounded by glyphs. Something blue glows on a reading stand in the corner of the study. I point it out to Bronnen, but he doesn’t see the glow of the papers or even the papers themselves. He only sees a scroll. The papers have writing on them, but I cannot read them. I remove my gauntlets and pick up the papers. I feel tingling, like the papers know me, and I can see what is on them. There are 3 sketches of men. I sketch copies of the 3 men so Bronnen can see them himself. One of the men looks Hularen because of the markings on his face.
I walk over to the closed door and put my hand on the glyph. Again, I can see it but Bronnen cannot. The door tingles and I open it revealing Father Bodin’s secret study. I look around but take nothing. When I shut the door behind me, the glyph reactivates.
We walk upstairs and find a large bedroom. There’s a 2nd different glyph on the floor up here and it looks like a teleportation circle. We also find a small barracks room with 4 beds, a bathing room, a second bedroom, and a music room. The music room is filled with all manner of instruments, and I wonder if Father Bodin taught himself to play every instrument here. I think of the paintings downstairs and wonder aloud if Father Bodin also taught himself to paint and those paintings on the wall are his works. 
We check the second half of the building. We find a larger barracks with 10 beds, armor stands, and weapon racks. We also find a livery with 3 live horses. 
“Someone has been taking care of them,” Bronnen observes. “The are Sumarac Plainsrunners; White Horse Clan. They are fast, distance runners and smart.”
A small room nearby holds hay and feed for horses and another room functions as a bedroom. A table holds fresh fruit and there are two small beds in here.
Back inside the house, we find the pantry which is stocked with food and drink, the kitchen, a washroom, and a second set of stairs leading up to the servant’s quarters with 6 beds. We go back downstairs and wait in the main room for Father Ardin Gayluss to arrive. When another hour passes, we decide to use Father Gayluss’s map to find him. 
He is in Low Town and the snow is falling harder. In the distance I hear crashing and banging. We head that direction and discover Father Gayluss fighting 3 strange creatures. He screams to Porthios, thunder shakes the area and lighting blasts down at the creatures he fights. We run up and join the fight. One of the creatures blinds me but when Bronnen attacks him, the spell is interrupted, and I can see again. Bronnen kills one of the creatures and it turns to ice. When the second creature is killed, it too, turns to ice and again with the 3rd. 
“This was a trap,” Father Gayluss says. “They followed me and I was trying not to lead them back to you.”
We walk back to Father Bodin’s home together. 
“I killed two before you arrived,” Father Gayluss tells us. 
We pull the iron gates closed behind us and once inside, we close the door. I tell Father Gayluss what we encountered when we arrived at Father Bodin’s home. We also tell him we searched the house and found it empty. I show Father Gayluss the glyph on the floor in the downstairs room and the small hidden office warded by a powerful glyph that is attuned to me.
Father Gaylus points to the glyph on the floor.
“Two below the dark East and 3 West the light South,” Father Gaylus recites.
I touch the coordinating spots on the glyph on the floor. The statue of the Warrior in the corner of the study moves and his sword raises, revealing hidden steps in the floor. I look around the room and the two statues in here, the door, and the stairs all glow with magic. I recognize the 4th step has a glyph to banish evil. The three of us walk down the steps to find a small entrance hall outside a large, round room with a 15-foot-tall ceiling. The walls are lined with honeycomb shelves filled with scrolls. There are 2 chairs and 2 desks in this room and 2 floating magical orb lights. The floor is stone, but lighter, not black mountain stone. The chairs and desks sit in the center of a stone garden – a Mor’Fang.
“Father Bodin is not Hularen, how could he be in here,” I ask, knowing that neither Bronnen nor Father Gayluss would have an answer for me.
Mother’s magic is active, pulsing, and strong here. I turn back and look at both Bronnen and Father Gayluss and I know this room is meant for me, not them.
“Stay back,” I say, “this room is meant for me. I don’t know if you will be safe, either of you.”
They both nod though neither of them look happy about it. I walk into the room and into the stone garden over to what must be Father Bodin’s desk. I find a stack of letters, one of them is addressed to me. The other letters are addressed to: Meroth, Esthera, Vordoon, Ohja, and Ardin. I open the letter written in Father Bodin’s hand and read:
If you are reading this, you have come, and I am not here. All is as it is willed. Find me; I will need your aid and you, mine. Be prepared for conflict. There are others you may encounter. Their names and letters are here as well. Do not read them and do not allow them to be read to you. If you are here and I am missing, then time is short. The holy strategy is in motion. Make haste but follow His will. Bodin.
A large book lays open on his desk. He was writing “the Anthology of Hule.” The last entry was the battle of the North-east Citadel. There is also a scrying bowl on his desk along with an ink bottle and quill. Inside the Mor’Fang is an armor and weapon stand but the armor and the weapons are gone. There is also a hand-written bible – he wrote it. I gather up the letters. There are 9 stones in this stone garden with 9 symbols on each stone and the tops curve in. They protect this place.
“There are 37 stone gardens in Woodhome and none of them are like this,” Bronnen tells me in Hularen. “The stones all have one or two glyphs, not 9.”
We walk back upstairs and I seal the room back up. I hand Father Ardin Gayluss his letter and repeat Bodin’s instructions – that I should not read their letters or allow the recipient to tell me what it says. Father Gayluss nods, reads his letter, then burns it. He looks over at me with a raised eyebrow. He must not like what he read. I watch as he then walks over to a lagger, climbs it, finds a hidden switch and reveals a hidden alcove behind a bookshelf. Father Gayluss reaches in and pulls out something long and slender, wrapped in leather. He does not explain what the item is, and we do not ask.
“I will be staying with you, at least for a time,” Father Gayluss says without any explanation.
I nod and show Father Gayluss the rest of Father Bodin’s house including the teleportation circle on the upstairs balcony. When we get to Bodin’s room, Father Gayluss touches the fur on the floor.
“It’s from a great big cat in the far North,” Father Gayluss says. “They can be 800 pounds.”
Father Gayluss says a Prayer of Guardianship in Celestial instead of in common. He glances over at me and I say it with him. A new glyph appears on the floor, and I feel a wave of magic pass over us. The corpses inside and outside are obliterated where they lay. We eat dinner together that night and find rooms to bed down in. I bathe and write an update to Father Sandlin which I send in the scroll case, feeling it vibrate as it sends. 
I fall asleep almost immediately.

### Summary of the Journal Entry:
Cara, Bronnen, and Father Gayluss navigate escalating tensions in Stonehill as they search for Father Bodin, investigate the framing of the Keln family, and fend off increasingly dangerous threats. Cara discovers Father Bodin’s secret study, a sacred stone garden infused with divine magic, and letters addressed to key allies. The group battles undead and necrotic forces, uncover conspiracies, and prepare for what lies ahead, their purpose intertwined with divine guidance and growing danger.

---

### Important Items:
1. **Mama’s Holy Symbol:** A keepsake tied to Cara’s connection to the divine and her family.
2. **Disguised Armor:** Bronnen dyes Cara’s Porthios armor for anonymity.
3. **Strange Ring with Tiger’s Eye:** Found on the leader of the attackers; likely magical or significant.
4. **Necrotic Wand:** Corrupted item linked to the enemy, destroyed by Bronnen.
5. **Key Items in Father Bodin’s Study:**
   - Letters addressed to key figures, including Cara.
   - "The Anthology of Hule" manuscript.
   - A handwritten bible by Father Bodin.
   - Scrying bowl.
6. **Hidden Item from the Bookshelf:** Retrieved by Father Gayluss, wrapped in leather, nature unknown.
7. **Mor’Fang Stone Garden:** Unique protective stones with nine glyphs each, unparalleled in design and power.
8. **Teleportation Circle:** Located in Father Bodin’s home, likely used for escape or travel.

---

### Important Locations:
1. **Broken Fence Tavern & Inn:** Owned by Lanerass Keln, a central hub of activity and tension.
2. **Stonehill:** The town where most events take place, under significant strain from political and supernatural forces.
3. **Father Bodin’s Home:** A fortified house hiding numerous secrets, including a sacred Mor’Fang.
4. **Barlin Indale’s House:** Temporarily shelters Lanerass and Kieli Keln, targeted by attackers.
5. **Porthion Church:** Where Cara meets Father Gayluss.
6. **Stone Garden in Father Bodin’s Study:** A divinely protected space infused with Mother’s magic.
7. **Low Town:** Where Father Gayluss was ambushed.

---

### Important Names:
1. **Cara Yornlin:** Protagonist and Priestess of Porthios.
2. **Bronnen:** Cara’s protector, scout, and trusted companion.
3. **Father Ardin Gayluss:** Renowned Porthion priest and ally in the search for Father Bodin.
4. **Father Aladin Bodin:** Groundskeeper and key figure in Cara’s mission, currently missing.
5. **Laneras Keln:** Owner of the Broken Fence, targeted for assassination due to his wife’s false accusations.
6. **Esthera Keln:** Accused of murder; a transmutation mage and descendant of Lord Kelgin Windamere.
7. **Lady Arana Keln:** Matriarch of the Keln family, protective and sharp-witted.
8. **Captain Greeland:** Acting Marshall of Stonehill, managing escalating crises.
9. **Barlin Indale:** A friend of the Keln family and temporary host to Lanerass and Kieli.

### Objectives:
1. **Find Father Bodin:** Cara’s divine mission, with clues leading East.
2. **Protect the Keln Family:** Unravel the conspiracy framing Esthera Keln and targeting her family.
3. **Investigate the Letters:** Deliver Father Bodin’s letters to their recipients without reading them.
4. **Uncover the Enemy’s Plans:** The involvement of necrotic magic, corruption, and conspiracies demands action.
5. **Prepare for Future Conflicts:** Strengthen the group’s resources and alliances.

### Important Events:
1. **Cara’s Vigilance:** She remains alert while Bronnen retrieves materials to disguise her armor.
2. **Attack on Barlin’s House:** Cara and Bronnen fend off assassins targeting Lanerass and Kieli.
3. **Confrontation with Skeletons:** Cara and Bronnen battle undead creatures at Father Bodin’s home, encountering necrotic forces.
4. **Discovery of the Mor’Fang:** Cara finds Father Bodin’s hidden stone garden, steeped in divine protection.
5. **Encounter with Father Gayluss:** The group reunites with Father Gayluss after he survives an ambush.
6. **Securing Father Bodin’s Home:** Cara and her companions explore and safeguard the property, discovering significant clues.

8. **Final Preparations:** The group regroups and prepares for the challenges ahead, securing Father Bodin’s house and laying plans. 

This journal entry showcases a pivotal day in Cara’s journey, filled with divine revelations, critical discoveries, and escalating threats. The stakes grow higher as she gathers her allies and prepares to face the challenges ahead.
